while we are living and if you are ashamed of the non-fulfilment of our father's words, adandon all doubt, return and rule the earth."

 54. Bharata also addressed Râma in just words, "How shall I, a youngster, be able to bear the yoke of the kingdom of which an elderly heir exists? do not set me to work at the destruction of our family glory."

 55. "Powerful is this army consisting of elephants and horses, these jewels are worthy of royal enjoyment, here is this company of warrior princes; God forbid (शान्तं) that I should rule when you are alive."

 56. To him who was thus speaking Rãma said, “O Bharata ! go back, taking my sandals with you;

**च्युतनिखिलविशङ्कः पूज्यमानो जनीघैः  
सकलभुवनराज्यं कारयास्मन्मतेन॥५६॥**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

and abondoning all doubt and respected by the people, rule the kingdom (for me) according to my counsel.”

**इति भट्टिकाव्ये प्रकीर्णकाण्डे रामप्रवासो नाम**

**तृतीयः सर्गः॥३॥**

**<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-17496259651.jpg"/>**

**चतुर्थः सर्गः **

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-174962620415-removebg-preview.png"/>

**निवृत्ते भरते धीमानत्ररोमस्तपोवनम्।  
प्रपेदे पूजितस्तस्मिन् दण्डकारण्यमीयिवान्॥१॥**

**अटाठ्यमानोऽरण्यानीं ससीतः सहलक्ष्मणः।  
बलाद्बुभुक्षुणोत्क्षिप्य जड्रे भीमेन रक्षसा॥२॥**

**अवाक्शिरसमुत्पादं कृतान्तेनापि दुर्दमम्।  
भक्त्वा भुजौ विराधाख्यं तं तौ भुवि निचख्नतुः॥३॥**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

 1. After Bharata's return the prudent Râma went to the hermitage of Atri; being honoured there he proceeded to the Dandaka forest.

 2. Râma, roaming in that great forest in company of Sîtá and Lakshmaṇa, was forcibly uplifted and seized by a terrifie demon.

 3. They dashed him, named Virãdha, on the ground after breaking his arms, whose head was

**आंहिषातां रघुव्याघ्रौ शरभङ्गाश्रमं ततः।  
अध्यासितं श्रिया ब्राह्म्या शरण्यं शरणैषिणाम्॥४॥**

**पुरो रामस्य जुहवाञ्चकार ज्वलने वपुः।  
शरभङ्गः प्रदिश्यारात् सुतीक्ष्णमुनिकेतनम्॥५॥**

**यूयं समैष्यथेत्यस्मिन्नासिष्महि वयं वने।  
दृष्टाःस्थ स्वस्ति वो यामः स्वपुण्यविजितां गतिम्॥६॥**

**तस्मिन् कृशानुसाद्भूते सुतीक्ष्णमुनिसन्निधौ।  
उवास पर्णशालायां भ्रमन्ननिशमाश्रमान्॥७॥**

**वनेषु वासतेयेषु निवसन् पर्णसंस्तरः।  
शय्योत्थायं मृगान् विध्यन्नातिथेयो विचक्रमे॥८॥**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

below and feet above and who was difficult to be chastised even by the god of death.

 4. They, brave descendants of Raghu, repaired thence to the hermitage of Śarabhanga which was inhabited by the Bráhmanical lustre and which was the place of refuge to those who sought it.

 5. S'arabhanga, having informed (Râma) of the abode of Sutikshṇa near by, threw his body into the fire in the presence of Râma.

 6. "We have dwelt in this forest," (said the sage. before burning himself) "with the hope that you would come here. You have been seen Hail to you. We go to the state we have earned with our merit."

 7. After he (शरभङ्ग) was reduced to ashes Râma resided in a hut of leaves in the vicinity of the sage Sutîkshṇa, walking always to the hermitages (of distant Ṛishis).

 8. Residing in habitable forests and sleeping on the bed of leaves, and hunting beasts just after

**ऋग्यजुषमधीयानान् सामन्यांश्च समर्चयन्।  
बुभुजे देवसात्कृत्वा शूल्यमुख्यं च होमवान्॥९॥**

**वसानस्तन्त्रकनिभे सर्वाङ्गीने तरुत्वचौ।  
काण्डीरः खाङ्गिकः शार्ङ्गी रक्षन् विप्रांस्तनुत्रवान्॥१०॥**

**हित्वाशितङ्गवीनानि फलैर्येष्वाशितम्भवम्।  
तेष्वसौ दन्दशूकारिर्वनेष्वानभ्र निर्भयः॥११॥**

**व्रातीनव्यादीप्रास्त्रः सुत्वनः परिपूजयन्।  
पर्षद्वलान्महाब्रह्मैराट नैकटिकाश्रमान्॥१२॥**

**परेद्यव्यद्य पूर्वेद्युरन्येद्युश्चापि चिन्तयन्।**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

his rising from his bed, he passed his days in hospitality.

 9. Worshipping the Bráhmins well-versed in the Ṛigveda and Yajusha and well-studied in the Sămaveda and performing a sacrifice, (he) ate best roasted meat after offering some to the gods.

 10–11. Putting on bark-garments fresh like garments on the loom, and covering his whole body, Râma, the archer, sword-bearer and bowman, and armour-bearer, the protector of the Vipras, and the enemy of the demons, leaving the forests already grazed by the cattle, roamed in those forests in which sustenance upon fruits was possible without any fear.

 12. He, whose missile was resplendent against beasts of prey and men who live by violence, visited the hermitages of ascetice who lived therein in company of the great Bráhmanas by forming small as sociations.

 13. At all times thinking of the prosperity and

**वृद्धिक्षयौ मुनीन्द्राणां प्रियम्भावुकतामगात्॥१३॥**

**आतिष्ठद्रु जपन् सन्ध्यां प्रक्रान्तामायतीगवम्।  
प्रातस्तरां पतत्रिभ्यः प्रबुद्धः प्रणमन् रविम्॥१४॥**

**ददृशे पर्णशालायां राक्षस्याभीकयाथ सः।  
भार्योढं तमवज्ञाय तस्थे सौमित्रयेऽसकौ॥१५॥**

**दधाना बलिभं मध्यं कर्णजाहविलोचना।  
वाक्त्वचेनातिसर्वेण चन्द्रलेखेव पक्षतौ॥१६॥**

**सुपाद् द्विरदनासोरूर्मृदुपाणितलाङ्गुलिः।  
प्रथिमानं दधानेन जघनेन घनेन सा॥१७॥**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

destruction of the sages, he earned the favour of them.

 14. Performing his evening twilight adoration from the time of the arrival of the cows to the time of their standing for milking and saluting the sun on rising up earlier than birds, (he earned their favour).

 15. In the hermitage he was seen by the libidinous female demon; leaving him aside who had a wife she stood before the son of Sumitrá.

 16. Having the middle part (between the breasts and hips) contracted into wrinkles, with eyes reaching the root of the ears, resembling the digit of the moon. on the first lunar day, on account of her speech and skin excelling all.

 17. Possessing beautiful legs, having thighs like the trunk of an elephant, having tender fingers and cavity of the hands, and appearing plumpy owing to, her bulky hips.  


**उन्नमं दधती वक्रं शुद्धदल्लोलकुण्डलम्।  
कुर्वाणा पश्यतः शंयून् स्रग्विणी सुहसानना॥१८॥**

**प्राप्य चञ्चूर्य्यमाणासौ पतीयन्ती रघूत्तमम्।  
अनुका प्रार्थयाञ्चक्रे प्रियाकर्तुं प्रियंवदा॥१९॥**

**सौमित्रे मामुपायंस्थाः कम्रामिच्छुर्वशंवदाम्।  
त्वद्भोगीनां सहचरीमशङ्कः पुरुषायुषम्॥२०॥**

**तामुवाच स गौष्ठीने वने स्त्रीपुंसभीषणे।  
असूर्यम्पश्यरूपा त्वं किमभीरुररार्यसे॥२१॥**

**मानुषानभिलष्यन्ती रोचिष्णुर्दिव्यधर्मिणी।  
त्वमप्सरायमाणेह स्वतन्त्रा कथमञ्चसि॥२२॥**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

** **18. Endowed with a face, the nose being erect, the teeth in which were white, with ear-rings pendant; making the observers happy, wearing a garland and with a smiling face.

 19. Having approached (Lakshmaṇa) she, gesticulating indecently, wishing the best of the Raghus for her husband, being libidinous and speaking sweetly, requested (him) to accept her (as his wife).

 20. "O Soumitra ! being desirous and free from apprehension marry me who am beautiful, who have offered myself (to you) who am of advantage to your body and who am (to be) your companion for the life of man."

 21. He replied to her, "Why do you, whose form is not to be observed by the sun, wander being fear less, in this forest where not a cow-pen is to be seen and which produces dread in man and woman."

 22. "Why do you, desirous of the company of a man, elegantly dressed, possessing a supernatural na-

**उग्रम्पश्याकुलेऽरण्ये शालीनत्वविवर्जिता।  
कामुकप्रार्थनापट्टी पतिवत्नी कथन्न वा॥२३॥**

**राघवं पर्णशालायामिच्छानुरहसं पतिम्।  
यः स्वामी मम कान्तावानौपकर्णिकलोचनः॥२४॥**

**वपुश्चान्दनिकं यस्य कार्णवेष्टकिकं मुखम्।  
सङ्ग्रामे सर्वकर्मीणी पाणी यस्यौपजानुकौ॥२५॥**

**बद्धो दुर्बलरक्षार्थमसिर्येनोपनीविकः।  
यश्चापमाश्प्रनप्रख्यं सेषुं धत्तेऽन्यदुर्वहम्॥२६॥**

**जेता यज्ञद्रुहां सङ्ख्ये धर्मसन्तानसूर्वने**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

ture and acting like a nymph, wander here at your entire liberty ?"

 23. "How is it that in this forest inhabited by ferocious beings you have no husband when you have given up all modesty and are very clever in entreating an amorous man?"

 24. "Do you secretly desire Râma dwelling in the hut for your husband——Rãma who is my lord, who is married and who has ear-reaching eyes."

25\. "Whose body is besmeared with sandal, whose face shines with pendant ear-rings, whose hands are dexterous in the use of weapons in battle and reach the knees."

 26. "By whom is tied to the knot of his garment a sword for the protection of the weak; who holds a bow hard like a stony thing; fitted with an arrow and impossible to be borne by others."

 27. "The conqueror of the haters of sacrifices in a battle, the source of righteous conduct, approaching

**प्राप्य दारगवानां यं मुनीनामभयं सदा॥२७॥**

**ततोवावृत्यमानासौ रामशालां न्यविक्षत।  
मामुपायंस्त रामेति वदन्ती सादरं वचः॥२८॥**

**अस्त्रीकोऽसावहं स्त्रीमान् स पुष्यतितरां तव।  
पतिरित्यब्रवीद्रामस्तमेव व्रज मा मुचः॥२९॥**

**लक्ष्मणं सा वृषस्यन्ती महोक्षं गौरिवागमत्।  
मन्मथायुधसम्पातव्यथ्यमानपतिः पुनः॥३०॥**

**तस्याः सासद्यमानाया लोलूयावान् रघुत्तमः।  
असिं कौक्षेयमुद्यम्य चकारापनसं मुखम्॥३१॥**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

him (i. e. at his approach) there is absence of fear to the wives and cattle of the sage."

 28. Afterwards she, desirous to marry Râma, repaired to the hut of Rãma and said respectfully, "O Ráma marry me."

 29. "He is without a wife, I have a wife, he will best maintain you, (becoming) your husband, go to him only, leave me aside," thus said Râma to her.

 30. She, being desirous of enjoyment, repaired again to Lakshmaṇa as a cow in heat approaches a great bull; —she whose mind was troubled with the fall of the cupid's weapon.

 31. Lakshmaṇa who intended to cut off, lifting up his sword which was (before) in the sheath, rendered noseless the face of her who was jesticulating indecently.

**अहं शूर्पणखा नाम्ना नूनं नाज्ञायिषि त्वया।  
दण्डोऽयं क्षेत्रियो येन मय्यपातीति साब्रवीत्॥३२॥**

**पर्यशाप्सीद्दिविष्ठासौ सन्दर्श्य भयदं वपुः।  
अपिस्फवच्च बन्धूनां निनङ्क्षुर्विक्रमं मृहुः॥३३॥**

**खरदूषणयोर्भ्रात्रोः पर्यदेविष्ट सा पुरः।  
विजिग्राहयिषु रामं दण्डकारण्यवासिनोः॥३४॥**

**कृते सौभागिनेयस्य भरतस्य विवासितौ।  
पित्रा दौर्भागिनेयो यौ पश्यतं चेष्टितं तयोः॥३५॥**

**मम रावणनाथाया भगिन्या युवयोः पुनः।**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

 32. "Verily I am Surpanakhá by name, by you have I not been known; since by you this irremdiable stroke of the sword was directed against me,” thus she said.

 33. She, standing in the sky, reviled (her enemies) after displaying her terrific body; wishing to disappear she trumpeted over and again the prowess of her brothers.

 34. Wishing to incite Râma to fight (with her brothers) she wept in the presence of her brothers, Khara and Dúshana, dwelling in the Dandaka forest.

 35. "Look at this deed of them, the sons of the unfortunate (Kous'alyã and Sumitrá), who have been sent into exile for the sake of Bharata, the son of the fortunate (Kekayî)."

 36 "Moreover this destruction (of the nose) of me whose lord is Râvana and who am your sister

**अयं तापसकाद्ध्वंसः क्षमध्वं यदि वः क्षमम्॥३६॥**

**असंस्कृत्रिमसंव्यानावनुप्त्रिमफलाशिनौ।  
अभृत्रिमपरीवारौ पर्यभूतां तथापि माम्॥ ३७॥**

**श्वःश्रेयसमवाप्तासि भ्रातृभ्यां प्रत्यभाणि सा।  
प्राणिवस्तव मानार्थं व्रजाश्वसिहि मा रुदः॥३८॥**

**जक्षिमोऽनपराधेऽपि नरान्नक्तन्दिवं वयम्।  
कुतस्त्यं भीरु यत्तेभ्यो द्रुह्यद्भ्योऽपि क्षमामहे॥ ३९॥**

**तौ चतुर्दशसाहस्रबलौ निर्ययतुस्ततः।  
पारश्वधिकधानुष्कशाक्तिकप्रासिकान्वितौ॥४०॥**

**अथ सम्पततो भीमान् विशिखैरामलक्ष्मणौ।**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

comes from an insignificant ascetic; take no heed of this if you think it (the deed) excusable."

 37. "Though humbly clad (in bark garments), though living upon the fruit of forest trees, though not served by any attendants, they have vanquished me."

 38. "You will (soon) have full happiness,” thus was she addressed by her brothers, "we live for your honour, go (to your place) rest secure, do not weep.

 39. "Even in the absence of any offence we eat human beings day and night; how is it possible then that we shall forgive those who hate us, O fearful one?"

 40. Thence they set out with an army of fourtythousand consisting of halbert men, archers, spearmen and swordsmen.

 41. Then in this battle Râma and Lakshmaṇa,

**बहुमूर्द्ध्नी द्विमूर्द्धांश्च त्रिमूर्द्धंश्चाहतां मृधे॥४१॥**

**तैर्वृक्णरुग्णमम्भुग्नक्षुण्णभिन्नविपन्नकैः।  
निमग्नोद्विग्नसंह्रीणैः पप्रे दीनैश्च मेदिनी॥४२॥**

**केचिद्वेपथुमासेदुरन्ये दवथुमुत्तमम्।  
सरक्तं वमथुं केचिद्भ्राजथुं न च केचन॥४३॥**

**मृगयुमिव मृगोऽथ दक्षिणेर्मा  
 दिशमिव दाहवतीं मरावुदन्यन्।  
रघुतनयमुपाययौ त्रिमूर्धो  
 विषभृदिवोग्रमुखं पतत्रिराजम्॥४४॥**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

with their arrows, killed the terrible demons who had faced them and some of whom were many-mouthed, two-mouthed and three-mouthed.

 42. The battle-ground was swarmed with the demons who were cut down, who were broken (in limbs), who were mutilated, who were powdered, shattered to pieces, were killed, who were overpowered with fear, who were terrified, who were ashamed and who were miserable.

 43. Some (of them) evere overtaken by fear, some with distress, others vomitted blood, there were none who showed any spirit.

 44. A demon by name Trimurdha approached the son of Raghu as a deer wounded in the right side should go to a hunter, or as a deer, being thirsty repairs to the burning quarter of the Maru, or as a serpent approaches the terrible king of the birds (Garuda).

**शितविशिखनिकृत्तकृत्स्नवक्रः  
 क्षितिभृदिव क्षितिकम्पकीर्णशृङ्गः।  
भयमुपनिदधे स राक्षसाना-  
 मखिलकुलक्षयपूर्वलिङ्गतुल्यः॥४५॥**

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

 45. He, whose all the mouths were cut off by sharp arrows, and who (therefore) looked like a mountain with its summits shattered by earth-quake, engendered fear foreboding the destruction of the whole race, in the (hearts of) demons.

**इति भट्टिकाव्ये प्रकीर्णकाण्डे रामप्रवासो नाम**

**चतुर्थः सर्गः॥४॥**

**<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-17497149359.jpg"/>**



**NOTES.**

**CANTO I.**

**<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-175567448665.png"/>**

** भट्टिकाव्यम्** 'A poem of Bhatti;' this name denotes that the book is a poetic composition of a poet by name भट्टिः. This name gives no more clue to the subject of the poem than the Poems of Milon' give to the subjects of Milton's poetry This name can with equal propriety be applied to any other poem of the same poet. This is therefore possible that the poet might have given another name to his poem expressive of the subject. We find in some old books that this poem is styled as the 'रावणवधमहाकाव्यम्'. Whether this name is given by the poet himself or by others it is not easy to determine.

 **काव्यम्——कवेः इदं काव्यम्** 'a poem'. काव्य is variously defined by writers on Poetics. The student can do well to understand some of the definitions; a तददोषौ शब्दार्थौ सगुणावनलङ्कृती पुनः क्वापि—Kâvya Prakásha I; वाक्यं रसात्मकं काव्यम् S. D. I; रमणीयार्थ-प्रतिपादकः शब्दः काव्यम्—R. G; शरीरं तावदिष्टार्थव्यवच्छिना पदावली—Kāv. I. 10; निर्दोषा लक्षणवती सरीतिर्गुणभूषिता। सालङ्काररसाऽनेकवृत्तिर्वाक् काव्यनामभाक्॥ Chandr. 1. 7. Kãvya, then, is a metrical composition depicting human sentiments in a more or less figurative style. The defiinition given by the author (मम्मठभट्ट) of the Kâvya Prakás'a is comprehensive and can therefore be taken as the model.

 **भट्टिकाव्य** is reckoned as a महाकाव्य 'a great classical poem.' The characteristics of a *Mahákávya* will be enumerated in the Introduction in which the claims of this poem to this high honour will be examined. The number of *Mahákávyas* is usually said to be five:

—रघुवंश, कुमारसम्भव, किरातार्जुनीय, शिशुपालवध and नैषधचरित, or six, if मेघदूत—a very small poem or खण्डकाव्य—be added to the list. This enumeration is evidently only traditional, as there are several other poems, such as भट्टिकाव्य, विक्रमाङ्कदेवचरित, हरविजय, हम्मीरकाव्य, &c. which have an equal claim to be considered as महाकाव्याऽ.

 The purposes of a Kâvya, as mentioned by Mamraṭa are:—काव्यं यशसेऽर्थकृते व्यवहारविदे शिवेतरक्षतये। सद्यःपरनिर्वृतये कान्तासम्मिततयोपदेशयुजे॥

 Our poem is divided into twenty-two chapters (सर्गा). Again these twenty-two chapters or cantos are arranged into four sections (काण्डाः). The division into chapters is based upon the subject—matter of the poem which is, in the main, the destruction of the demon king Rãvana. The story begins with the king Das'aratha, Ráma's father, and ends with the coronation of Rãma on his return to his capital Ayodhya' after the destruction of Rãvana. The four cautos with which we have to do at present are named रामोत्पत्तिः 'the birth of Ráma;' सीतापरिणय' the marriage of Sitá;' 'the journey of Ráma'; Canto IV continues the same subject (रामप्रवासः). All these four, together with the fifth, make up the first काण्डः. The divisions into sections (काण्डः) has a different purpose. One of the objects of the author is to aid the study of the Sanskrit tongue, (see Can. XXII stanzas 32-34). That object is fulfilled by the second plan. The first काण्डः is प्रकीर्ण, i. e. a mixed section dealing with various grammatical peculiarities. The second is अधिकारकाण्डः based upon the Ashtâdhyáyi of Pãnini; (3) प्रसन्नकाण्डः illustrating Poetics, word-figures (शब्दालङ्कार) such as प्रास. & c.; sensefigures (अर्थालङ्कार) such as उपमा, रूपक &c., and गुणाः (quality of a sentiment अर्थालङ्कार) such as माधुर्य, ओजः; (4) तिङन्तकाण्डः illustrating the ten tenses and moods.

 The student will remember the definition of काव्य

given above. As observed above, in a काव्य sentiments are delineated. Cp. नवरसरुचिरां निर्मितिमादधती भारती कवेर्जयति K. P. I. The *Rasas* are usually eight:—शृङ्गारहास्यकरुणरौद्रवीरभयानकाः। बीभत्साद्भुतसञ्ज्ञौ चेत्यष्टौ नाट्ये रसाः स्मृताः॥ The ninth रस sometimes added to this list is शान्तरस. Though all these sentiments find their delineation in a poetic composition, only one of these is the ruling sentiment of it which runs through the entire body of the poem. Accordingly in our poem the रस, that is most predominent, is वीर 'the heroic.' राम is the hero of our poem. There are four main kinds of नायकः — धीरोदात्त, धीरोद्धत, धीरललित and धीरप्रशान्त. राम falls in the first category. रावण is the उपनायक (नायकस्य गुणोत्कर्षकथका उपनायकाः). सीता is the heroine of the poem (नायिका). She is स्त्रीया ' the married wife' of Râma.

 As a rule every undertaking should begin with an invocation to some deity and mention of the subjectmatter, आशीर्नमक्रिया वस्तुनिर्देशो वापि तन्मुखम्. Our poer addresses no separate lines to his deity but he thinks that the name of his इष्टदेवता, which he manages to bring in the first verse, serves the purpose of an invocation. Or as this poem sings the deeds of राम, an incarnation of विष्णु, there remains no need of a separate invocation. Cp उत्तरत्रापि द्रष्टव्यमिति प्रदर्शनार्थे अत्र यद्यप्यादौ कविना देवतानमस्कारो न कृतस्तथापीष्ठदेवतासङ्कीर्तनमपि विघ्नोपशमनहेतुर्भवतीति मन्यमान आह। अभूदित्यादि तस्य हीष्टदेवता सनातनो विष्णुः स चादौ कीर्तितः। तत्प्रतिबन्धना चेयं कथेति प्रबन्धेनैवात्र सङ्कीर्तनं रामायणवन्त्तत्रविष्णोर्यस्मिन्काले जगत्कार्यवशादवतारः कृतस्तदेव प्रथमं दर्शयति। J. M. महाकाव्यस्यादावाशीर्नमस्क्रिया वस्तुनिर्देशो वा कर्त्तव्य इति सम्प्रदायानुरोधाद्वस्तुनिर्देशं कुर्वन्नेवेष्टदेवतास्मरणात्मकं मङ्गलमप्यादौ प्रकाशयति। Bharata.

 1 **अभूत्** ‘there was,' 'there flourished.' Here the aorist is used merely as a past tense to denote a past action. Strictly speaking there should be used the Perfect tense (लिट्) as the event is past and beyond the poet's personal observation. अन्यथा राज्ञश्चिरातीतत्वा-

त्कवेः परोक्षत्वाच्च लिट् स्यात्। J. M. The form is 3rd pers. sing, I Variety.

 नृपः 'a king,' नॄन् पातीति 'one who protects men.'

 **विबुधसखः** 'the friend of gods.' Many of the ancient kings had the honour of being personal friends of Indra. They assisted him in his wars against demons. पुरुरवस्, दुष्यन्तः and दशरथ are among them. As the friend of Indra Daśaratha may be said to be a friend of gods, or विबुध, though in its general significance means 'a god,' might be restricted to Indra. विबुध 'a god' विशेषेण बुध्यत इति. The epithet विबुधसखः suggests the धर्मविजयित्व of the king. धर्माविस्मरणसुरलोकविजयिनश्चये राजानस्तेषां धर्मविजयी प्रधानम्। J. M. The student should observe that राजन्, अहन् and सखि become राज, अह and सख at the end of a determinative compound. For exceptional cases vide Kielhorn's, from. art. 561.

 **परन्तपः** 'a tormentor of enemies' परान् शत्रून् तापयतीति परन्तपः. Enemies are of three sorts, उच्छेदनीयाः उपपीडनीयाः and कर्षणीयाः A परन्तप is one who torments the two last sorts. परन्तपः from qr 'an enemy' and तपः, the latter is derived from तप् by the addition of the krit affix अ before which the nasal is inserted. Similarly द्विषन्तपः, द्विषत्परयोस्तापेरितिखच् (अ). The epithets नृपः and परतपः speak of Das'aratha's work among his people and among his enemies respectively.

 **श्रुतान्वितः**—श्रूयन्त इति श्रुतानि वेदादीनि तै रन्वितः ' wellversed in the Vedas.' He knew the Vedas by heart and understood their meaning. अन्वितः p. p. from अनु + इ, 'possessed of' (the knowledge of the Vedas). **श्रुतः** = श्रुतिः 'a Veda;' (lit) 'what is heard.' The Vedas, which are four in number, ऋग्वेद, यजुर्वेद and सामवेद forming the त्रयी 'the sacred triad,' and अथर्ववेद, are so called because they are *apaurusheya*, 'not human compositions,' being supposed to have been directly revealed by the Supreme Spirit, Bráhman, and are

called श्रुति 'what is heard' or revealed, as distinguished from 'Smṛiti, i e. 'what is remembered or is, the work of human origin. The several sages to whom the hymns of the Vedas are ascribed are there-fore called द्रष्टारः 'seers' and not कर्तारः or स्रष्टारः 'composers.' The commentator भरत proposes a different meaning. श्रुत he takes to mean all learning other than the Vedas, अधीतशास्त्रः to avoid the fault of repetition, as again in the second stanza the king is described as सोऽध्यैष्ट वेदान्; श्रुतमत्र वेदादन्यच्छास्त्रं; श्रुत meaning what is heard from the teachers. This sense proposed, bу भरत is not bad in general, though the repetition that he is afraid of can be explained away; vide note st. 2.

 **दशरथः** 'the name of the Monarch.' He was the son of Aja and the father of Râma and his three brothers. He is described as a **महारथः** i. e. one who can fight singlehanded with ten thousand warriors; "एको दश सहस्त्राणि योधयेद्यस्तुधन्विनाम्। शस्त्रशास्त्रप्रवीणश्च स महारथ उच्यते॥" cp. दशरथः प्रशशास महारथो यमवतामवतां च धुरि स्थितः R. 9. 1. But his name with his appellation महारथः makes him an अतिरथः "धनुर्वेदस्य तत्वज्ञः सर्वशास्त्रविशारदः सहस्त्रं योधयत्येकः स महारथ उच्यते। महारथाद्दशगुणोविज्ञेयोऽतिरथो बुधैः॥" More of this monarch the student will learn in the course of his reading also Cp. R VIII. 29.

 **उदाहृतः** ‘named' p. p. from उदा+हृ. Bharata mentions an interpretation of इत्युदाहृतः as attempted by some. As it is far-fetched we give helow his own words इत्युदाहृत इत्यत्र केचिद्व्याचक्षते। इतं ज्ञानं विद्यतेऽस्येति इती ज्ञानी उदाहृतः ख्यातएव। यद्वा इतिषुज्ञानिषु उदाहृतः इतीति इतगतावित्यरमाद्भावेक्तः सर्वे गत्यर्था ज्ञानार्था इति इतं ज्ञानं ततोऽत्यर्थेनैकाज्ञादितिद्वन्।

 **गुणैर्वरंः** 'eminent or superior by his virtues गुण्यन्त अभ्यस्यन्त इति गुणाः. The virtues are धैर्य, गाम्भीर्य & c. वर comes from वृ 'to choose' therefore 'foremost'. The root meaning is appropriate since he was to be chosen for the father on account of his virtues.

 **भुवनहितच्छलेन** 'under the pretext of the good of the worlds. The भुवनाः are three in number, भूर्भुवः स्वरितित्रयो लोकाः, स्वर्ग, पृथ्वी and पाताल but according to fuller classification the Bhuvanas are fourteen, seven higher regions, rising from the earth one above the other, i. e. भूः, भुवः, स्वः, महाः, जनः, तपः, and सत्य or ब्रह्म; and seven lower regions, descending from the earth, one below the other, i. e. अतल, वितल, सुतल, रसातल, तलातल, महातल and पाताल (भवन्ति उत्पद्यन्त इति भुवनानि). The student will bear in mind that the ten incarnations of Vishṇu were intended for our good. The following verse from the Bhagavatgîtá gives reasons for an incarnation of God: परित्राणाय साधूनां विनाशाय च दुष्कृताम्। धर्मसंस्थापनार्थाय सम्भवामि युगे युगे॥ Ch. IV. 8; aiso Cp. IV. 7. यदा यदा हि धर्मस्य ग्लानिर्भवति भारत। अभ्युत्थानमधर्मस्य तदात्मानं सृजाम्यहम्॥ The ten incarnations of Vishṇu are enumerated in the following verse: मत्स्यः कूर्मोवराहश्च नरसिंहोऽथ वामनः। रामोरामश्च कृष्णश्च बुद्धः कल्कीच ते दश॥ The Avatár meant in this connection is Râma. हित is translated by J. M. 'as an incarnation of Vishnu' तेभ्यो हिता भुवनहिता विष्णोर्देशावताराः। इहतुरामो द्रष्टव्यः। perhaps from the literal sense of the p. p. हित of धा 'what is placed.' But the first sense is decidedly better as it gives the reason for such an Avatára. The good in this connection will be accomplished by killing Râvaṇa.

 **सनातनः** 'the Primeval Being,' i. e. Vishnu. The prefix ? सना=सदा 'always' सदा तनोतीति 'one who pervades the existence for all times.'

 **उपागमत्** ‘approached' i. e. become his (Das'aratha's) son; 3rd pers. Sing. II Variety (of उप + गम् ). Vishnu fixed his choice upon Das'aratha because the latter was the most distinguished monarch of his time on account of his superior virtues, गुणैर्वरं. This therefore serves as a reason, it is हेतुगर्भविशेषण. सत्खन्येषु राजसु गुणैर्वरत्वाद्यं पितरं जनकमङ्गीकृतवान्।

 **स्वयम्** ' voluntarily. The force of this word is that

Vishṇu assumed the incarnation of Râma, not as a result of his actions (कर्म), nor instigated by others but out of his grace or love for his creation. In this connection it may be remarked that the Supreme. Being has a three-fold function to perform which he does by means of his Trinity, ब्रह्म, विष्णु, महेश; the function of creation is assigned to ब्रह्मा, that of protection to विष्णु and that of destruction to महेश. Cp the Christian Trinity of the Father, the Son and the Holy Ghost.

 The student will remember that we have said above that the poet manages to bring in the name of his इष्टदेवता in the first verse which serves as an invocation. The poet therefore purposely puts अभूत् in the very beginning, thus managing to bring in अ as the first letter. It is well known that अ is said to be the first syllable of the word ओम्. अ means Vishṇu. Cp. अकारो विष्णु रुदिष्ट उकारस्तु महेश्वरः। मकारस्तुस्मृतो ब्रह्मा प्रणवस्तु त्रयात्मकः॥ The figures of speech in the first verse are काव्यलिङ्ग (काव्यलिङ्गं हेतोर्वाक्यपदार्थता K. P. X) and अपहुतिः (प्रकृतं यन्निषिध्यान्यत्साध्यते सात्वपह्नुति K. P X ). गुणैर्वरं points to the first Alankára and भुवनहितच्छलेन to the second. There is सङ्कर T of these two figures.

 2 **अध्यैष्ठ**—3rd per. sing. IV variety of अधि + इ 'to study'—'studied' or repeated as a part of his daily religious duty. A *kshatriya* has a five-fold duty to discharge, अध्ययनं, यजनं, दानं, शस्त्राजीवः, and भूतरक्षणं. He must study the Vedas; sacrifice to the gods, to his manes &c.; must be charitable; live by his weapon and must protect all the creatures. Another form of इ with अधि is अध्यगीष्ट.

 **वेदान्** ‘the Vedas,’वेदयति आज्ञापयति धर्माधर्मौइति, lit. which acquaints us with our duty and non-duty. This is अध्ययन.

 **त्रिदशान्** 'the gods.' They are called thirty-three

(त्रिदश) because originally the number of gods was only thirty-three which in course of time approache the high number 33 crores. Here the word appears to be used without any reference to the number. It is however good to remember the names of the thirty gods: eight वसु, twelve आदित्याः, eleven रुद्राः, इन्द्र and प्रजापति.

 अयष्ट — 4th form of यज् 'to sacrifice'— 'sacrificed.' This is यजनं to the gods. Under यजन five such यजनाः are included: अध्यापनं ब्रह्मयज्ञः पितृयज्ञस्तु तर्पणम्। होमो दवो (or देवयज्ञः) बलिर्भौतः (or भूतयज्ञः) नृयज्ञोऽतिथिपूजनम्॥ अग्निष्टोमादिभि; पूजितवान्इत्यर्थः J. M. B. says some are of opinion that त्रिदशान् is superfluous since यज् necessarily involves that idea but in fact the verb is not thus restricted in its sense.

 पितॄन् 'forefathers,' 'manes.' अपारीत् — 5th form of पॄ to feed'—'fed by oblations.' Another reading mentioned by the Com. is पितॄनताप्सीत्. अतार्प्सीत्—4th form of a 'to gratify', other forins are अतृपत् 2nd form and a 5th F. The 4th Form is optionally अत्राप्सीत्. Other roots which are conjugated like तृप are स्पृश्, मृश्. कृष् and दृष्. This is also due to the forefathers (पितृयज्ञ). The reading stated above is equally good.

 सममंस्त — 4th Form of सम+मन् —'respected' his relations by liberal grants; दानमानादिभिः पूजितवान् This is. दानम्.

 व्यजेष्ट — 4th F. of वि + जि to conquer '—' conquered,' 'subjugated.'

 षड्वर्गम् 'the six enemies of mankind, i. e. काम, क्रोध, लोभ, मोह, मद and मात्सर्य. The Christian theology includes these among deadly sins which, according to it, are Idleness, Gluttony (लोभ), Lechery, Avarice (लोभ) Envy (मात्सर्य), Wrath (क्रोध) and the head of

these all Pride (मद). The poet Spenser gives a very vivid description of these enemies of mankind in the Can IV Bk I of his 'Faery Queene.' A true conqueror is he who puts down these internal enemies and not he who conquers external enemies. The king was a conqueror of his internal as well as external enemies. Mark that with is âtm. cp. Can II. 39.

 अरंस्त — 4th Form of रम् 'to take delight in'—'took delight in,'fondly practised.' When रम् is Paras. it takes the VIth Form.

 नीतौ 'in good conduct,' either in politics (राजनीतिः) or in daily observances (सन्ध्यादि). In the former are included his home politics and foreign politics. He was a just ruler and his relations with his brother—kings were also based upon right principles of government. J. M. says सामादिषु सन्ध्यादिषु च रतो नीतिमानित्यर्थः But this explanation restricts his dealings with his enemies because सामन् conciliation or negotiation; दानं bribery; भेदः sowing dissensions and दण्ड punishment (open attack) are means of success against an enemy. It is better to give a wider application to the word. The last two duties शस्त्राजीव and भूतरक्षण are indicated by the word नृपः which occurs in the first verse.

 समूलघातं न्यवधीत् 'completely exterpated or destroyed. This applies to those enemies who are to be exterpated (उच्छेदनीयाः); समूलघातं is an infinitive form (णमुल्) of हम्. (Vide Apte's Guide). न्यवधीत् — 5th Form of हन् = वध् 'killed.'

 The metre of the first verse is रुचिरा and that of the second is इन्द्रवज्रा (vide Appendix for definition &c). The author of the *Kávya Prakásha* says that there is a fault (दोषः) in this verse which he calls वाक्यश्रुतिकटुर्दोषः 'harshness of sounds' (vide Chapter VII). The Alankára is दीपक as there is one noun for many verbs,

अरीन् शत्रून् समूलघातं यथास्यात्तथा न्यवधीत् हतवान्। समूलानां शत्रूणां घातः प्राणवियोगफलकव्यापारो यत्र हिंसाक्रियायां (in which action predicated by the verb, there is destruction of all enemies)। अन्ये तु समूलशब्दात्परात् गतार्थाद्धन्ते श्चणं विभक्त्यन्त तदनुप्रयोगश्चेत्याहुः। Some think that here घात is used in the sense of 'going' as हन् when preceded by a few words means 'to go' cp पद्धति. "समूलान्निशेषा नरीन्प्राप्य हतवानित्यर्थः। ' चणम्वा अभीक्ष्णेपूर्वकाले' इत्यत्र वा शब्दस्य व्यवस्थावाचित्वाद्योगविभागाद्वा अन्यत्रापि चणम्वो स्यादिति देवीदासचक्रवर्तिना व्याख्यातम्। The infinitive in अम् gives the idea of frequency (अभीक्ष्ण) or a prior action (पूर्वकाल) but the वा in the sutra gives room for any other use of the infinitive as in समूलघातं. This is the explanation of देवीदासचक्रवर्ती अरीन् समूलान् हत्वा तत्प्राणत्यागानुकूलव्यापारं कृतवानित्यर्थस्तेनपूर्वकालत्वमपीति दुर्गसिंहप्रभृतयः। This explanation of दुर्गसिंह &c. is based upon the पूर्वकाल sense of the infinitive. एतेन पुनः सन्धानशङ्कया सदा सावधानत्वं सूचितम्। घात may be treated as an abstract noun, the whole term being adverbial to न्यवधीत्। व्यजेष्टषड्वर्गमित्यनेन मानसा रिपवः अरीभ्यवधी दित्येनेन च बाह्याश्च निर्जिता अतः परन्तप इतिप्रागुक्त मुपपादितम्। Bharata.

 3 वसूनि 'wealth.' तोयं 'water.' B. thus accounts for the sing. तोयशब्दोऽयं स्वप्राधान्यैकत्वादत्युक्तैकवचनः। अनेकेषामपिवसूना मेकतुल्यतेत्याशयः। घनवत् = घनः इव 'like a cloud.' The king is here compared to the cloud. The घन is उपमान and असौ दशरथः is the उपमेय. The particle वत् is used to form a comparison.

 व्यकारीत् ‘scattered,' 'distributed' घनपक्षे 'showered down.' The latter expression can be aptly used to apply it to both — 5th Form of वि + कॄ ‘to scatter’—- This distribution takes place among his subjects; बन्धुव्यतिरेकेण बालादिभ्यो व्यकारीद्दत्तवान्। J. M. The king had no desire to reap fruit by his charity, he did it disinterestedly as a cloud does. Cons. यथाघनस्तोयं विकरति तथासौ वसूनि व्यकारीत्। निरपेक्षतया। The idea is that the taxes the king gathers from his subjects are spent in their own interest. For a very similar idea Cp. ''प्रजा-

नामेव भूत्यर्थं स ताभ्यो बलिमग्रहीत्। सहस्र गुणमुत्स्रष्टु मादत्ते हि रसं रविः ॥ R. I. 18. The अलङ्कार is उपमा (शाब्दी वाक्यगा).

 आसनम् 'a seat,' the throne of Indra is meant here. आसन is a noun from आस् 2A by the addition of the termination अन, Cp वसन.

 गोत्रभिदा 'with Indra,' lit. 'a breaker of mountains;' गोत्र 'a mountain,' A mountain is so called because it gives shelter to the cattle (गो). The mythological Indra is said to have clipped off the wings of the mountains, which they once possessed, when they grew turbulent. मैनाक alone escaped this punishment on account of his being a friend of the ocean.

 अध्यवात्सीत् — 4th Form of अधि + वस् I P वसति— 'occupied,' 'sat. Remember that वस् with उप, अनु and अधि is transitive and takes an acc. of place. Cp यानि प्रियासहचरश्चिरमध्यवात्सं U. 5. 63, दण्डकामध्यवात्तां यौ वीर रक्षः प्रकाण्डकौ Can. V. 6, मा धिवात्सीर्भुवं &c. Can. VIII. 79 of this poem. आसनं is the object of this action. अनेनात्यन्तधर्मविजयित्वस्यफलं दर्शयति. This highest honour is due to the king's धर्मविजयित्व.

 The highest honour to which the ancient Aryan kings aspired was to occupy the seat with Indra.

 त्र्यम्बकादन्यम् 'other than Tryambaka i. e. Siva.' In this sense of other than' अन्य is used with the abl. or at the end of a compound. Cp. नास्ति जीवितादन्यदभिमततन्रमिह सर्वजतूनां K. 35. त्रम्बक the god Siva,' so called because he is supposed to have three eyes, two like ours and one in the middle of the forehead. त्रीणि अम्बकानि अक्षीणि यस्य. According to भारतं quoted by Bharata the sky, the earth and the water, द्यौर्भूमिरापस्तिस्त्रोऽऽम्बा, are the three eyes of the God, Bharata gives two more senses of त्र्यम्बक suggested by others. त्रयाणां ल्लोकानामम्बः पितेति अन्ये। 2 तिस्त्रोऽम्बाः शक्तयोऽस्येतिकेचित्। Kalidása speaks of शिव as the father of the world जगतः पितरौ व्वन्दे पार्वतीपरमेश्वरौ R. I. 1. But the शक्तिऽ are eight in

number. So the last two may be considered as possible interpretations.

 उपस्थित — 4th Form of उप + स्था to wait upon,' 'to worship'—'worshipped.' Mark that उप + स्था is Atm only in the following senses: 'to approach with prayers,' cp ये सूर्यमुपतिष्टते मन्त्रैः Can. 8. 13 of this poem; to treat one as a friend,' cp सख्येन मामुपतिष्टते; 'to approach for intercourse,' कं रहसि उपतिष्टते Can. 5. 68; 'to meet or join (as a river)' गङ्गायमुनामुपतिष्टते; sk; 'to form friendship with,´ उपास्थितैवमुक्ते तंसखायं राघवः पितुः Can. 6. 42; ‘to lead to,' पन्थाः स्त्रुघ्नमुपतिष्टते sk. देवपूजासङ्गतिकरणपथिष्वितिदेवपूजायां तङ् (Atm ) J. M; मैत्राध्वसङ्गाराधइति आराधनार्थे मम्। (Atm) Bh. Why the poet restricts Dasaratha's. adoration to one deity it is not easy to say. We cannot believe that Dasaratha was a bigoted Saiva and therefore like a modern शैव who considers himself an inveterate foe of a वैष्णव (a follower of Vishṇu) or of a follower of any other god hated the worship of every other god. It is, no doubt, true that every Hindu shows his predilection for one particular god (उपास्यदेवता) but he is never known to set aside other gods. He pays his homage equally to all.

 सर्वेषुभृतां 'of all archers,' इषुः 'an arrow,' (इषून् बिभ्रतीति).

 निरास्थत् — 2nd Form of अस्, 4P. 'to throw'— 'eclipsed,' 'obscured.' यशांसि being the obj. एतेनास्य असाधारणीकृतास्रत्वं दर्शितं J. M. The metre of this verse is उपेन्द्रवज्रा (vide Appendix ).

 4 (पुण्यः) (अग्निपक्षे) 'one who purifies.' Agni, by receiving oblations of man is said to purify; अग्निरपि पुण्यः पावनात्पुण्यः यागादिः पुण्यः तेन पुरुषः पूज्यते J. M. (राजपक्षे) 'meritorious.' 'righteous,' अत्यन्तपुण्यकरणद्राजापि पुण्यइत्युच्यते J. M; पुण्यं धर्मे मनोज्ञेचपावने च प्रयुज्यते, Bh.

 महाब्रह्मसमूहजुष्टः 'worshipped by many learned Brahmanas,' महतां ब्रह्मणां ब्राह्मणानां वेदविदो समूहेन जुष्टः सेवितः;

the king is served by them by acting as priests on sacrificial occasions; the fire, as he is the medium of offering oblations to gods. It is a belief that Agni carries oblations to gods. ब्रह्म is a synonym of ब्राह्मण, 'ब्रह्मा विरिञ्चिद्विजयो' रितिविश्वः Bh. Bharata connects महा with to avoid contradiction with a rule which says: “शङ्खे तैले तथा मांसे वैद्ये ज्योतिषिके द्विजे। यात्रायां पथि निद्रायां महच्छब्दो न दीयते"॥ Mark also his other interpretations:। महांश्चासौ ब्रह्म समूहजुष्टश्चेति। 2 यद्वा महद्ब्रह्म तपो येषां तेषां समूहेन जुष्टः। वेदस्तत्वं तपो ब्रह्म ब्रह्मा विप्रः प्रजापतिरित्यमरः। 3 यद्वा अमहा अस्येवविष्णोरिव महस्तेजो येषाम्। अमहा इति पृथक् पदम्। 4 यद्वामद्यते पूज्यतेऽअसौ महा स्नासुसिति कर्मण्यस्। 5 यद्वा यमो रोगस्तंहन्तीति अमहा। तस्मिन् राजनि सति लोकानां व्याधिभयं नासीदित्यर्थः। आरोग्यमपि कविभि र्वर्ण्यते तथाच कालिदासः 'जनपदे नगदः पदमादधावविभवः कुतएव सपत्नज' इति अग्नेर्व्याधिहन्तृत्वमस्त्येव। These are all possible but unnecessary speculations.

 सन्तर्पणः 'one who pleases,' सन्तर्पयतिप्रीणयतीति; the king pleases the gods by his oblations and the fire by acting as a medium for the transmission of them to gods. This abstract noun is used to indicate an agent (कर्तरिल्युट्). नाकसदां ' of the gods,' goes with सन्तर्पणः. नाके सीदन्तीतिनाकंसदो देवाः (सद् = सीद् 1 P to dwell). नाक 'the paradise,' lit, a place where is no sorrow, कं सुखं तद्विपरीतमकं नास्यस्मिनितिनाकः Bh. The word नाकसदां is कर्मणिषष्ठी.

 वरेण्यः ‘most distinguished,' both the king and the fire ; वृ + एन्य, वृ ' to choose ' वरति. This word appears in our sacred Gayatri Mantra. जज्वाल (perfect of ज्वल् ) 'Shone.'

 लोकस्थितये ' for the sustenance or support of the world,' the king by the enforcement of his laws and by his good government supports his people; Agni by indirectly being the cause of rain which is useful for the livelihood of people. लोक is our earth भूः. Mark

the verse अग्नौ प्रास्ताहुतिः सम्यगादित्यमुपतिष्टते। आदित्याज्जायते वृष्टिर्वृष्टेरन्नं ततः प्रजाः॥

 **अभिप्रणीतः** 'propitiated' with the Mantras. This attribute is applicable only to the fire. The Metre is इन्द्रवज्रा, the अलङ्कारऽ are वाक्यगाश्रौतीउपमा as is shown by यथा and श्लेष in the first line as the adjectives bear double applications

 5 **पुण्यकीर्तिः** (Bah. Com. पुण्या कीर्तयोयस्य सः) 'of holy fame.'

 **शतमन्युकल्पः** 'almost like Indra' the termination कल्प is added to nouns and adjectives in the sense of 'a little less than,' 'almost like,' 'nearly equal to,' (denoting similarity with a degree of inferiority); cp कुमारकल्पं सुषुवे कुमारं R. 5. 36, उपपन्नमेतदस्मिन्नृषिकल्पे राजनि; कल्प is therefore a termination denoting comparison शतमन्युः 'Indra', lit, 'one who performed a hundred sacrifices,' (मन्युः 'a sacrifice'). The idea of Indra as having performed a hundred sacrifices is modern, of the Puranic times; the Vedic idea is different. मन्युः is in the Vedas used in the sense of 'courage'. 'power' as in its synonym शतक्रतुः, क्रतुः means 'power,' 'strength.', So Indra is one who has or possesses hundred powers i. e. who is omnipotent. But later on ऋतुः, मन्युः were somehow taken to mean 'a sacrifice' and the myth that Indra performed hundred sacrifices came to be invented.

 **महेन्द्रलोकप्रतिमां** 'like the world of the great Indra,' i. e. Amaravati, Indra's capital प्रतिमा 'equal to', a word showing comparison like कल्प and उपमा when the last member of a compound. Cp. अथैकधेनोस्पराधचण्डाद्गुरोः कृशानुमतिमाद्विभेषि R. 2. 49 and अपिलङ्घितमध्वानं बुबुधेन बुधोपमः R. 1. 47. Dasaratha's capital is here compared to that of Indra. It is adjectival to अयोध्याम्. J. M. begins his Com. स्वामिगुणपूर्वका हि निवासस्य गुणा भवन्तीति प्रदर्शनार्थे पश्चात्तभिधानं तथाचोक्तम्। स तु यच्छीलस्तच्छीला अस्यप्रकृतयः (subjects) भवन्तीति।

 **समृद्ध्या** 'by its great prosperity,' सम्यगतिशयेन ऋद्धिः समृद्धिः

 **अध्यास्त**—Imperfect of अधि + आम् — 'resided,' 'dwelt;' आस् with अधि governs the accusative of the place, ep. अधिशीङ्गस्थासां कर्म (vide Apte's Guide).

 **सर्वर्तृसुखां** 'pleasant in all the seasons,' सर्वेषु ऋतुषुमुखयतीति सुखा ताम्, Ayodhya is मुखा because it is the source of pleasure or सुखा is a feminine noun formed from the verb सुख् by adding the termination आ (अच्) before which no Guna or Vṛiddhi takes place; पचाद्यच् यद्वा सुखहेतुत्वात् मुखा J. M अध्यासितां p. p. of आम् with अधि — inhabited' by ब्रह्मभिः 'by the Brahmanas,' ब्रह्म is a synonym of ब्राह्मण ep ब्रह्मसमूहजुष्टः above.

 **इद्धवोधैः** 'of sharp intellect,' सर्वशास्त्र परिज्ञानात्पटुबुद्धिभिरित्यर्थः J. M; इद्ध p. p. of इन्ध् 'to kindle.' बोधः a mas. noun from बुध् by the krit termi. अ before 'which the penultimate short or the final vowel of a root commonly takes its Guna or Vriddhi substitute. Metre is उपेन्द्रवज्रा.

 Cons. पुण्यकीर्तिः शतमन्युकल्पः स समृद्ध्या महेन्द्रलोकप्रतिमां सर्वर्तुसुखाम् इद्धबोधैर्ब्रह्मभिः अध्यासिताम् अयोध्याम् अध्यास्त.

 6 **निर्माणदक्षस्य** 'clever in creation.' This genetive adjective appears naturally to qualify पद्मासन. But the latter is made subordinate to कौशल, the whole word पद्मासनकौशलस्य being a genetive compound and it eannot therefore as a subordinate word in a compound, be detached and be qualified by an independent attribute. It is therefore necessary to understand निर्माणदक्षस्य as qualifying पद्मासनकौशलस्य.

 **समीहितेषु** sc विषयेषु 'things undertaken or "desired' (to be created); p. p. of सम् + ईह् 1 A to desire. सीमेव “as if the boundary or limit. The idea is that Ayodhya forms, as it were, the limit of creation, there is nothing superior to it in point of beauty and magni,

ficence among all created objects. Ayodhya, as it were, marks a limit beyond which the creative genius of the Creator cannot go. इव shows that it is उत्प्रेक्षा (सभावन मथोत्प्रेक्षा प्रकृतस्यपरेण यत् K. PX) in which there is superimposition of one thing upon another.

 **पद्मासनकौशलस्य** ' of the skilfulness of the Creator.' पद्मासन—पद्मम् आसनं यस्य—the Creator whose seat is a lotus. Mythologically Brahman is represented as being born in a lotus which sprang from the navel of Vishṇu. This compound does not violate the rule which lays down that a numeral or a word denoting a quality is not compounded with a noun in the genetive case. Under गुणाः some particular qualities, i. e. रूपरसगन्धस्पर्शाः, their particular properties, i. e. शुक्लनीलादयः of रूप, कटुकाम्नादयः of रस, सौरभ्यादयः of गन्ध, शीतोष्णादयः of स्पर्श only are to be included. But even the primary qualities रूपरसगन्धस्पर्शाः enter into such compounds. Because there is a rule which allows a genetive compound of a primary quality with its substratum but not with sub-qualities. Com. तस्यपूरणगुणेत्यादिना न प्रतिषेधः तत्र विशिष्टा एव गुणा रूपरसगन्धस्पर्शाः तद्विशेषाश्च शुक्लनीलादयः कटुकाम्लदयः सौरभ्यादयः शीतोष्णादयश्च गृहीताः। तत्र रूपादिभिः समासोभवत्येव। तत्स्थैश्च गुणैः षष्ठी समस्यते नतु तद्विशेषगुणैरितिवचनात्॥ अन्यैस्तु समास प्रतिषेधः। J. M. In this way only can the views of the three Munis पाणिनी, कात्यायन and the भाष्यकारपतज्जलि be reconciled. Com. "अधिकरणैतावत्वे च" "तदशिष्यं सञ्ज्ञाप्रमाणत्वा" दितिपाणिनेः। “युगपद्देशपृथक्त्तवदर्शनादिति रूपसामान्याद्वा इति वचनप्रामाण्यादिति चेदलोपप्रतिषेध" इति कात्यायनस्य। नकारग्रहणसामर्थ्यात् लोपो न भविष्यतीतिकिं पुनरत्रार्थसत्तत्वमिति भाष्यकारस्येति। J. M. The Com. Bharata has exercised his scholastic ingenuity in interpreting the first line in various ways which do not commend to us. We are inclined to prefer the simple explanation above given, wherein we are supported by J. M., to his. For the student's information, however, we give them below: He takes निर्माणदक्षस्य to mean of विश्वकर्मणः' the architecture of Gods, connecting it with समीहितेषु and

सीमेव with पद्मासनकौशलस्य. निर्माणदक्षस्य विश्वकर्मणः समीहितेषु सम्यक् चेष्टितेषु (works) यास्थापिता तामयोध्या मध्यास्तेति पूर्वेणान्वयः समुपसर्गेण बहुत्वेन (plu. number) च चेष्टाया आधिक्यं सूचितम्। विश्वकर्मणा नेदृशी शोभना पुरी निर्मिता अत इमां विलोक्य ईदृक् पुरीनिर्माणे चेष्ट। जातेत्यभिप्रायः। पद्ममेवासनं यस्य सपद्मासनो ब्रह्मा तस्य कौशलस्य नैपुण्यस्यसीमेव उत्प्रेक्षायां ब्रह्मणा नेदृशी शोभनान्या पुरी निर्मितेतिभावः। अतः सुतरां विश्वकर्मण ईदृक निर्माण चेष्टावतम्। 2 connects सीमेव with समीहितेषु and interpretes पद्मासनकौशलस्य as adj. to निर्माणदक्षस्य यद्वा निर्माणदक्षस्य विश्वकर्मणः समीहितेषु निर्मितेषु सीमेवातः परं शोभनं न निर्मितमित्यभिप्रायः। किम्भूतस्य तद्मासनस्येव कौशलं यस्य। 3 agrees with our interpretation; 4 takes as a सप्तमी Aluk compound and connects निर्माणदक्षस्य with मघोनः। यद्वा कौ पृथिव्यां शलते चलतीति पचादित्वादन् सरसिजमित्युदाहरता वोपदेवेन क्वचित्समासे विभक्तेर्नलुक् इति सूचितं तेनात्र सप्तम्या अलुक् पद्मासनश्चासौ कौशलस्यश्चेति कर्मधारयस्तस्य समीहितेषु सीमेव क्वचिद्विशेष्यः प्राक् प्रयुज्यते प्राग्भावस्य विवक्षाधीनत्वादिति पद्मासनस्य प्राग्भाव कौशलम् इति विशेषणात् पृथिव्यां विहितसृष्टेर्नैतादृशी सृष्टिरिति सूचितम्। अतएव पृथिव्यां प्रतियोग्यभावात् (being unrivalled) स्वर्गमुपहस्य स्थिता मघोनः किम्मूनस्य निर्माणदक्षस्य स्वपुरनिर्माणं दक्षते हन्तीति पचारित्वादन् इमां पुरीं दृष्टवा स्वपुरी निर्माणनिन्दकस्येत्यर्थः। We have already remarked we do not like these scholastic hair splittings.

 **ऊर्ध्वस्फुरद्रत्नगभस्तिभिः** construe this with अवहस्येन 'with rays of jewels glittering upwards;' ऊर्ध्वं स्फुरन्तो ये रत्नानां गभस्तयो रश्मयः तैर्हासभूतैर्मघोन इन्द्रस्य पुरममरावतीमवहस्येव स्थिता। Whether the pavements of Ayodhya were of jewels or the walls or floors of the houses were set with diamonds is not clear. But it is necessary to understand some such idea to make this description real. **अवहस्येव** 'as if laughing at.' This is an instance of उत्प्रेक्षा, which is suggested by the rays issuing out of the jewels. The lustre of the rays is white and poets speak about कीर्ति and हास as being white. It is not the lustre of the rays but the laugh of Ayodhya. **पुरं** 'the town' (of Indra) i e. Amaravati,

object to अवहस्य. **मघोनः** (Gen. of मघवन्) 'of Indra.' Mark that श्वन्, युवन् and मघवन् undergo Samprasaraṇa, i. e. change their व् to उ before vowel terminations beginning with the acc-plu.

 Cons: या निर्माणदक्षस्यपद्मासनकौशलस्य समीहितेषु सीमेव स्थिता, याच ऊर्ध्वस्फुरद्रत्नगभिस्तिभिर्मघोनः पुर मवहस्येव स्थिता तामध्यास्त. It is necessary to supply तामध्यास्त from st. 5 in this verse and the two following verses.

 7 **सद्रत्नमुक्ताफलवज्रभाञ्जि** 'containing diamonds, pearls and beautiful jewels;' सद्रत्नानि मुक्ताफलानिव्रजाणिच (Dwa. Com.) तानि भजन्ते यानि गृहाणि तानि Tat. Com. This adjective and the following three adjectives are applicable both to the houses in Ayodhya and the summits of the mountain मेरु. Diamonds (वज्र) and pearls (मुक्ताफल) come under the category of jewels (रत्न) but they are mentioned separately as being the best of their kind, मुक्ताफलवज्रयो रत्नान्तर्भावेऽपि प्राधान्यख्यापनार्थे। J. M. मुक्ताफलवज्राणां रत्नत्वेऽपि प्राधान्यात् प्राचुर्याद्वा पृथगुपदानम्। जातौ जातौ यदुत्कृष्टं तद्धि रत्नं प्रचक्ष्यत इत्यनुशासनात्। The number of such precious jewels is given as five or nine; "नीलकं वज्रकं चेतिपद्मरागश्च मौक्तिकम्। प्रवालं चेति विज्ञेयं पञ्चरत्नं मनीषिभिः"॥ or ' सुवर्णं रजतं मुक्ता राजावर्तं प्रवालकम्। रत्नपञ्चकमाख्यातम्'॥ or 'कनकं हीरकं नीलं पद्मरागश्च मौक्तिकम्। पञ्चरत्नमिदं प्रोक्तमृषिभिः पूर्वदार्शिभिः'॥ and "मुक्तामाणिक्यवैढूर्यगोमेदा वज्रनिद्रुमौ। पद्मरागो मरकतं नीलश्चेतियथाक्रमम्"॥ The variant 'युञ्जि is not so good as the above.

 **विचित्रधातूनि** (Bah. Com, विचित्रा धातवो येषु) ' having various metals;' such as मनःशिल, सुवर्णं &c. **सकाननानि** 'with forests or gardens;' The mountain मेरु must have forests in it but it is possible to suppose that there were gardens in it prepared by the Apsaras who resided on it. कानन may therefore be translated as 'groves or gardens.' **युतानि** 'filled with.'

 **अप्सरसां** 'of the Apsaras.' They are a class of female divinities or celestial damsels who reside in the

sky and are regarded as the wives of Gandharvas. They are very fond of bathing, can change their shapes and are endowed with superhuman power (प्रभाव). They are called स्ववैश्या and are usually described as the servants of Indra, who alarmed by the rigorous austerities of some mighty sage, sends down one of them to disturb his penance and her mission is generally successful. They are so named because they are said to have come out from the ocean when it was churned ; अद्भ्यः सरन्ति उद्गच्छन्ति. Cp. अप्मु निर्मथनादेव रसात्तस्माद्वरस्त्रियः। उत्पेतुर्मनुजश्रेष्ठ तस्मादप्सरसोऽभवन्॥ cp. also या तपोविशेषपरिशङ्कितस्य सुकुमारं प्रहरणं महेन्द्रस्य। They are also said to covet heroes who die on the battle-field, cp. अमर्त्यभावेऽपि कयोश्चिदासीदेकाप्सरः पार्थितयोर्विवादः R. 7 53. Bana mentions fourteen families of these nymphs (see K. 136 B E). The word is usually said to be pl. (स्त्रियां बहुप्प्सरसः) "आपः सुमनसो वर्षाः अप्सरसिकताः समाः एते स्त्रिया बहुत्वे स्युः एकत्वेप्युत्तरत्रयं" इति। but the sing, as also the form अप्सरा, sometimes occur; नियमविघ्नकारिणी मेनका नाम अप्सराः प्रेषिता S. 1 and अनप्सरेव प्रतिभासि V. 1.

 **ओघैः** 'by the inultitudes' (of the Apsaras). The mountain Meru is described as being inhabited by them. In order to make the comparison complete. the women of Ayodhya are likened to them. इव shows comparison. Bharata says that the comparison of one woman in Ayodhya with a number of the Apsarasas shows the superior beauty of the former. ओघशब्दादे कैकशोऽपि स्त्रीणामप्सरःसमूह सादृश्येनातिसौन्दर्यं दर्शितम्।

 **मेरोः** 'of the mountain Meru.' As far as our knowledge goes we may consider this to be a fabulous mountain. Around this mountain all the planets are said to revolve and this forms the centre of several Dwipas. It is also said to consist of gold and gems. **शिरांसि** 'summits.' **गृहाणि** the peculiarity with this word is that it is generally masculine in the plural

number (गृहाः cp. इमे नो गृहाः Mu 1), though neuter forms are sometimes used. But in the singular it.is always neater. गृहइति गेहेकः तत्र गृहशब्दोपनि नपुंसकलिङ्गः तत्स्थायिषु पुंलिगो नित्यं बहुवचनाच्च J. M. In the pln. it denotes, then, the innates of the house. Metre is इन्द्रवज्रा, Alankara उपमा.

 8 अन्तर्निविष्टोज्ज्वलरत्नभामः (अन्तर्निविष्टानि उज्ज्वलानि रत्नानि Kar. Com. तेषाम्भामः Gen. Tat. Com.) the rays (भामः) of the brilliant jewels stored in the house; it is Subject to भान्ति.

 **गवाक्षजालैः** 'through the lattice-windows. The net-work of a window is called its जाल 'a lattice.' गवामक्षीव गवाक्षः (अक्षि being changed to अक्ष). जाल may mean a collection,' then the whole word 'through many windows,' गवाक्षजालैर्वातायनसमूहैर्जालाकृतिगवाक्षैर्वा Bh. Con. this with **अभिनिष्पतन्त्यः** (fem. plu of the pre. p. अभिनिष्पतत्) 'issuing out,' 'radiating'

  **हिमाद्रिटङ्कादिव** 'as if from the summit of the Himalayas;' हिमाद्रि (हिमस्य अद्रिः Gen. Tat. or हिमेनयुतोऽद्रिः Ins. Tat. Com.) 'the mountain of snow;' the slope or declivity of a mountain' 'उन्नतमदेशष्टङ्कइत्युच्यते J. M. टङ्कात् पाषाणदारणाद्विदीर्णप्रस्तरभागात् Bh. The rays issuing from the houses are said to issue from the summit of the Himalayas, इव therefore shows उत्प्रेक्षा . It has to be supposed that the houses in Ayodhya were very tall, many-storied. **भान्ति** 3rd pers. pl. of भा 2nd P. 'to appear.' **गङ्गाम्बुपातप्रतिमा** 'like the flow of the waters of the Ganges. For a note on प्रतिमा vide-st. 5 supra, The comparison is suggested by the pellucity of the Gangetic waters, (स्वच्छत्वात्). Bharata construcs इव wlth •प्रतिमा which necessitates another interpretation of प्रतिमा for प्रतिमा in the sense of इव will give rise to the fault of redundancy. Bh. gives therefore a different sense to प्रतिमा i. e. च्छटा 'splendour,' 'continuous line,' but we think that our explanation is more

natural and appropriate since it is necessary to take इव with ॰टङ्कात् to make the description more vivid.

 9 **धर्म्यासु**—धर्म्य may mean either 'legitimate,' i. e. they were Dasaratha's legitimate, legally married wives; or 'righteous' i. e. they never deviated from their duties and womanly virtue; धर्म्य=धर्मादनपेत 'not deviating from duty &c.,' other words which are thus dissolved are पथ्य, अर्ध्य and न्याय्य from पथिन्, अर्थ and न्याय respectively; अनपेत comes into the dissolution,न्यायदनपेतं न्याय्यम् &c. The locatives in the first line qualify पत्नीषु as well as विद्यासु. As explained above Dasaratha's wives were righteous or legally married. the Vedic lore is धर्म्य because it leads to धर्म one of the aims of human existence. **कामार्थयशष्करीषु** 'who were instrumental in acquiring fame, worldly prosperity, and worldly pleasures.' The four ends of human existence are धर्म, अर्थ, काम, and मोक्ष But the three first form the well known triad of the aims of human existence. The four or three aims are to be gained in company of a wife who contributes largely to their attainment. The wives of Dasaratha, as all good wives do, helped him in the attainment of the three aims of life and in acquiring fame. Knowledge also brings all these to him who possesses it.

 **लोके मतासु** 'respected among people.' The wives of king had earned the good-will and love of the people on account of their virtues and general goodness of nature. विद्या are always respected by people. **अधिगतासु काले** 'wedded,' 'married' at the proper time, i.e. (विवाहयोग्ये काले परिणीतासु); when they had reached marriageable age; विद्यापक्षे 'acquired in boy-hood,' (शैशवसमये गृहीतेषु) cp. शैशवेऽभ्यस्तविद्यानां &c. R.1.7; i.e during the stage of celibacy, second of the four stages into which the life-time of a twiceborn is divided. **विद्यासु** 'the three Vedas, Rigveda, Samaveda and Yajurveda. The Triad of the Vedas is often described

as the three wives of him who has mastered them thoroughly.

 **अभिरेमे** (per. 3rd per. siug of अभिरम्), पत्नीपक्षे 'sported or cohabited;' विद्यापक्षे 'took delight in,' used with instr. or loc. cp. verse 2 supra असंस्त नीतौ and लोलापाङ्गैर्यदि न रमसे लोचनैर्वेचितोऽसि Me. 27........, सीते मा संस्था जीवितेन नः Can. 6. 15. So construe विद्यासु and पत्नीषु with अभिरेमे. **तिसृषु** loc. plu. of fem. of त्रि , the three wives of the king, viz., कौशल्याकैकेयीसुमित्रा, or the three learnings, vide विद्यासु above. **उत्तमासु** 'the best' on account of good womanly virtues or the vedic knowledge being the highest kind of knowledge. Metre इन्द्रवज्रा, Figures श्लेष and उपमा. Cons. यथा धर्म्यासु........विद्यासु विद्वान् रमते तथा धर्म्यासु........पत्नीषु सराजाऽभिरेमे.

 10 **पुत्रीयता** 'by him desirous of a child,' pres. par. of the denomi. base of पुत्र. There are various ways of forming verbs from nominal bases, one of which is by means of the suffix य and conj. in Paras; (vide Kielhorn for further information p. 207). Though the king had three wives he was without any issue down to his old age. He was advised by his family priest Vasistha to invite the sage Ṛishyasringa who knew of a child-bearing sacrifice. The king had great difficulty in bringing him to his capital. He bad to employ some damsels for this purpose, who, by their machinations, at last succeeded in bringing him down to the king's palace. The Com. J. M. gives this version of the story, which differs from another which says that the use of damsels was not made at this time. vide note on ऋष्यशृङ्ग infra. **वराङ्गनाभिः** 'with the help of beautiful women,' 'courtesans.' **अनायि**, pas, aorist of नी, 'was brought.' Remember that the roots नी, वह् and some others (vide Apte's Guide) take two accusatives, one of person and the other of place; in this case the two accusatives are पुरं and मुनिं,

the latter being made the subject of the passive voice. **क्रियावान्** 'versed in the practice of ' sacrifices (क्रतुषु). This shows that his knowledge was not only theoretical (विद्वान् means that) but he was able to use it for practical purposes. The adjectives are हेतुगर्भ i.e. serve the purpose of the sage being brought. वत् is a possessive termination; This मतुप् has the sense of प्रशस्तं (प्रशंसाया मतुप्): मतुप् (the possessive term.) is used in the following senses यदुक्तं भूमनिन्दाप्रशंसासु नित्ययोगेऽतिशायने। सम्मगस्तिविवक्षायां भवन्ति मतुबादय इति॥ Bh.

 **विपक्त्रिमज्ञानगतिः** 'having access to fully developed knowledge.' When the intellect is so developed through successive previous births that a man gains knowledge without the aid of ordinary means, such as austerities or education, his knowledge is said to be विपक्त्रिम 'fully developed.' Knowledge by intuition is meant here, all intuitional knowledge being according to this idea, but the accumulation of the knowledges of previous births. Plato held a similar view. विपाकेन जाता ज्ञानस्यगतिर्मागोयस्य स तथा विनोपदेशाज्ज्ञानं जामित्यर्थः। अतिपरिणतज्ञानमार्ग इत्यर्थोवा। Bh. विपाकेन निर्वृत्तंयत्पूर्वजन्मकृतमनिवर्तनीयं कर्म तस्योग्रतपः प्रत्ययाद्विनोपदेशात् ज्ञानात्प्रवृत्तिर्बुद्धावस्य जातेत्यर्थः। J. M. विपक्त्रिम adj. from विपच् ' to mature or develop' with the suffix त्रिम. The suffix is used in the following senses 'ड्वितस्तज्जइति त्रिमक् गतिर्मार्गे दशायाञ्च ज्ञाने यात्राद्युपायने' इति विश्वः । Bh. निर्वृत्त or जात comes into the dessolution.

 **मनस्वी** (प्रशस्तं मनोयस्यास्तीति) high-souled,' ‘high-minded.' See note on क्रियावान् above. विन् is the possessive termination applied to some words such as स्रक्, मेधा, माया and यशः &c., instead of वत् or मत्.

 **मुनिः** 'a sage,' धर्मादिमननान्मुनिः Bh. J. M. He is thus defined by the divine author of the Bhagavatgita: दुःखेष्वनुद्विग्नमनाः सुखेषु विगतस्पृहः। वीतरागभयक्रोधः स्थिरधीर्मुनिरुच्यते॥ Bg. 2. 56.

 **ऋष्यशृङ्गः** (ऋष्यस्यशृङ्गमिवशृङ्गं यस्य Bah. Com.) 'the name of a sage.' He was the son of Vibhandaka. According to mythical account he was born of a female deer, and had a small horn (शृङ्ग) on his forehead, and hence called 'Ṛishyasṛinga,' or 'deer-horned.' He was brought up in the forest by his father, and he saw no other human being till he nearly reached his manhood. When a great drought well nigh devastated the country of Anga, its king Lomapada, at the advice of Brahmanas, caused Ṛishyasṛinga to be brought to him by means of a number of damsels, and gave his daughter Santa (adopted by him, her real father being Dasaratha) in marriage to him, who being greatly pleased, caused copious showers of rain to fall in his kingdom. We know also that he performed for king Dasaratha the sacrifice which brought about the birth of Rama and his three brothers.

 11 **ऐहिष्ट**—5th Form of ईह् 'desired.' This verb is used with acc. or inf. Here it is used with both. Cp. ईहन्ते कामभोगार्थमन्यायेनार्थसञ्चयान् Bg. 16. 12. **कारयितुं** the causal form is used to show that the sacrifice was to be performed by him for the king, the fruit of it was to accrue to the king. तं मुनीद्रं and क्रतुं are the objects of this inf. The causal of takes either the acc. or instr. of the original agent. Cp. भृत्यं भृत्येनवा कटं कारयतिऽk. (vide Apte's Guide on this point).

 **कृतात्मा** 'self-subdued,' वशीकृतात्मा. This sense is better than Bh. which is कृत आत्मायत्नो येन, though आत्मा means यत्नः, आत्मायत्नो धृतिरित्यमरः **पुत्रफलं**—पुत्रः फलं यस्य child.' Bah. Com.— 'the fruit of which was to be a **मुनीन्द्रम्** the best of sages,' इन्द्र is used to show superiority. नरेन्द्र or नृपेन्द्र &c. **व्यतानीत्** — 5th Form of वितन्—performed.' **कर्मठः** 'clever in the performance 'of sacrifices,' यागक्रियानिष्पादकः **कर्म** ' a sacrifice. सुतानुव-

न्धम् 'of which a child is the result.' 'सुतमनुबध्नातीति. The sacrifice which was to be performed is called पुत्रेष्टि 'sacrifice. सुतानुबन्धि Ha is a variant having the same meaning, सुतावनुबन्धुंशलिमस्येति.

 12 **वेदीं** 'the alter' upon which the sacrificial fire was lighted. **परितः** 'round about,' encircling.' Mark that the prepositions अभितः, परितः, समया &c. govern a noun in the acc. **निरास्थत्** — 2nd Form of निर् + अस्) 'warded off."

 **अङ्गानि** 'the limbs of a sacrifice,' i e. the deities subordinate to the one who is the principal deity of sacrifice The principal deity in this sacrifice is Vishṇu. Other gods may, therefore, be considered as, subordinate to him, यद्देवतामयोयागः सा देवता तत्र प्रधानं पुत्रफलत्वाद्विष्णुः प्रधानम्। तमिष्टवा तस्योभयतः पार्श्वयोर्यान्यङ्गानिचक्षुरादीनिदेवतान्तराणि तान्ययाक्षीत्। J. M. The अङ्गानि, according to J. M are चक्षुरादीनि Bh gives the same meaning but suggests also that the limbs may be लोकपालनवग्रहादीन्. Bh gives to अङ्ग a different meaning altogether. By अङ्ग he says, may be meant अङ्गयाग 'subordinate sacrifices'. **अयाक्षीत्**—4th Form of यज्—worshipped,' अग्नावाहुत्यापूजितवान् by offering oblations in the fire.

 **प्रधानं** 'the chief deity' of the sacrifice, i. e Vishṇu; the acc. is governed by अभितः **शेषाणि** 'the rest.' It appears that the images of the gods were made of the rice-flour at this sacrifice. The image of the principal deity was preserved and all the rest, after they had been duly worshipped, were thrown into the fire. अहौषीत्—4th Form of हु—'offered as an oblation' अग्नौ हुतवान् **सुतसम्पदे** 'for tho acquisition of sons,' or 'for wealth in the form of sons' सुता एव सम्पद् तस्यै पदे. **अमार्गीत्**—5th Form of मृग 'to beg'—'asked for.' All the verbs are used in the Parasmaipada to show

that the fruit was to accrue not to the sage but to the king.

 13 **निष्ठाङ्गते** 'when it was fnished.' कर्मणि निष्ठाङ्गते is an instance of the loc, absolute. Mark the idiomatic use of गम् in निष्ठाङ्गते.

 **दत्रिमसभ्यत्तोषे** adj. to कर्मणि, 'in which the satisfaction of the assemblage (of the Bramanas) was gained by gifts.' दत्रिम 'secured by gifts' (दानेननिर्वृत्त). The whole word is a Bah, Com. दत्रिमः सभ्यानां तोषो यस्मिन्कर्मणि. Vide note on विपक्त्रिम म st. 10 *supra*. **विहित्रिमे** — adj. to कर्मणि, ' which was performed with due rites,' निधानेननिर्वृत्ते कर्मणि. **सभ्य** 'a member of an assembly,' here a Brahmaṇa. The Tad. ter. य as applied to सभा (before which the final vowel is dropped) means 'worthy of, सभायांसाधवः सभ्याः, cp. शरण्यः **प्राशुः** 'ate,' perf. of प्र + अश् 5 P. A. अश्नोति, अश्रुते. **हुतोच्छिष्टं** obj to प्राशुः, 'the residue of the oblations,' हुतावशेषं शिष्टचरुं. **उदारवंश्याः** of noble birth,' of noble descent,' वंश्याः वंशे भवाः (शेषेयत् = य Tad. ter.). प्रसोतुं—int. of प्रसु 'to give birth to'— 'in order to give birth to.' चतुरः Mark the declension of त्रि and चतुर् in all the genders. The poet says that the three wives of Dasaratha ate the residual oblations to give birth to four sons. The wives should bear three sons but it appears that सुमित्रा to whom were born Lakshmaṇa and Satrughna, was not a क्षत्रियी woman. She came of a mixed extraction. She was therefore given some portion out of their shares by कैकेयी and कौशल्या who considered her their attendant. Sumitra therefore got two portions which gave her two sons. We have followed J. M. in giving the above account. In the Ramayaṇa there is nothing to show that Sumitra was of mixed extraction. Kalidasa too assigns another cause why Sumitra was given two portions; अर्चिता तस्य कौशल्या प्रिया केकयवंशजा। अतः सम्भावितां ताभ्यां सुमित्रामैच्छदीश्वरः R. X. 55. The king, according to the prince of Indian poets,

wished that Sumitra should be honoured by them both. Thus this becomes a question of precedence, love and honour. Sumitra was not offended at the partiality shown by the king to her co-wives because she was tenderly attached to them. सा हि प्रणयवत्यासीत्सपल्योरुभयोरपि। R. X. 57. This, therefore, with the question of distribution, presents a knotty point for solution. In our childhood we were told a different. account. The king distributed the चरु equally to all his wives but the portion of Sumitra, white it lay on the cavity of her hand, was suddenly snatched away by a kite. This left her no portion. Then it was that Kousalya and Kaikey gave a portion each from theirs. The student will find that Bhatti's account differs from that of Kalidasa. It is said that a being arose out of the sacrificial fire with some food in his hand, which he offered to the king &c. Cp. हेमपात्रगतं दोर्भ्यामादधानः पयश्चरुम्। अनुप्रवेशादाद्यम्य पुंसस्तेनापिदुर्वहम्॥ प्राजापत्योपनीतं तदन्नं प्रत्यग्रहीन्नृपः। &c. R. X. 51-52.

 14 **असावि**—pas. aor. 3rd pers sing of स—'was born,' 'was given birth to.' **कौशल्यया**, कौशल्या was the daughter of the king of Kosala, a country, situated according to Ram., along the banks of Sarayu and 'Dakshina-Kosala.' The former is also called 'Ganda,' and it must have therefore signified the country north of Ayodhya, comprising Ganda and Baraitch. Aja, Dasaratha &c. are said to have ruled over this province. At the time of Rama's death his two sons Kusa and Lava reigned respectively at Kusavati in the southern Kosala in the defiles of the Vindhyas, and at Sravesti in northern Kosala. केकयीतः 'to Kekayi,' तः is an ablative termination used sometimes instead of the ablative case-termination, प्रासोष्ट—4th Form of प्र + सू—'gave birth to.' केकयी—fem. of केकय—pl. N. of a country and its people;

nounced the world. **यमिन्**=यतिः 'an ascetic.' 'Cp. अहिंसा सत्यमस्तेयं ब्रह्मचर्यमकल्मषम्। इतिपञ्च यमा येषां सन्तीति यमिनः स्मृताः॥ J. M., also ब्रह्मचर्यं दयाशान्तिर्दानं सत्यमकल्पता। अंहिसास्तेयमाधुये दमश्चेतियमाः स्मृताः Yaj. **वरिष्ठः** (Super of उरू) 'the greatest or higest' of the ascetics (यमिनां).

 16 **अङ्गवान्** 'with all the limbs.' There are several vedic works which are considered as members of the Veda. These works are auxiliary to the Vedas and designed to aid in the correct pronunciation and interpretation of the text and the right employment of the Mantras in ceremonials. The Vedangas are six in number:—शिक्षाकल्पो व्याकरणं निरुक्तं छन्दसां चयः। ज्योतिषामयनं चैव वेदाङ्गानि षडेवतु॥. अध्यगायि—pas. aor. of इ with अधि 'to study’—'was studied.' Mark the conj. of this verb in the act. and pas.

 **उपायंसत**—pas. aor. of उप + यम् 'to receive'—'were received.' उपपूर्वो यमिः स्वीकरणे वर्तते। तस्मात्कर्मणि लुङ् (Aorist), **जित्वगणि** 'invincible,' 'conquering' वर is a krit ter, showing 'tendeney' or disposition. Cp. गत्वर, इन्वर, नश्वर &c; therefore जित्वराणि = जयशीलानि.

 **भिन्नवृत्तीनि**—भिन्ना वृत्तयोयेषां—'of different dispositions or natures' **समम्** adv. to अध्यवात्सुः **गुणिनः** १०. रामादयः मानसानि acc. to अध्यावात्सु 'उपानु' इत्यादिना अधिकरणस्य कर्मसञ्ज्ञा. see note on अध्यवात्सीत् st. 3 *supra*.

 17 **अध्यगात्**—1st Form of इ 'to go'—'came to' or 'approached.' **गाधिसुतः** 'the son of Gadhi, i. c विश्वामित्र. He plays an important part in the Puranas. He was a kshatriya king of Kanyakubja who subsequently became a Maharshi by his severe austerities to which he was led by a scuffle he had with Vasistha as regards the appropriation of the cow of plenty (सुरभिः) who rightfully belonged to the latter. Vasistha refused to part with the cow; Visvamitra tried to take her by force but he was signally defeated in

his attempt. He was then struck with the power inherent in Brahmanism and devoted himself to rigorous penances which ultimately made him a Brahmarshi. His power, even before he attained to that highest dignity was great. He is said to have transported Trisanku in body to the heaven. He emulated the Creater in the act of creation. He was the companion and councillor of young Rama to whom he gave several miraculous weapons. Some of the Vedic hymns are ascribed to this great sage.

 **अभ्याहतकर्मवृत्तिः** (अभ्याहताअभिभूतायागादेः कर्मणोवृत्तिः प्रवृत्तिर्यस्य) 'whose daily performances (sacrifice &c.) were disturbed or molested.'

   **वरीतुं** (inf of वॄ 'to ask for') 'to ask for.' **परिरक्षणार्थं** sc. विहन्यमानस्यकर्मणः आर्जिहत्—3rd Form अर्ह् पूजायां 'to worship'—' worshipped.' **मधुपर्कपाणिः** 'a mixture of butter, ghee and honey in his hand,' मधुपर्कः पाणौयस्य —Vya. Bah. Com. The usual ingredients are five:— दधि सर्पिर्जलं क्षौद्रं सिता चैतैश्च पञ्चभिः। प्रोच्यते मधुपर्कः। It was a custom with the ancients to offer मधुपर्क to any guest or a bridegroom on his arrival. J. M. renders, by लक्षणा perhaps, मधुपर्क by मधुपर्कपात्र and Com. तस्मिन्पात्रे स्थितःपाणिर्यस्येति विग्रहः। सप्तम्युपमाने' इत्यादिना उत्तरपदलोपीसमासः। पात्रादुद्धृत्य मधुपर्केण पूजितवानित्यर्थः। We do not see any reason to find fault with the usual sense given above. Bh. agrees with us. Cp. कौशिकेन स किल क्षितीश्वरो राम मध्वरविघातशान्तये। काकपक्षधरमेत्य याचित स्तेजसांहिनवयः समीक्ष्यते॥ R. XI. 1.

 18 **ऐषीः** (2nd pers. sing, 5th Form of इष्=इच्छ्) 'desired.' पुर्जन्मजयाय 'in order to conquer rebirth.' We, Hindus, believe in the doctrine of the transmigration of the soul or metempsychosis. The transmigration of the soul is due to its actions of which an earthly fruit is desired. It is as impossible to avoid the results of our actions as to avoid the law of universal gravitation. Both are natural and therefore

inexorable. But we can suspend, nay, destroy, the working of this law 'of as you sow, so shall you reap' by abandoning the fruits of our actions, i. e. making our actions our duties. Cp. विहाय कामान्यः सर्वान्पुमांश्चरति निस्पृहः। निर्ममो निरहङ्कारः स शान्तिमधिगच्छति॥ Bg, II. 71 and निस्मादसक्तः सततं कार्यं कर्म समाचर। असक्तो ह्याचरन्कर्म परमाप्नोतिपूरुषः Ch. III. 18. also Ch. II. 47. The Hindu student is strongly recommended to read the divine Bhagavatgita. **यत्** obj to ऐषीः, relating to ध्यानं.

 **रूपादिबोधात्** 'from the perception of Rupa and others. आदि includes the other twenty-three of the Vaiseshikas. गुणास्तु रूपरसगन्धस्पर्शसङ्ख्यापरिणामपृथक्त्वसंयोगविभागपरत्वापरत्वं बुद्धिसुखदुःखेच्छाद्वेषप्रयत्नगुरुत्वद्रवत्वस्नेहसंस्कारधर्माधर्मशब्दाश्चतुर्विंशतिगुणाः Tarkakoumudi. He that wishes for final emancipation should not attach himself to these but should turn his soul on the Universal Soul and meditate upon him. Cp. Benedictory stanza I in the मृच्छकटिक,..... आत्मन्यात्मानमेव व्यपगतकरणं पश्यतस्तत्वदृष्टया। शम्भोर्वः पातु शून्येक्षणघटितलयब्रह्मलग्नः समाधिः॥ न्यवृतत्— 2nd Form of वृत् with नि—'turned from.' यत्ते रूपादिषुळे शब्दस्पर्शरूपरसगन्धेषु चक्षुरादिद्वारेण यो बोधोऽध्यवसागलक्षणबुद्धिः ज्ञानं वा तस्माच्चयध्द्यानं न्यवृतत् निवृत्तम्। ज्ञानं न रूपरसगन्धादिविषयकं स्यात्। J. M., Bh.

 **तत्वानि** 'the twenty-five elements. They form the categories of the Sankhya Philosophy. These are enumerated in the following verse: "मूलप्रकृतिराविकृतिर्महदाद्याः प्रकृतिविकृतयः सप्त। षोडशकश्च विकारो न प्रकृतिर्न विकृतिः पुरुषः॥ मूलप्रकृतिः=प्रधानं; महदाद्याः = महत्, अहङ्कार and पञ्चतन्मात्राः (रूप, रस, गन्ध, स्पर्श and शब्द); विकारः=five ज्ञानेन्द्रियाणि (श्रोत्रं त्वक्चक्षुषी जिह्वा नासिका चैव पञ्चमी), five कर्मेद्रियाणि (पायुपस्थं हस्तपादं वाक् चैव दशमीस्मृता), मनः and पञ्चमहाभूत (पृथ्वी, अपः, वायुः, आकाश, and तेजः); and पुरुष 'the spirit or self.' **अबुद्धाः**—4th Form of बुध् st.—'understood' the real nature of **प्रतनूनि** 'very subtle'.

 **ध्यानं** 'meditation,' concentration of the mind upon one object, chiefly upon the Universal Being. Op. ध्यानस्तिमितलोचनः R, I. 73. शिवं 'well' i. e. without disturbance.

 19 **द्विषद्वीर्यनिराकरिष्णुः** 'able to nullify the prowess of his enemies.' इष्णु is kritter, showing 'tendency' or 'disposition'. Cp Can. III. and निराकरिष्णू वर्त्तिष्णू वर्द्धिष्णुपरितो रणम्। उत्पतिष्णू सहिष्णूच चेरतुः खरदूषणौ Can, V. 1.

 **तृणेढु** — 2nd per. imperative of तृह् 'to kill'—'let (him) kill. तानि obj.

 20 **शुश्रुवान्** (per. pre. parti.) hearing.' **मुमोह** (per. of मुह् 'to swoon') 'fainted'. The poet here follows explicitly the *Ramayana* which also speaks of the swoon of the king for some time. In the Ram. The king pleads the tender age of his sons as a reason for sparing them but the sage overcomes his scruples by acquainting him with the true greatness of his sons. Kalidasa speaks of the ready willingness and assigns the following cause "अप्यसुप्रणयिनां रघोः कुले न व्यहन्यत कदाचिदार्थिता. Kalidasa is here, in our humble opinion, more heroic than natural. The human mind is scarcily susceptible of heroism under such circumstances, however strong it may be. Nature proves too strong for it. **असहिष्णुः** 'unable to bear,' vide निराकरिष्णुः above.

 **अहंयुना** adj. to तापसकुञ्जरेण 'proud,' 'haughty.' अहम् अहङ्कारोऽस्त्यस्य. The termination यु as applied to अहं and शुभं means 'possessed of,' स्वप्रार्थनाभङ्गसम्भावनया क्रोधादहङ्कारवता Bh. J. M. mentions one variant अहंयुनाथः 'the lord of the proud,' अहंयूनां क्षत्रियाणां नाथ इतियोज्यम्. But the one we have adopted is better since it prepares us for something bad in case his request were not granted. **शुभंयुः** 'blessed' **ऊचे** (pas. perfect of वच्) 'was spoken to', 'was addressed', **तापसकुञ्जरेण** 'by the pre-eminent

hermit.' कुञ्जर as used at the end of a compound signifies any person preeminent or excellent of the class. Amara gives the following words used similarly; स्यरुत्तरपदे व्याघ्रपुङ्गवर्षभकुञ्जराः। सिंहशार्दूलनागाद्याः पुंसि श्रेष्टार्थवाचकाः॥ The Com. is Karmadharaya.

 21 **आप्थाः** (pas. aor. 2nd per. sing of आप्) 'hast been approached.' **शरणं** 'refuge,' 'protection.' We may construe this with आप् as a compound verb meaning to go to for protection;' or we may take it in apposition to त्वं 'thou who art my refuge or protection.' That शरणं is used with a masculine noun is clear from many classical usages. Cp. स सुरासुरस्य जगतः शरणं, सन्तप्तानां त्वमसि शरणं. J. M. construes in the first way त्वं शरणमाप्थाः प्राप्तोऽसि। Bh. in the second भयेषु शरणं रक्षिता त्व प्राप्थाः।

 **धर्मवृद्धयै** 'for the increase of religious merit.'

 **क्षात्रं** 'heroism' (क्षत्रियत्वं). It is a duty of a क्षत्रिय to make use of his military valour in the protection of Brahmanas absorbed in meditation, in return the latter give one sixth part of the merit of their austerities. Cp. क्षात्रो धर्मः श्रित इव तनुं ब्रह्मघोषस्य गुप्त्यै U. 6. 9. **परस्परार्थं** 'for mutual help.' अन्योन्यप्रयोजनकर्मव्यतीहारे सर्वनाम्नो द्वे भवतः समासवच्च बहुलमिति यदा न समासवत्तदा अयम्। J. M. अन्योन्यप्रयोजनकं जातिव्यक्त्योरभेदोपचारात् व्यतीहारे 'गतिहिंसे'ति सूत्रेऽन्योन्यार्थ इतिज्ञापका'त्परस्परं व्यतिलुनन्ति' इति उदाहरणेन च क्रियाव्यतीहारे परस्परार्थं भवतीतिबोद्धव्यम्। Bh. परस्पर is used in the sing only. Vide Can II 5 of our poem. परस्परार्थं is used adverbially since acc, are often used adverbially. sc. भवति.

 **कृथाः**=अकृथाः, अ being dropped as the negative particle मा is used along with the verb alone; मायोगे अम्निषेधः। sc. अस्मिन्सङ्कटे कथम्पुत्रं नियोजयामीति J. M. **प्रहिणु**—the imperative is expressive of request.

 22 **घानिष्यते** (pas. future of हन्) ' will be killed.' **विपक्षः** 'an enemy,' i. c. रावण as the adj. महान् shows.

**स्थायिष्यते**—pas. fut. of स्था—'will be resisted, lit, will be faced.' But to stand before or face an enemy is to oppose him and fight with him. The construction येन स्थायिष्यते is impersonal because स्था is an intransitive verb: Cp. येन गम्यते 'he goos.' येन is taken by the Com. J. M. and Bh. to refer to तेन i, e. रामेण, It is not wrong but we think that it is more natural to connect it with विपक्ष because it was रावण who opposed राम on the battle-field. Even taking परशुराम to be the great enemy, (पुरस्तादग्रतो यद्रणं युद्ध भावि परशुरामेण सार्धमितिभावः), we are justified in connecting येन with him and not with Rama, because we shall know later on that it was परशुराम who first challenged Rama to fight with him; (Can. III 50 &c.). Again तेन need not have येन or any other form of यद्, its correlative, since तेन refers to राम or स्वसूनुः in the previous stanza and names therefore one who is प्रक्रान्त (already described or known), while we know nothing of the enemy whom he is to kill. And moreover when यद् is used in the subsequent sentence it does not require its correlative. (यच्छद्वस्तूत्तरवाक्यगत एव सर्वत्र तच्छद्वापेक्षः समर्थः). For further information the acholar may refer to K. P. VII. J. M. alludes to परशुराम which is not right. We think that महान्विपक्षः may mean any great enemy but if any particular allusion is to be sought for it must be to Ravaṇa since the ultimate purpose was to kill Ravana and thus rescue the earth from the oppression of the great demon. Bh is silent on this point. The destruction of the great enemy includes that of petty ones. **पुरस्तात्** 'in the front,' तात् is used to denote 'the direction,' 'the place' and 'the time' पुरस्तादिति दिक्शब्दाद्विग्देशकाले इति सप्तम्याः स्तात् Bh. This termination is generally applied to पूर्व, अधर and अवर which are changed to पुरः, अधस् and अवस् respectively. पुरस्तात् is used alone or with Gen. or abl. Cp. यः पुरस्ताद्यतीनाम् M. 1. vide Can. II. 50.

 महात्मन्—'high-souled,' 'noble-minded.' महासत्व J. M. Bh. has महामते 'of great intellect.' आत्मा does bear

this meaning. 'आत्मादेहमनोब्रह्मस्वभावधृतिबुद्धिष्वि'तिविश्वः परिभूः—the augment अ is dropped as there is the prohibitive particle मा; मापरिभूः therefore means 'do not disregard. मावज्ञासीः or मातिरस्कुरु. See Can. IV. 37. परिभवनीयं is used in M. I. **मद्विधा** 'men of my sort or type', मद्विध इवि विधाप्रकार 'आतश्चोपसर्गे' इत्यङ्। (ter. अ before which no guna or Vriddhi takes place) विधा भेदः सादृश्यश्च। इह सादृश्यं गृह्यते मया विधा सादृश्यं यस्येति मद्विधः। मट् is substituted, cheifly at the beginning of a compound. It is sing. first person. 'प्रत्ययोत्तरपदयोश्च' इति मदादेशः। मद्विधः मत्सदृशः मदन्यः। J. M. अयोग्ये 'in an improper or feeble place or person.'. योगाय प्रभवति योग्यः 'योगाद्यत्'। Bh's discussion about the sense of अ in अयोग्य is given below: अनित्वविवक्षया नतिः तत्पुरुषो वानञः समास इति। 'नञ्तत्पुरुषसञ्ज्ञकसमासार्थं' परेसूत्रं कुर्वन्ति तन्मते प्रयोग्योऽयोग्य इतिविग्रहः। स्वप्नते योग्यादन्यः अयोग्यः 'अन्यारग्येत्यादिना' नञोऽन्यार्थत्वात् पञ्चमीसमासः। व्यम्पूर्वमिति नञः प्राग्भावः नञोनैवेत्यः एवंयद्ब्राह्मण इत्यत्र ब्राह्मणस्यनप्तदृशोऽब्राह्मणः समार्थेनेत्यादिना नञः समार्थत्वात्षष्ठी तेनात्र षष्ठीसमासः। 'अनिमित्तान्यथापश्यन्नि'त्यत्र एकार्थेन निन्दितानि च तानि निमित्तानि चेति कर्मधारयः नञो निन्दितार्थे एकार्थत्वात्। अपापमित्यत्र पापस्याभावोऽपापमित्यव्ययीभावः नञोऽव्ययत्वात्। एवमन्यत्र यथान्वयं बोद्धव्यम्। Bharata bases his discussion upon the various senses of अ, which are embodied in the following verse: तत्सादृश्यमभावश्च तदन्यत्वं तदल्पता। अप्राशस्त्यं विरोधश्चनञर्थाः षट् प्रकीर्तिताः॥ He explains the various senses by giving different illustrations and ultimately is in favour of the sense of तदन्यत्व in the word अयोग्य.

 23 **धक्ष्यति**—Future of दह् 'to burn' —'will burn,' 'will consume.' **विप्रवह्निः** 'the firy sage' the Brahman as burning as the fire. He is fire incarnate. Bh's dissolution विप्रएववह्निः is better than J. M's विप्रवह्निरिव because it is an instance of रूपक (तद्रूपकमभेदो य उपमानोपमेयोः K. P. X). The property of burning is peculiar to fire and the verb is धक्ष्यति which determines that the अलङ्कार is रूपक instead of उपमा. There is need of ident-

tity (अभेद) to make the sense real. (vide discussion on रात्रिकापालिक in काव्यप्रदीपः N. S, Ed. p. 385) यास्यन्—fut. part. of 'to go' —who will be going.' **समन्युं** 'full of grief. मन्यु is frequently used by Bhatti in this sense. अवालुलोचे—Perfect of लोच् with अव—'pondered over,' 'thought.' Between two disagreeable alternatives the king chooses the grief of separation, which is merely personal while the sage's wrath will be insrtumental in destroying his whole race which is a far greater calamity.
