He showed his wisdom in choosing the lesser evil.

 **अनुजज्ञे** sc. तेन 'avas sanctioned.' अनुज्ञातं नृपेणेति विभक्तिविपरिणामेन तेनेनियोज्यम्। कर्मणि लिट् (pas. perfect). ज्ञा अवबोधने परस्मैपदिलात्। न चानुपूर्वादस्मादात्मनेपदं विहितम् J. M. Though अनुज्ञा is both Paras and Atm, Cp. तदनुज्ञानीहि मां गमनाय U. 3. or यदि मानानुजानामि परित्यक्तोऽस्म्यहं त्वया M. I. 19 and अनुजज्ञे गमनं सुतस्य quoted by Prof. Apte in his Guide as an instance of active Aum form of अनुज्ञा, we are inclined to agree with J. M, cirtainly a high authority, in taking अनुजज्ञे as the pas. form. Mereover we think that as far as the 'sanctioning' sense of the verb is concerned, it is more often Paras in the active construction. Whenever we find it in the Atm it is invariably the passive construction Cp. सेयं याति शकुन्तला पतिगृहं सर्वैरनुज्ञायताम् S. IV. 8. Bharata makes it active, though he suggests that it may be passive, यद्वाविभक्तिव्यत्ययेन नृपेणसुतस्य गमनमनुजज्ञे अनुज्ञान्त कर्मणि प्रत्ययः। His another interpretation which takes अनु to niean पश्चात् is wrong since ततः gives the same sense. Herein also he takes जज्ञे as pas.

 24 **आश्रमाय** mark the dative. It is equivalant to आश्रमं गन्तुं (प्रतस्थे). The student will remember this idiomatic use of the dative. Cp. फलाय गच्छति. **प्रष्ठं** 'going before' (in front).

 **हिंस्रेषुदीप्ताप्तधनुः** 'with a brilliant, unfailing bow and deadly arrows'. The bow was unfailing on account

of the deadly arrows which it discharged. हिंस्रेषु (हिंस्र + इषु) deadly arrows ;' आप्त 'unfailing = अविसंवादि. हिंस्रेषुभिर्दीप्तं च धनुर्यस्य इतिविग्रहः Bah. Com. Rama's arrows were so well known for their unfailing character that they have become proverbial to denote an efficacious, never failing thing.e. g. रामबाण औषध. Mark that धनुः is not changed to धन्वन् because this change is अनित्य, "समासान्तविधिरनित्यः" इति। J. M. notices one variant हिंस्रेषु दीप्रास्रधनुः and comments दीप्र सस्त्रं धृष्टतया यस्य धनुषस्तद्वीप्रास्त्रं धनुर्यस्येतिसः। कस्मिन्विषये हिंस्रेषु (towords the ferocious ) नान्येषु। हिंस्रेषु is loc. plu. of हिंस्र. Bh's reading, which is adopted by one Bengalee editor, is हिंस्रेषु दीप्रास्त्रधरः। हिंस्त्रषु हिंसकेषु दीप्रं दीप्यमानम् अस्त्रं धरतीति। He takes notice of another reading हिंस्रेषु—दीप्तात्तधनुः। इतिपाठे हिंस्रेण इषुणा दीप्तमात्तं गृहीतं धनुर्येनेतिविग्रहः। Bh. The one we have adopted with J. M. is the best. The र that we find in नम्र, दीप्र & c. is a krit termi., नमिकम्पीत्यादिनारप्रत्ययान्ताः or कर्तरिरः।

 25 **पुण्यवनाय** is obj. to प्रयास्यतः (fut. part. of प्रया). It is कर्मणि चतुर्थी. **रोचिष्णुमुखस्य** ' of a blooming or resplendent face.'. Rama was very willing to accompany Visvamitra to the forest and when his father consented to send him with the hermit his face brightened. **धृष्णुः** brave.' The termination णु denotes a capability to do something or to undergo something. Mark well all such words occurring in these verses. क्षिपत्रसगृधघृषः क्नुरितिक्नुः शीलार्थे Bh.

 **त्रैमातुरः** Lakshmana, ‘the son of the three mothers.' तिसृणां मातॄणामपत्यं. As a last member of a Tat. compound मातृ is changed to मातुर् when the first member is a numeral, or सत् or भद्र ; अ is a krit ter. showing descent.' Lakshmaṇa is called the son of three mothers because he was born to his mother on her eating the sacrificial oblation given her by the other two wives of Dasaratha. Both Kousalya and Kekayi may be supposed to contribute their shares to his birth. पिण्डद्वयप्राशनात्ताभ्याञ्चजनितः J. M. **कृत्स्नजितास्रशस्त्रः**— अस्त्रञ्चशस्त्रञ्चेति-

द्वन्द्वः। कृत्स्नं समग्रं जितमधिगतम् अस्त्रं येनेति विग्रहः। 'who has maatered the whole science of missiles and weapons. Weapons are swords, arrows & c., Missiles are miraculous weapons backed by their respective incantations. The mental repetition of these incantations was enough to set the missile to work. There were missiles and counter— missiles to nullify the effect of the former; such as अग्न्यस्त्र, पर्वतास्त्र, पर्जन्यास्त्र &c. The acquisition of these two sciences made their possessor an invincible, at least an iudomitable, warrior. Cp. त्वचम्ममेध्यां परिधायरौमिशिक्षतास्त्रं पितुरेव मन्त्रवत् R. III. 31. **सध्य्रङ्** 'companion' सहाञ्चतीति 'to go with' अञ्च् 'to go ;' nom. of सध्यञ्च्.  
सध्रि is substituted for सह. सहस्य सधिरिति सध्र्यादेशः J. M. सहसन्तिरः सध्रीसमितिरीति सहशब्दस्य सध्र्यादेशः Bh. **रतः** 'intenton,’ ‘devoted to,' takes locative of the object. cp. Can. I. 2.

 26 Agreeably with the custom of poets, our poet changes at the end of the canto the metre of his verces. Cp. Raghu. In this verse we get an instance of locative absolute.

 **रघुसिंहे** vide note on तापसकुञ्जर st. 20. **दन्दशूकान्** 'demons' noun from the frequentative of दंश्, ऊक is a ternination showing 'tendency.' जिघांसौ (pres. part. from the desi. base of हन्) 'wishing' to kill.'

 **मुष्टिपीडं** (an instance of णमुल् infinitive in अम्, vide Apte's Guide) ' so as to press against the fist,' मुष्टिना पीडयित्वा। मुष्टिशब्दे तृतीयान्त उपपदे सप्तम्यां चोपपीडेतिणमुल्। J. M.  
This is adverbial to दधाने, pres. part. of धा atm 'holding.' Bh. takes this as an adj. to धनुः and translates सृष्टिनापीडायस्यतत्तथा। एतेन मुष्टेर्दार्ढ्यं सूचितम्। The fist was too strong to be pressed by the bow. The view of J. M. and others he characterises as the view of others. अन्ये तु प्रमाणाशक्त्यो स्तृतीयासप्तमीभ्यां क्त्वाच् चणं (णमुल्) समासो (compound) वेत्याहुः। तन्मते मुष्टिना पीडयित्वा इत्यर्थः। Some, he says, take पीड as a noun from and interprete मुष्टि पीडयतीतिपचादित्वादन् मुष्टिपीडमिति विशेषणेन धनुषोऽतिदार्ढ्यं सूचितमिति

केचित्। others take मुष्टि to mean 'stealing' and quote Kalidasa for a similar idea. केचित्तु मुष्टिं मोषणं पीडयतिखण्डयती त्यनेन चौर्यापसारणमपि कविभिर्वर्ण्यते "श्रुतौ तस्करतास्थिता" (R. I 27) इति कालिदास इत्याह। This explanation taken with the context is quite absurd. Some take मुष्टि to mean 'an enemy's fist' मुष्टिं हि सामर्थ्यात् शत्रुकृतां पीडयतीति केचित्। This is also not elegant.। धारणक्रियाविशेषणमिति केचित्। We favour J. M's view as being the view of Panini and agree with the last केचित् in making it an adverb to दधाने.

 ** बद्धचित्राङ्गुलित्रे** 'by whom the finger protector was tied' (to his finger). अङ्गुलित्र (अङ्गुलित्रायते) 'a finger protector,' a contrivance like a thimble used by archers to protect the thumb or finger from being injured by the bow-string. This adj will help us to explain मुष्टिपीडं as we have done. If the finger were stronger than the bow there should have been no need of a fingerprotector.

 **कथमपि** 'with great difficulty.' कथं connected with the particles चित्, चन and अपि has the above sense; cp. तस्य स्थित्वा कथमपि पुरः Me. 3 कथमपि उन्नमितं न चुम्बितं तु S 3.35. गुरुशोकात् 'though heavy with grief.' This renders the task of the damsels extremely difficult. They had to uake their best efforts to suppress the unauspicious tears which heavy greif was too prone to drop down. This abl, is therefore very significant and bespeaks the high poetic genius, which is able to paint the picture with single words, of our poet. Great poets possess this insight to the utmost degree. **मारुदन्** (मा + अरुदन् 2nd Form aorist) 'did not weep,' 'withheld their weeping. J. M. reads गुरुशोकाः (गुरुः शोको यासां ताः) but the ablative is more appropriate since it makes the position quite clear. It is a हेतु which lends beauty to  
the description.

 **माङ्गलिक्यः** 'auspicious.' The termination is expressive of प्रयोजन। मङ्गलमयोजनाः माङ्गलिक्यः। तदस्यप्रयोजनमिति ठञ् (इक termi.) J. M. मङ्गलायहिता मङ्गलप्रयोजना वा Bh. The form is

fem. nom. plu. of माङ्गलिकी. The presence of young married women is very auspicious and crying also is forbidden at an auspicious occasion. The young women had therefore to withhold their weeping tendency which was natural at a time when they were to be separated from one whom they dearly loved. Like the abl. above this adj. also is very significant, and does highest credit to our poet's artistic power. This also serves as a हेतु. It is हेतुगर्भविशेषण.

 The metre of this stanza is मालिनी . The Alankara is काव्यलिङ्ग.

 27 **तुपुलकलनिनादं** 'which gave out high and pleasing notes,' तुमुलो महान्कलो मधुरो निनादः ध्वनिर्यस्यति। J. m. **तुर्यम्** 'a kind of musical instrument,' i. e. कांस्यतालपटहादिसमूहम्। आजघ्नुः 'played upon,' lit. 'struck upon' ताडितवन्तो वादितवन्तो वा। हन् with आ is Paras except when the obj. is some limb of one's own body when it is Atm. Cp. कुट्टिममाजघान K. 10; परस्य शिर आर्हति sk; भाहते शिरः (one's own head). But we find Atm use even when the limb does not belong to oneself, cf. आजघ्ने विषविलोचनस्य वक्षः K I. 17. 63. In Can. VIII 15 we meet with आघ्नान इव...... सर्वतो मुहुः, i ea Atm form of आहन् upon which J. M. comments आङो यमहन इत्यविवक्षितकर्मकत्वादात्मनेपदम्, viz. the Atm is used since the object is not particularised. It is used intrasitively. "आङो यमहनः" इत्यात्मनेपदं नभवति। अकर्मकादित्यनुवर्त्तते। J. M. on आजघ्नुः॥

 **अभिमतफलशंसी** ‘indicating (शंसी) a desirable or agreeable fruit.' Though अभिमत is a past participle, the above meaning is preferrable since Rama had no desired object as such. The throbbing of the right arm is itself indicative of good fruit. This according to Com. foretells the acquisition of Sita in marriage. is The बाहु is necessarily 'the right arm' because the indication of agreeable fruit is the work of that arm according to our poets, in the case of men and that of the left arm in the case of women. Similarly the

throbbing of the eye. अत्र दक्षिणबाहुः सामर्थ्याद्रस्यते स्वाङ्गवात्। अनेनसीताप्राप्तितीव मुपन्यस्तम्। J. M. दक्षिणबाहुस्पन्दनं कान्तालिङ्गनमूचकमिति वृद्धाः Bh. Cp. शान्त मिद माश्रमपदं स्फुरतिच बाहुः कुतः फलमिहास्य S. I. 16. बिवृण्वतेव कल्याणमान्तरज्ञेन चक्षुषा। स्फुरता वामकेनापि दाक्षिण्यणबलंव्यते॥ Mal. I. 8; aloo अहो अपोगो मे परिस्कुराते किमपि वामकम् M. II. 4. and मृच्छकटिक act II, चारुदत्तः apeech on his way to the City Court, अनुकुलाः auspicious' the warbling of certain birds is suspicious, cp. बामे मधुरवाक् पक्षी वृक्षः पल्लवितोऽग्रतः। अनूकुलो वहन्वायुः प्रयाणे शुभशंसिनः quoted by Bh. The metro is मालिनी

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

**CANTO II.**

 This canto begins with a very beautiful description of the autumn. The autumn was ever considered to be the fittest time for carrying on wars with an enemy and Vishvamitra has chosen that period for the destruction of the demone at the hands of Rama. The student will therefore see that Rame with his brother Lakshmana sets out with the sage to his hermitage in the autumn. The beauty of this sesson is really attractive. Nature everywhere appears to be full of life and beauty. The student will notice the richness of imagery, the flights of poetic fancy and the descriptive power, in general, of our poet which is undoubtedly very high and which forms one of the qualities of this poem, thus entitling him to the honour of a great poet. The great Kalidasa describes this season in his "Description of the seasons" (ऋतुसंहारकाव्य) Can. III. A similar description he gives in his gi Can. I and IV where Dilipa sets out to the hermitage of his family priest and Raghu is said to surpass he season by his glory (cp. पुण्डरीकातपत्रस्तं.....चामरः। ऋतुविण्डम्बयामास नपुनः प्राप तच्छियम् Can, IV. 17) respectively. The student is strongly recommended to read them.

 ** वनस्यतीनां** 'of trees' in general; we need not restrict the application of this word to big trees. His

not necessary to take the word in its literal sense. वनस्य पतिः वनस्पतिः अत्र लोकप्रत्यीत्या वृक्षा द्रष्टव्या न तु पारिभाषिकाः। J. M. The compound belongs to the class of पारस्करादि स् is inserted in the middle irregularly. **तेजस्विनां** 'of the shining ones,' 'of the brilliant ones,' lit, possessing lustre तेजोयस्यास्तीति. The heavenly bodies, the sun, the moon and the stars are meant here. The sky being entirely free from clouds which impart darkness to the quarters by shutting out the light of these luminaries, the quarters receive the full lustre of these heavenly bodies aud appear resplendent. We are not to suppose that that the sun, the moon, the planets and the stars spread their light at one and the same time, which, it is at once manifest, is impossible but when they do it, they do it to the utmost degree, there being no hindrance from the clouds. विन् is a possessive termination applied to स्रज्, मेधा, माया and mostly to nouns ending in अस्. **कान्तिभृतां** adj. to दिशां 'bearing clearness,'तेजस्विनां चन्द्रतारकादीनां कान्तिं नैर्मल्यं बिभ्रतीति तासां दिशाञ्च। तदाहि निर्मला दिशा भवन्ति। The quarters put on clear appearance because there are no clouds to mar their natural beauty. Cp. स्फुटकुमुदचितानां राजहंसंस्थितानाम्। मरकतमणिभासा वारिणा भूषितानाम्॥ श्रियमतिशयरूपाव्योमतोयाशयानाम्। वहति विगतमेर्घं चन्द्रतारावकर्णिम्॥२१॥ विगतजलदवृन्दा दिग्वि भागा मनोज्ञाः। ...विमलकिरणचन्द्र व्योम ताराविचित्रम्॥२२॥ Rs.III. also 11 and 12, and vide R. X. 11-12. **निर्याय** 'going out' (gerund). Mark that instead of the termination a, is used when the verb is preceded by a preposition. **श्रियम्** 'beauty,' 'splendour,' of trees &c. This word is frequently used by the poets in this sense ; Cp. मुखं कमलश्रियं दधी Ku. 5. 21, .......सुजातयोः पङ्कजकोशयोः श्रियम् R. III. 8, श्रियमतिशयरूपां quoted above and ...... सप्तच्छदेानुषङ्गता कुसुमोद्रमश्रीः R. III. 13. वनस्पतीन्ना पुष्पसम्बन्धात् सरसां विकसितपद्मादिमत्वान्नदीदिक् तेजखिनामन्यत्कान्तिभृत्त्वम् Bh. **ददर्श** It is impossible to observe the autumn—a time which is abstract. But we can see its effects

and thus figuratively say that we see the season itself. Metre is इन्द्रवज्रा.

 2 **तरङ्गसङ्गात्** 'through contact with the billows.' The petals were set in gentle motion by the billows which gently dashed against them. **चपलैः पलाशैः** 'by (their) petals gently moving.' **ज्वालाश्रियम्** 'the beauty of flames,' 'the beauty like that of flames," ज्वालानांश्रीरिवश्रीताम् **सातिशयां** 'excessive.' **दधन्ति** neu. plu, of the pre part. of धा . 'bearing.' **सधूमदीप्ताग्निरुचीनि** 'splendour like that of the fire accompanied by smoke,' सधूमदीप्ताग्ने रुचिरिवरुचिर्येषाम्. **रेजुः**— 3rd per. plu. perfect 0. राज् ‘shone,’ vide · फणाञ्चसप्तानाम्' in Dhaturupakoshaf ताम्रोत्पलानां of red lotuses,' lit. 'possessing red petals.' The red lotuses are particularly mentioned because here there is a comparison, so to speak, between the splendour of lotuses and of fire accompanied by smoke. The flames of fire are, it need not be told, red and it is therefore essential that to make the comparison complete, red lotuses should be particularly stated. Again the flames of fire have a gentle waving motion which the lotuses also have as much as their petals are moved by their coming in contact with the gentle waves of the lake. Again the fire is accompanied by dark smoke. The lotuses are also smoky since the bees humming thereon possess a dark colour greatly resembling the dark smoke. The student will thus see that the comparison is complete in all its parts. Mark the beauty of the description. **आकुलषट्पदानि** 'on which bees are hovering.' Bees are described as being very fond of lotus-honey which they drink till they get intoxicated. The student will not fail to read ऋतुसंहार Can. II. for similar descriptions which cannot be transcribed here for fear of increasing the bulk of the book. The Alankara in this stanza as well as in many others is स्वभावोक्ति, in which things are described

to the very life, (स्वभावोक्तिस्तु डिम्मादेः स्वक्रियारूपवर्णनम् K. P. X.).

 3 **विवाङ्गतैः** 'reflected into the water.' The trees on the bank were reflected into the water. **समृद्धिम्** 'splendour.' **अपहृताम्** 'snatched away' 'deprived of' by the waters. **सामर्षतयेव** 'as if through jealousy.' अमर्षता = अमर्षस्यभावः अमर्षता 'jeolousy.' इव shows that it is उत्प्रेक्षा. **सरोजलक्ष्मी** 'the splendour of the water-lotuses, सरसि जायन्तेसरोजास्तेषां लक्ष्मीम्. **स्थलपद्महासैः** ‘with the splendour of land-lotuses.' The simple fact, so poetically expressed by our poet, is this: As there were lotuses in the rivers so there were lotuses, also on their banks. There were likewise trees on the banks which were reflected into the waters. It is always a pleasant sight to see objects reflected into water. The water also appears to be invested with the beauty of the trees therein reflected. When it was therefore abserved by the banks that the waters had deprived them of their beauty which rightfully belonged to them, they wished to retaliate and showed their retaliation by the splendour of the lotuses growing on them as it were depriving the waters of their beauty which they possessed on account of their lotuses. It appears necessary to suppose that the lotuses in the waters were moon-lotuses, while the lotuses on the land were sun-lotuses. It was in the day time that Rama is described as observing the splendour of the season-a time when the moon lotuses fade and lose their splendour. The land lotuses may therefore be aptly described as depriving the former of their splendour.

 Cons: बिम्बागतैस्तरिवनैः (करणभूतैः) पयोभिः (कर्तृभिः) निजां समृद्धिमपहृतां विलोक्य (नद्यादिनां) कूलानि सामर्षतयेव स्थलपद्महासैः (पयः सम्बन्धिनीं) सरोजलक्ष्मीं तेनुः

 4 निशातुषारौः 'with dew drops of the night. The

falling of dew in the night is a common spectacle in these cold days. **नयनाम्बुकल्पैः** 'resembling tears.' तुषारऽ are here poetically described as the tears of the tree on the bank (तीरतरु). Vide for कल्प the note on शतमन्युकल्प Can. I. 5. **पर्णान्तपर्यागलदच्छबिन्दुः** 'from the ends of the leaves of which water-drops were tickling down,' पर्णान्तात्पर्यागलन्तः अच्छबिन्दवोयस्य. **उपारुरोद** 'wept for,' (Perf, of उपा + रुद्), used transitively. **नदत्पतङ्गः** 'on which birds were warbling.' 'the lotuscreeper' which blooms on a moon-lit night, a moonlotus.

  The poet has expressed in this verse, a poetic idea, the very conception of which is itself very happy. Our poet has ascribed life and sympathy to an inanimate thing. Only a poet of high emotions and feelings who sees nature replete with life and amination can conceive such an exquisite idea. All great and true poets, like Shakspeare and Wordsworth, Kalidasa aud Bhavabhuti are pantheistic in their nature. Our poet, who it is evident from such verses, does not lack this high poetic faculty, presents natural objects as full of life. The idea of such exquisite beauty is this: as remarked above a water-lily blooms at moon rise and the moon is considered as the lord of such creepers. At moon-set therefore the waterlily fades and loses her splendour and thus wears a gloomy appearance, as if, grieved for the separation of her lord. The tree on the banks is descrihed as sympathising with her sorrowful condition; he shares in her grief which he manifests by weeping (i. e. dropping dew-drops) and crying (with the notes of birds). Is this not a most happy idea ? The अलङ्कार is उत्मेक्षा as एव shows.

 5 **निलीनभृङ्गैः** 'with bees settling on them.' This is to be construed both with पुष्पैः and सरोजैः. The action of observing each other's beauty is done by

means of the eyes in the form of the bees. The Alankara is उत्प्रेक्षा.

 6 **प्रभातवाताहतिकम्पिताकृतिः** 'whose body was trembling with the morning breeze.' आहति 'striking,' 'pushing.' प्रभाते यो वातस्तस्याहत्या कम्पिता आकृतिर्यस्याः पद्मिन्याः सा। The पद्मिनी is gently moved by the morning breeze. This movement to and fro of her makes its difficult of the bee to alight on her. The poet says that the lotus wards the bee off by the angry shaking of her hand. She plays the part of an angry woman. The body of the offended woman also trembles with anger and the passionate heat of the night which she spends alone. The morning breeze is enough to excite her on the occasion of her false lord's approach.

 ** कुमुद्वतीरेणुपिशङ्गविग्रहम्** 'with a body reddish with the pollen-dust of the moon-lotus. कुमुद्वत्या रेणुभिः पिशङ्गो विग्रहो यस्य. This reddish colour of his body betrays his faithlessness to her (पद्मिनी). The man also is betrayed by the reddish colour of the ointments of the woman's body transmitted to his. **निरास** (Perf. of अस् with निः) 'warded off,' 'rejected.' **पद्मिनी** 'at lotus-creeper blooming at sun-rise.' मानिनी 'an angry woman,' "one offended with her husband' (through jealous pride) for his addresses or love to another woman. **अन्यसङ्गमम्** 'intercourse with another woman,' अन्ययासहसङ्गमं sc. पन्युः। यथा अन्यया स्त्रिया सहोषितं तदङ्गसङ्क्रान्तपरिमलकण्ठमालमात्मदयितं काचित् कुपिता निरस्यति तद्वत् । J. M. अन्ययोषिता सह गमितरात्रिं पतिं तदङ्गलग्नचन्दनचिन्हेन निर्णीय क्रोधात्कम्पितवती निरस्यति तथेयमपीतिभावः। Bh. The idea is that the bee during the night enjoys the company of the moon-lotus creeper by gathering the pollen-dust or honey therein, since at that time a Padmini is closed. As soon as the sun rises he quits the moon-lotus since she then closes and comes to the Padmini, for enjoyment who like a proud jealous woman rejects him. This is analogous

to the conduct of a woman who rejects her husband who has bestowed his love on her co-wife (or it may be a mere harlot). The greatest pain to a proud woman is that her husband flirts with another woman. Such a woman is technically called खण्डिता (पार्श्वमेति प्रियो यस्या अन्यसम्भोगचिह्नितः। सा खण्डितेति कथिता धीरैरीर्ष्याकषायिता S. D., or निद्राकषायमुकुलीकृतताम्रनेत्रो नारीनखव्रणविशेषावचित्रिताङ्गः। यस्याः कुतोऽपि गृहमेतिपतिः प्रभाते सा खण्डितेति कथिता कविभिः पुरराणैः॥). The Alankaras are उपमा and अर्थातरन्यास in which a general proposition is adduced to support a particular one and vice versa, (उक्तिरर्थान्तरन्यासः स्यात् सामान्यविशेषयोः vide also K. P. X). Bh. gives another reading, viz. 'न मानिनीशं सहतेऽन्यसङ्गमम्' which means a proud woman rejects her lord who enjoys the company of another woman. This reading makes अन्यसङ्गमम् an adj. (Bah. Com.) qualifying ईशं . But we think that this reading is not so good as the one we have adopted in the text because संसहते gives a better meaning, the preposition सम् makes the action intensive, meaning 'rejects him entirely.'

 7 **दत्तावधानं** 'who has fixed his attention,' construed with **मधुलोहगीतौ** 'on the song or buzz of bees,' मधु लेदुंशीलमेषामिति णिनिः (इन् a krit term.). Another reading mentioned by J. M. is मधुलेहगीतौ which gives the same sense but लेह is a noun from the verb by the termination अ and not by इन् as in लेहिन्. लिहन्तीति लेहाः पचाद्यच् (अ, e. g. पचः) मधुनो लेहाइतिषष्टीसमासः मधुलिहन्तीति वा कर्मण्यम्। J. M. **प्रशान्तचेष्टं** 'whose movements were at a complete standstill,' 'गीतो 'धानम् serves as a reason for the suspension of his movements. It is हेतुगर्भविशेषणम्. **आकर्णयन्** adj. to मृगावित्. **लक्ष्ये** 'on the mark aimed at' i. e. the deer whom the hunter wanted to shoot, Cp.. उत्कर्षः स च धन्विना यदिषवः सिध्यन्ति लक्ष्ये चले S. **समाधिं** ‘fixed attention,' 'concentration of the mind.' मृगावित् ‘the.hunter,’ (मृगान् विध्यतीति).

 It is well known that even inferior animals exhibit a strong love for songs and music. Sometimes deer are caught by the same trick. The hunters begin music and singing and the deer get so enraptured with it that they scarcely suspect the danger. Similarly the snake charmer makes use of his music to catch snakes. Cp. गीतमुत्सादकारिमृगाणाम् K. 32.

 8 **नितम्बे** 'on the ridge.' **विभिन्नं** 'broken up,' ' scattered,' adj. to अभ्र. **हिमाभम्** 'having the appearance of dew(हिमरयेव आभायस्य) on account of the residual water. **सरिन्मुखाभ्युच्चयम्** ‘augmentation of the sourse of the river.' मुखं 'source,' 'spring. The water coming down from the cloud augments the flow of a river at its scource. **अनुचकार** 'imitated,' used with acc, as here or with gen; cp. अनुकरोतिभगवतो नारायणस्य ; ननु कलमेन युथपते रनुकृतम् M. 5. The cloud is described here as bearing the beauty of the Himalayas. The Himalayas are a souce of a good many rives, two of which are the Ganges and the Brahmaputra. There is evidently beauty about a mountain from which spring forth rivers. This beauty the cloud is described to imitate.

 ** अभ्रं** 'cloud,' Bh. derives this word in various way, though the correct derivation appears to be अपो बिभर्तिति अब्भ्रः or अभ्रः। अभ्रतीति अभ्रम् अभ्रगत्यां पचादित्वादन् (i. e. a noun in अ from अभ्र ‘to wander'). यद्वा न भ्रश्यन्ति जलान्यस्मादिति गमादित्वात् हनजनाद्रमादेर्ड इतिजः (i. e, formed by adding the krit termination 34 before which the final consonant of a root is dropped, cp. अन्तगः, दूरगः). न भ्रश्यन्तियतस्तेभ्यो जलान्यभ्राणि तान्युत इतिनिरुक्तिः। अपोभ्रश्यन्त्यस्मादितिवा पूर्ववत्डः, the word being अब्भः। अपो बिभर्तीति केचित्। Bh:

 9 **क्रमम्बबन्ध** 'prepared himself, 'put himself in a position' assumed by an animal before taking a leap. उत्पतितुं यत्सामर्थ्ये तच्चकार J. M. उत्पतनानुकूलशरीरक्रियां चकार। Bh. बन्ध is here used in the sense कृ. अनेकार्थत्वाद्धातूनां बधिरत्र करणे वर्तते J. M. How often do we think that an echo is

an answer given us by somebody else! Tue story of a boy who called bad names and was answered accordingly in return by the echo is familiar to us.

 From Vers 2 to vers 9 our poet described the season in general. Now he describes it with reference to Rama, what experiences he had on the way. This former description, though very beautiful, may appear out of place, dissociated as it is from the hero of the poem. Kalidasa is more artistic in giving us only such description as is connected with the king दिलीप.

 10 **अदृक्षत**— 6th Form of दृश— 'saw.’ **नवोत्पलानि**— Bah. Com. नवान्युत्पलानियेषु— 'in which there were fresh lotuses.' Bh's interpretation of this word as a Karma. Com. नवानि उत्पलानि चादृक्षतेतिवा is not good. आघ्रायि— pas. aor. of घ्रा— 'smelt.' : **सुगन्धः** 'sweet-scented,' Mark that according to the rules which lays down that is changed to गन्धि in a Bah. Com. when it is preceded by उत्, पूर्ति, सु and सुरभि or when the compound implies comparison, here गन्ध is not changed to गन्धि because in the formation we are to take into consideration the fact that गन्ध must be the peculiar property of the object itself or the object must be completely surcharged with it. In this instance we know that is not the property of the wind and the wind is not completely surcharged with it since the fragrance of the अरविन्द cannot do it. "गन्धस्येदुत्पतिसुसुरभिभ्य" इतीकारः समासान्तो नभवति। गन्धस्येत्वे तदेकान्तग्रहणमितिवचनात् सुगन्ध आपणिक इतियथा। J. M. सूत्सुरभिपूतेर्गन्धादिरिति समवेतस्यैव गन्धस्य ग्रहण मत्रतु परम्परया गन्धसम्बन्धान्न इप्रत्ययः। Bh. This Com. mentions सुगन्धिः as a reading which is inconsistent with his explanation which makes it a noun in इन् i. e. सुगन्धिन् which requires सुङ्गधी. But we might defend this reading thus समवायाध्याहारात् सुगन्धिः समीरण इतिप्रयोग इतिपाणिनीयाः। Bh.

 11 **लतानुपातं** 'going to creeper after creeper,' or. 'after bending one creeper after another.' अनुपातं is

the gerund in अम् (णमुल्) from पत् with अनु. The णमुल् is here used to give the idea of succession, a going from one to another; other verbs whose णमुल् forms are used in a similar sense are विश्, पद् and स्कन्द्. Three of these are illustrated in this stanza. It is generally found that either the form is used twice or the thing which is governed by them (Cp. स्थायं स्थायं क्वविद्यान्तं क्रान्त्वा क्रान्त्वा स्थितं कचित् Can. 5. 51). But here the णमुल् forms are used as compounds and so the repitition of the gerund or the object governed by it, is not found in this verse. In the dissolution of the compound, however, we are to write thus लतां लतामनुपात्य or लतामनुपान्य अनुपात्य and it is similar with other verbs. विशिपतिपदिस्कन्दां व्याप्यमानसेव्यमानयोरिति द्वितीयान्त उपपदे णमुल्विधीयते। तत्र व्याप्यमाने द्रव्यवचनस्य आसेव्यमाने च क्रियावचनस्य नित्यवीप्सयोरिति द्विर्वचनं विधीयते। अत्र तु समासेनैवोक्तत्वात् नोपयुज्यत इति स्थितम्। J.M. The dissolutions given by Bharata differ : लतानां पातस्य पश्चात् लतानुपातमित्यव्ययीभावः। लतानां पातमनुक्रम्येति लतानां पतनमनतिक्रम्येति वा। अव्ययानामनेकार्थत्वादनुशब्दोऽनतिक्रमेऽपि। We say, once for all, that we like to follow पाणिनी. **नद्यवस्कन्दम्** (नदीं नदीमवस्कन्द्य नदीं वा अवस्कन्द्य अवस्कन्द्य)। J. M. ‘descending into one river after another.' नद्यामवस्कन्दोऽवगाहो यत्रस्नानक्रियायां नदीयमितिबोधो यत्रेति वा। Bh. **उपास्पृशत्** (Imperf. of उप + स्पृश्) 'sipped,' आचमनं कृतवान् J. M. Bh. translates स्नातवान् and quotes उपस्पर्शः स्पर्शमात्रे स्नानाचमनयोरपीतिविश्वः But the sense of bathing is not good in this instance since it is impossible, nay even absurd, to suppose that Rama bathed in each and every river he met on his way. **कुतूहलात्** 'through curiosity.' This is to be construed with all his actions, i. e. with all the verbs. **चारुशिलोपवेशम्** (चारुशिलाः चारुजिला उपविश्य or चारुशिला उपविश्य उपविश्य). J. M. ' sitting on one beautiful stone after another' चारुशिलायामुपवेशोवसनं यत्रासनक्रियायां चारुशिलानां रत्नशिलानामुपगता वेशायस्मादिति वा। एतेनरामस्थित्या रत्नशिलानां सौन्दर्ये सूचितम्। Bh. चारुशिला does mean a jem or jewel but it is evidently better to take it to

mean ‘a beautiful slab of stone' Bh. gives the view of, the followers of Paniṇi and refers his explanation of what we have called gerunds, to theirs पातादयो घङनाः लतानुपातमादयो णमन्ता इति पाणिनीयाः। तन्मते लतां लतामनुपालय नदीं नदीमवस्कन्ध गत्वा चारुशिलायामुपविश्येत्यर्थः। स्वमते चणम् 'समूलघात'मित्यत्र व्याख्यातः।

  **काकुत्स्थ** 'a descendant of king Kakustha. ककुत्स्थ is an epithet of Puranjaya, son of Sasuda, a king of the solar race and a descendant of Ikshvaku. It should be observed that Rama belongs to the race of the solar kings who claimed the sun for their primitive ancestor; the Pandavas belonged to the lunar race. Mythology relates that, when in their war with the demons, the gods were often worsted, they, headed by Indra, went to the powerful king Puranjaya and requested him to be their friend in battle. The latter consented to do so, provided Indra carried him on his shoulders. Indra accordingly assumed the form of a bull, and Puranjaya, seated on his hump, completely vanquished the demons. Puranjaya is therefore calJed Kakustha, ‘standing on a hump.' Cp. इक्ष्वाकुवंश्यः ककुदं नृपाणां ककुत्स्थ इत्याहितलक्षणोऽभूत्। काकुत्स्थशब्दं यत उन्नतेच्छाः श्लाघ्यं दधत्युत्तरकोशलेन्द्राः॥ महेन्द्रमास्थाय महोक्षरूपं यः संयति प्राप्तपिनाकीलीलः। ... .. R. VI. 71-2. Bh. reads the word as ककुस्थ and comments: ककुदि स्थितत्वात्ककुस्थदक्ष्वाकुः 'पृषोदरादित्याद्व'कारलोपइति रायमुकुटादयः। स्वमते 'मनीषादित्वादि'ति यथा देवीदासचक्रवर्ती कदाचिद्वानरेश्वरइवमुग्रीवो वैदेहीतिब्रुवाणस्यालघुका कुस्थस्यार्थिनः क्रियतां सफलेति वानरपुङ्गवानादिशदिति नलचम्पूश्लेषः तेन निस्तकारकाकुस्थ शब्द इति बोध्यम्। 'प्राधान्ये राजलिङ्गे च वृषाङ्के ककुदोऽस्त्रियामि'त्यमरः। केचित्तुः निपातनात् ककुन्द शब्दस्यातो लुकि ककुत्स्थशब्दस्तकारवानित्याहुः। तैस्तुनिपातनात्ककुदस्यातो लुगिति वृथोक्तं 'दान्तककुद्' शब्दस्य विद्यमानत्वात्। तथाहि ककुदोऽस्त्री ककुञ्च स्त्री 'वृशाङ्के राजलक्ष्मणी'ति भूरिप्रयोगः ककुद्यंशेद्दस्यागमश्च। निश्तकार एव ककुस्थ शब्दइति कश्चित् तन्न। तकारवतोऽपि प्रयोगस्य दृश्यमानत्वात्। तथाच राघवपाण्डवीये। "सार्द्धन्द्विजैः संवृतधाग्नि जिष्णावुपेयुषि ख्यातककुत्स्थवश्यः" इति। Both the forms are,

therefore, permissible. **ईषत्स्पयपानः** 'similing' यद्यपि स्मिङधातो रीषद्धसनमेवार्थस्तथापीषच्छब्देनात्यन्तानुपलभ्यहास्यत्वेन गाम्भीर्येसूचितम् Bh.

 12 **तिग्मांशुरपिच्छुरितानि** 'blended with the rays of the sun,' and therefore brightened by them. The lustre of the rays was transfered to the waters on account of the sun falling upon them and even piercing through them. **प्राञ्चि** 'in the east.' Mark the declension of this noun along with प्रत्यञ्च् उदञ्च् & c. **द्रुतानि** ‘melted,' ‘liquified.' The poet fancies that the waters were not as such but they were the lustre of the sun liquified or melted down. The process of melting went on by means of the streams of the rays गभस्तिधाराभिः). The lustre thus liquified filled same part of the earth. This fanciful description is suggested by the waters appearing as bright as the rays, through their contact with them. The idea is exquisitely poetical सम्भृतानि ' collected,' 'deposited. The Alankara is Utpreksha.

 13 **लोचनलोभनीयाः** 'fascinating or chaming to the eyes. अनीय is a krit, ter to form potential pas. part. तव्यानीयया इत्यनीयः Bh. लोचनाना लोभनीया इतिषष्ठीसमासः। Besides this dissolution Bh. gives two more : यद्वा लोचनानां लोभनीयं लोभो दर्शनेच्छारूपो यत्र पूर्वेणभावेऽनीयः। लोभनीय. is here taken as an abstract noun लोचनानि लोभयन्तीति कर्त्तयनीय इति केचित्। अनीय denotes agent. स्वमतेऽपि नियोक्तमर्हतीति 'नियोग्यः प्रभुः' इति वाक्यात् क्वचित्कर्त्तव्यपि तव्यादयःस्युरितिभूचितम्। **मृजान्वयाः** ‘pure.' मृजा ' purity, a fem. noun of the verb; before this fem. ter. no guna or Vriddhi मृज्; takes place; Cp. भिदा, छिदा, स्पर्धा. मृजया अन्योऽनुगमो यासाम्। शुद्धनुगत इन्वर्थः। J. M. मृजाया अन्वयाः शुद्ध्यनुगता इत्यर्थः। मृजाया अन्वयः सम्बन्धा यन्त्रेति वा। Bh. अन्वय = अन्वित cp. गन्धः कटुकान्वयः

 ** स्नेहमिवस्त्रत्रन्तीः** 'as if oozing out friendship.' For the elucidation of the idea expressed herein it seems necessary to suppose that there were drops of water

of the morning dew adhering to the corn rows, which were trickling down. The poet fancies that they were not the drops of water but at the approach of Rama the corn-rows were filled with a feeling of friendship for him; they were, as it were, therefore dropping down tears of joy and friendship at his arrival. Vide note on st. 4 supra. **ऋज्वायताः** (harma. Com. ऋजवश्चता आयताश्च) ' straight or upright and long 'or tall.' **वितृणान्तरालाः** ' the grass in the interval of which is removed or rooted out.' The grass is removed with a view that it may not obstruct the growth of corn. उत्पाटितानि तृणानि अन्तराले मध्यभागे यासां ताः। J. M. उत्पाटित्तृणत्वात्तृणरहितमन्तरालमभ्यन्तरं यासाम् Bh. Bh's dissolution is better than that of J. M. since the first dissolution makes it a व्यधिकरणबहुव्रीहि Com., which is not allowed in such cases. The Alankara in the first line is उत्प्रेक्षा.

 14 **काले** ‘at the proper or fixed time.' **नृपांशं** 'the tax imposed by the king,' lit. the part belonging to the king as the land-dues from his subjects. The portion to be paid to the royal treasury was generally one sixth part of the gross-produce. The land tax was then paid in kind and not in money. **विहितं** p.p of धा with वि, 'imposed,' 'levied.' **आहार्यशोभारहितैः** 'without artificial splendour,' i. e. without ornaments & c. There was no artificiality about these men. They were simple children of nature, possessed of such beauty with which they were invested by nature. This fact also shows their poverty. आहार्य 'artificial,' 'accidental,' कटकादिभि राहरणीया कृत्रिमा। Cp. न रम्यमाहार्य मपेक्षते गुणं ki. 4. 23. निसर्गसुभगस्य किमाहार्यकाडम्बरेण। **पुम्भिः प्रचितान्** 'occupied by the cowherds.' पुम्भिः here it is necessary to understand the गोप men though the general signification of the word is a male. The cowherds were living with their families, no doubt, since the adj. नभिज्ञैः shows that they never experienced the sorrow of separation.

 15 **अवक्राणि** 'straight,' i. e. free from glances, or side-long looks. This shows that the women were innocent and unacquainted with the art of jesticulation with which women of the town are familiar. The force of अपि is that the looks of these women were attractive in spite of their simplicity. वीक्षितानि 'tooks,' 'eyes.' वीक्षीत is used as an abstract noun. Past p. are used in this way according to the rule भावेक्तः **स्वभावान्** ‘natures' तत्कार्यविलोकनादेव तद्विलोकनव्यपदेशः Bh. Cp. विलासा नागरस्त्रीणां न तथारमयन्ति नः। यथा स्वभावसिद्धानि वृत्तानि वनयोषिताम्॥ इाते कौमुदी quoted by Bh.

 16 **विवृत्तपार्श्वम्** In the act of churning this pheno menon is observed. There is an alternate moving, to and fro, of the sides. • **हारम्,** अङ्गहार (अङ्गं ह्रियते इतस्ततः चाल्पतेयत्र) 'Movements of the limbs.' These two are adj. to नृत्य and as such are Bah. Com. **नितम्बरम्यम् **(समुद्वहता चारुनितम्बेनरम्यम्) pleasant on account of the graceful hips moving aside' '**दत्ततालं** adj. नृत्यं (Bah. Com.) ताल 'time kept in the dancing.' **नृत्यम्** 'the dance,' consisted in the postures of the women when engaged in the act of churning. They were churning but it appeared that they were dancing. A dance is accompanied by music, &c. which were present even in this act. नृत्यं or नृत्तं is thus defined 'अङ्गिकाभिनयपायमल्पवाचिकसासत्विकम्। भावानामास्पदं नृत्यं पदार्थव्यञ्जनात्मकम्.'

 17 **त्रस्नु ‘**timid' The deer are timid by nature. नु is a krit ter. showing tendency; also, गृध्नु, क्षिप्नुः &c. **वनोपशोभम् **The Com. translate this thus: 'who ** **come to the forest and who appear beautiful on the disappearance of the clouds.' It thus appears that they take वन and उपशोभा as two separate words, both governed by the p. p. उपात्त and not as a Gen. Tat. Com., वनस्योपशोभा. Their dissolution is मेघात्यये उपात्तं वनं (उपात्ता) उपशोभा चयेन. That the deer betake themselves to a forest after the rainy season may be easily grant-

ed but we do not know that the deer appear more beautiful than usual during this time. Another interpretation is possible and, to our mind, more natural. We may take वनोपशोभा to mean the beauty of the forest and the whole should be translated 'who have come to the beauty of the forest (i. e. to the beautiful forest) after the disappearance of the clouds, i. e. after the end of the rainy season; मेघात्यये उपात्ता वनस्योपशोभायेन.

 18 **लीनाः '**settled upon.' This is to be construed with ˚प्रचयेषु and सैकतेषु. **संसक्तफेणेषु** adj. to सैकतेषु 'to which foam was adhering.' **प्रतीयिरे** (pas. aor. of इ with प्रति) sc. रामेण 'were recognised.' The swans cannot be distinguished by their bodies because their whiteness was merged into that of the white lotuses and foam.

 19 **पङ्कज '**a tolus,' lit. anything born in mud (पङ्के जायते. Anything therefore produced in mud may be called पङ्कज but the word is restricted in its sense, such a sense is called a योगरूढ sense i. e. a sense which is partly etymological and partly conventional. A word may be either रूढ, यौगिक or योगरूढ. This stanza sums up the description of the season. The poet has displayed his power of marking the beautiful in nature. The Alankara is एकावली (पूर्वकालविशेषणतयास्थितं वस्तु परं विशेष्यं कृन्वायत्र स्थाप्यतेऽपोह्यते वा सैकावली K. P. X ). Metre is वंशस्थ.

 20 **यायजूकाः **this word is derived from the frequentative base of यज् by adding the ter. ऊक, showing a frequent tendency on the part of the agent. who frequently performs sacrifices.' Cp. वावदूक. **भिक्षुमुख्यैः** 'with the chief of the religious mendicants.' भिक्षु is one who has entered upon the fourth stage of religious life (सन्न्यास). The four periods of religious life of the three first castes are ब्रह्मचर्य 'the life of a student,’ गार्हस्थ ‘the life of a house-holder,' वानप्रस्थ 'the life of an anchorite or hermit' and सन्न्यास 'the life of

a भिक्षु or mendicant.' Some authorities deny the fourth period to the क्षत्रिय and वैश्य. **कुम्भहस्ताः** (व्यधि. Bah. Com.), उद is optionally substituted for उदक in a compound ; J. M. Bh. says that this is not a substitution but उद is a different word: स्वमते उदशब्दोऽप्यस्ति. The use of propitiatory water is believed to have the power to ward off or remove evil. The student will remember that use of this kind of water is made in Kalidasa's Sakuntala to remove the sickness of Sakuntala. The water is charged with mantras. **यायावराः **(वर is added to the fre. base of या) 'vagrant mendicants', **पुष्पफलेन** mark the sing. जातिरप्राणिनामिति एकवद्भावः J. M. पुष्पाणिफलानिच. **अर्च्याः **may be construed with यायूजकाः and यायावराः य is a potential termination as also ईय in दर्च्चनीयम् Vide note on लोभनीयं B. supra. Some take या in the sense of ज्ञान and say यातिरत्रज्ञानार्थः। सर्वे गत्यर्थः प्राप्त्यर्थाः ज्ञानार्थाश्चेति न्यायादव्यर्थज्ञानशीलाइत्यर्थः but this sense is not to be accepted since the sense we have given points to one of the conditions of such a life. An ascetic is not to stay for many days at the same place.

 21 **अथ** shows that the company has now arrived at Vishvamitra's penance-grove. **विजयां जयां** these are probably the same as बला and अतिबला two mystic charms or lores which were taught to Rama and his brother by the sage गृहाण द्वे इमे विद्ये बलामतिबलान्तथा। न ते श्रमो जरा बाभ्यां भविता नीगवैकृतम्॥ नच सुप्तं प्रमत्तं वा धर्षयिष्यन्ति नैऋताः। न च ते सदृशो राम वीर्येणान्यो भवष्यति॥ सदेवनरनागेषु लोकेष्विह पुमांस्त्रिषु। नसौभाग्ये नदक्षिण्ये न बुद्धिश्रुतिपौरुषे॥ नोत्तरे प्रतिपत्तव्ये त्वत्तुल्यो वा भविष्यति। एतद्विद्याद्वयं प्राप्य यशश्चाव्ययमाप्स्यसि॥ बलामतिबलां चैव ज्ञानविज्ञानमातरौ। क्षुत्पिपासेचते रामनाव्यर्थं पीडयिष्यतः॥ जयश्च दुर्गकान्तारप्रदेशेष्वटवीषुच। सारतो त्रिषु लोकेषु गमिष्यसि चराघव॥ Rama. cp. R. XI. 9. **अविक्षतात्मा** 'whose soul is undisturbed,' by such passions as anger, hatred &c. 'of  
an unperturbed mind.' A tranquil mind seems to be a condition of one's lore being successful. **अध्यापिपत्**-

3rd Form of the caus. of अधि + इ to study'— 'taught.' Mark that the agent of the verb in the primitive sense is put in the acc. in the causal. एनं in this st. Vide R. 15, 33. **निघातयिष्यन्**— fut. par, of the cau. of निहन् — This form is used to show that the act of killing was to be performed by Rama for the sage and the act was of a future occurrence.

 22 **स्थायुक** ‘firm,' 'steady.' स्थितिकरणशीलं जयावहत्वात् J. M., Bh. उक is a krit ter. showing tendency. लषपतेत्यादिनाउकञ् cp. पातुक. अतएवामोघम्। **अभ्यर्णमहाहवाय** 'before whom a great battle was looming' i. e, before long Rama was to be engaged in a fight with the demons.

 23 **विप्रदर्शम्** (Gerund णमुल्) = विमान् दृष्ट्वा 'on seeing the Brahmanas.' The idea of totality is involved. The राक्षसी was bent upon killing every Brahman that came within her sight. Construe this with कृतघातयत्ना. Bh. proposes another sense. He takes this as an adj. to तं and com. यद्वा विप्रानादर्शोदर्शनं यस्मात्। रामस्य विशेषणमेतद्। एतेन रक्षोभिया पलायमानानां विपाणां पूर्वदर्शनं नासीद्रामागमे तु विप्रदर्शनमिति व्यज्यते। This sense is not good. The first sense gives us an idea of her character. **जिघांसुवेदम् **'having known her desire to kill.' विप्रदर्शजिघांसुवेदमिति कर्मणि 'दृशिविदोः साकव्ये' इतिणमुल् (Vide Apte's Guide). जिघासु desi. adj. of हन. **ताडकाख्याम्** 'Tadaka by name.' She was the daughter of Suketu, wife of Sunda and mother of Maricha. She was changed into a fiend by the sage Agastya whose devotions she had disturbed. She was killed by Rama when she began to disturb the sacrificial rites of Vishvamitra, Rama was first unwilling to bend his bow against a woman but the sage overcame his scruples, see R. XI. 14-20. R. describes this episode as taking place on the way.

 24 **॰स्निग्धसमृद्धशाखम्** the whole is a Bah. Com; हुतश्चासौ धूमकेतुश्च (Kar. Cam.) तस्य शिखाः (Tat. Com.) ताअञ्जनमिव (Kar.) तेनस्निग्वासमृद्धाश्चशाखायम्य (Bah.) ' whose fruit-

laden (समृद्धाः) boughs were besmeared with the pigment like smoke of the blazing fire.' **॰चारुपतत्रिशिश्चम्** (प्राध्यययेनाभिभूतासमुचरन्तीचावीं पतत्रिणांशिञ्जायस्मिन्)' in which the sweetly warbled notes of birds were excelled by the reading' (of the Vedas). We think that the poet in using शिञ्जा to mean 'warbling' has committed a called प्रसिद्धिहतं, शिञ्जा being generally used to mean ' the jingling sound' of anklets. Vide K. P. VII and Cp. कूजितं राजहंसानां नेदं नूपुरशिज्जितम् V. 4. 14.

 25 **विशश्चसे **'relied upon one another.' The Cons. is pas. पक्षिगणाः परस्परं विशश्वसुः **नन्नम्यमाना** 'bending very low' because they were moved by the wind (विलोला). The form is pre. p. atm, of the fre. base of नम्.

 The idea of birds and beasts forgetting their natural antipathy and hatred and of living together in peace and harmony is frequently met with in the description of penance-groves of sages and of reigns of pious and holy kings of antiquity. The great Indian poet, in his 'ऋतुसंहार,' describes this phenomenon to take place in the hot season, (Cp. Rs. I. 13, 14, 15, 16, 18, 20), what wonder then that such a blessed scene is beheld in the penance grove of a sage whose life is one of intense religious enthusiasm and whose soul soars aloft in direct communion with the Supreme Being, above the sordid passions and considerations of this world. The influence of his pure soul is felt even in the lives of the beasts and birds in his vicinity. In fact Peace and Harmony reign supreme. The realisation of the ultimate triumph of what is divine in us over what is earthly is, to most philosophic minds, not a chimera, but a stern reality of the future. This conception is not confined only to the Aryans. The Christians believe that this phenomenon had once taken place in the Garden of Aden before the moral and spiritual fall of Adam and will once more take place when the kingdom of Heaven will have been established on earth.

 26 **अपूपुजन्**— 3rd Form of पूज— received' or 'worshipped,' sc. तौ or क्षितिपालपुत्रौ, the form being both nom. and acc. Cp. R. XI. 23.

 27 **दैत्याभिभूतस्य** 'troubled by the demons.' The student should observe that the earth was more than once troubled and tormented by the demons. When their wicked actions would reach such a high pitch that the earth groaned under their unbearable weight the God Vishnu agreeably with his promise (परित्राणायसाधूनां &c.) would assume human form and destroy them. It appears that the demons delighted in their work of cruelty. They were the sons of दिति a daughter of यक्ष and wife of Kasyapa, his other wife being अदितिः mother of the gods. The demons looked upon the gods with natural hatred and enmity. Cp. the words of satan in the P. L. Bk. I. **तपोधनैः** cp.अस्मान्साधुविचिन्त्यसंयमधनान् S.

 28 **राघवः** 'the descendant of Raghu,' Raghu was the son of Dilipa. He appears to have been named Raghu from ragh or ranch ‘to go,' because his father foresaw that the boy would go to the end of the holy learning as well as of his enemies in battle; cp. R. 3. 21. True to his name, he commenced the conquest of the directions, went over the whole of the then known world, overcame kings in battle, and returned covered with glory and laden with spoils. He performed the Vishvajit sacrifice in which he gave away everything to Brahmanas and made his son Aja successor to the throne. Raghu seems therefore to be the best renowned king of his race and it came to be called by his name. Kalidasa has styled his great, classical poem the Raghuvamsa. **प्रस्तुत**— 2nd per. plu. impera, of प्रस्तु— 'commence.' **तपोमरुद्भिः** 'with the wind in the form of your austerities.' तपास्येवमरुतः Rama speaks of his arrows as being fire; as the fire is inflamed by wind the austerities are spoken of as

being wind, i. e. the deadly effect of the arrows, will be more surely aided by their penances. The fire requires the fuel to burn. The enemies will serve that purpose. Vide note on विप्रवह्नि Can. I. 23. The figure is रूपक and not उपमा. It is evidently wrong to dissolve these words so as to give an उपमा as the Com have done. तपांसि मरुतइव, शरोऽग्निरिवारयः समिन्धनानीवेति J. M. Bh.

 29 **प्रतुष्टुवुः** 'commenced' (perf. of प्रस्तु). **कर्म **'task,' i. e. a sacrifice in this case. **प्रक्लुप्तैः** 'prepared' or 'arranged.' **यज्ञियैः** (यज्ञाय साधवायज्ञियास्तैः) fit to be offered, such as were duly consecrated. **दक्षिण्यदिष्टम्** 'directed by the great sages.' दक्षिण्याः (दक्षिणामर्हन्तीति) those who are worthy of receiving sacrificial gifts, i. e. the great. Munis. **आर्त्विजीनैः** (ऋत्विजः कर्म आर्त्वितदर्हतीति आर्त्विजीनः) "by those fit to officiate as sacrificial priests.' The four chief Ritvijas are (to recite the prayers of the Rigveda); उद्गातृ (to chant the hymns of the Samaveda); अध्वर्युः ('to measure the ground, build the alter, prepare sacrificial vessels, to fetch wood and, water, light the fire, buy the animal and immolate it' and while doing this to repeat the Yajurveda) and ब्रह्मन्. The student is to remember that these were Vedic duties and offices; some of the religious performances now being in disuse, and some of the duties being now performed by one and the same priest. Sometimes as many as sixteen Ritvijas were employed. **चिचिते** (pas. perf. of चित्) ' was known.' **प्रपर्यत् **(while) it was going on.'

 30 **आपिङ्गरुक्षोर्ध्वशिरस्यबालैः** 'whose hair of the head are somewhat tawny, erect and rough.' आपिङ्गारुक्षा ऊर्ध्वाः शिरस्याबालायेषां Bah. Com. आपिङ्ग = ईषत् पिङ्ग 'some-what tawny,' 'reddish.' It is more correct to give this sense to a than which J, M. does. Bh. is correct; रुक्ष 'rough,' dirtied.' This sense is better than given by J M. (सूक्ष्माः); शिरस्यबाल (शिरसिभवाः शिर-

स्याः) 'the hair on the head.' शिरस्य 'being on the head.' It is adj. to बाल. J. M. says that the particular mention of बाल is necessary because other things are found on the head (अन्योऽपि शिरभ्यो भवतिइतिबालग्रहणम्). But we think that the true interpretation lies in the fact that hair are found on other parts of the body. The hair on the head(शिरस्य)are therefore particularised. Bh. says that शिरस्य is mentioned to show that the hair were on the head. This point is discussed in the K. P. where it is laid down that though certain things are invariably associated with certain places, (e. g. कुण्डल always means 'an ornament' of the ear) still we may make particular mention of the words denoting the place to convey the idea of सन्निधानादि eg. कर्णावतंस means 'an ear-ring' worn on the ear. Similarly though बालाः mean hair on the head,'शिरस्य is used to show that the hair were not removed from the head but were on the head; (शिरस्यग्रहणं श्रवणकुण्डालादिवत्तदादिप्रतिपत्त्यर्थम्).

 **शिरालजङ्घैः **(शिराला जङ्घायेप्रातैः) 'whose joints were full of flesh;' ल is a Tad. ter. to show full of;' cp. मांसल **गिरिकूटदघ्नैः **'as high as the mountain summit.' दघ्न and द्वयस are two Tad. ter. showing 'measure,' 'height.' Cp. ऊरुदन्न aud ऊरुद्वयस. **क्षपाटैः** 'demons,' lit ‘night-wanderers.' क्षपायामटन्तीति. अट is a noun from अट्. See note on बोध Can. I. 5. Likewise रात्रीचर.**प्टथुपिङ्गलाक्षैः **mark that अक्षिन् and सक्थिन् change to अक्ष and सक्थ respectively in a Bah. Com; of red and broad eyes. **प्रावृषेण्यैः **(clouds) belonging to the rainy season." The clouds of this time are very dark. The demons were as black as the clouds of this season. **च J.M** says it is पादपूरणार्थं i. e. to make up the metrical foot. This interpretation gives rise to a Padadosa named निरर्थक (K. P. VII). But in order to acquit the poet of this charge we are rather inclined to follow Bh's explanation which is न केवलं चिचिते चानशेचेतिचार्थः। The Alankara is उपमा.

31 **अधिज्यचाप** 'whose bow-string is stretched," अधिरूढाज्यायस्य ज्यामधिरूढोवा. It is necessary to stretch the string when the arrow has to be fitted to the bow to give tension to it which enables the archer to dart the arrow at his aim. **उदञ्चिताक्षः** (उदञ्चिते अक्षिणीयस्य) 'with his eyes uplifted.' This was necessary since the demons had made their appearance in the sky. Vide note on ॰पिङ्गलाक्ष supra. **सन्नतवामजङ्घः** 'with the left thigh completely bent down.' The right thigh though was a little above in position to the left. सन्नतावामजङ्घायस्य. **शुद्धषुः** whose arrows were well-polished or pointed,' and therefore infallible. **अमन्दकर्षी **drawing his bow with force.' The position of an archer is well described in this stanza. Cp. R. XVIII, 51.

 32 **मायाचणम्** ' noted for juggling.' **अस्त्रचुञ्चुः** 'skilled in the use of missiles.' चण and चुञ्चु at the end of certain Com. mean 'noted for.' तेनवित्तश्चुञ्चुप्चरणपविति। **स्थास्नुं '**able to remain' because of his being the leader of the demons. स्नु is a krit ter, showing 'tendency' and applied to such verbs as ग्ला, म्ला, स्था, जि &c. **जगाद **mark that there are two objects to this verb according to चिब्रूशांसू &c. **गद्** is a synonym of ब्रू.

 33 **फलेग्रहीन् '**living on fruit,' i. e. vegetarians. Mark the Com. We have also फलग्रहीन्. **विभवाः** 'riches,' 'provisions;' येषां विभवा शौवस्तिकत्वं न व्रजन्ति ' whose provisions do not last even till tomorrow;' who live from day to day on provisions (fruit &c.) gathered to last for that day. **तेषां दयसे न** 'dost not protect them. तेषां is कर्मणिषष्ठी. Rama emphasises the fact that there was nothing to be proud of in killing those who live on fruits and whose provisions last for the day. It is, on the contrary, proper that such guileless men should be protected.

 34 **वेदवृत्ते** 'for the course of life sanctioned by the

Vedas.' वेदविहितंवृत्तं (भावेक्तः) is a मध्यमपदलोपी Com. The complaint of Maricha was true for his time. The demons or the aborigines of India were an object of hatred and scorn to the refined Aryans who called them Dasyus (black men), slaves &c. Their conquerers therefore gave them no opportunity to enjoy the fruits of the Aryan civilization. The complaint has not lost its truth and force even in this nineteenth century.

 35 **व्यतिस्ते **(3rd per. sing. pre. of व्यत्यस् 2 A to be superior to') 'excels or is superior to.' The duty of protection must be superior to that of killing; the  
former outweighs the latter. **येन** sc. धर्मेण। येन धर्मेणहेतुनाब्रह्मद्विषस्ते (obj. to ) प्रणिहन्मि मारयामिसव्यतिस्त इतियोज्यम् J.M. **राजन्यवृत्तिः '**bred to the profession of a Kshatriya.' As a Kshatriya I am bound to defend the weak and the innocent. (राज्यन्यं वृत्तिर्यस्य) cp. आर्तत्राणाय वः शस्त्रन्नप्रहर्तुमनागसि S.। **धृतकार्मुकेषुः** (धृतङ्कार्मुकन्धृताइषवाश्चयेन) 'the holder of a bow and arrows.' These two are mentioned by Rama as reasons justifying his resolve to kill the Rakshasas. Cp. क्षतात्किलत्रायतइत्युदग्रः क्षत्रस्य शब्दोभुवनेषु रूढः R 2. 53. and Bg. 18. 43. The variant धृतकार्मुकेषु is not good. The one in the text is more appropriate as it gives a reason.

 36 **इत्थं प्रवादं** 'in which such words were spoken.' इत्थमनेनप्रकारेणप्रवादोऽन्योन्याभिघातोयत्र। **युधि** 'on the battle-field,' It is better to understand a battle-field since there was no fight as such. The battle upto this time was one of words. **सम्प्रहारं** 'conflict,' 'striking,' with words. We have thought there was no battle and accordingly we have translated as above. सम्प्रहारं may be taken to mean "a battle' and then the idea is that after a conflict of words real fight began. We have a parallal to this in R. Can. III where Raghu

fights with Indra. तृणयमत्वा 'caring not even a straw for him' (तृणमपिनावमत्य).

 37 **वर्षुका '**a showerer.' It is well-known that gods have often been described as showing their gratification and joy by throwing flowers. Cp. R. अवाङ्मुखस्योपरिपुष्पवृष्टिः पपात विद्याधरहस्तमुक्ता Can. II. 60. **निर्व्याजम्** 'without any impediment.' It is an adverb, निर्गतंव्याजं यथास्यात्तथा.

 38 **घस्मरजित्वरेण** ' by the conqueror of the demons घस्मर is formed from घस् 'to eat' (a substitute of अद् in some forms) by the addition of the krit. ter. मर, (lit) 'gluttonous.' The demons were notorious for their. gluttony, जित्वर from जि + krit ter. वर showing 'tendency.' त् is put in the middle. **वज्रायुधभूषणायाः** 'whose ornament is India.' वज्रायुधः भूषणं यस्याः. Indra is well-known to wield thunderbolt as his weapon. Indra is one of the most distinguished gods of the Vedic period and even in later mythology he has not altogether lost his original high position. The student would do well to get a fuller knowledge of Indra, for which he is strongly recommended to refer to Apte's Prac. Sans. Eng. Dic. It is advantageous to mark how the Vedic gods are made to change or modify their characters in the later accounts of them preserved in the Puranas. **नह्रिणीयते** (denominative Atm.) 'is not excelled or surpassed.' The earth is not a whit inferior to Indra's paradise since she has such warriors like Rama as can compete with Indra. The verb is used with genetive as here or with instrumental. Cp. त्वयाद्य तस्मिन्नपिदण्डधारिणा कथन्नपत्याधरिणीहृणीयते N. 1. 133. We have also हृणीयते.

 39 **बलिः** N. of a celebrated demon. He was a son of Virochana, the son of Prahlada. He was & very powerful demon and oppressed the gods very much. They, therefore, prayed to Vishnu for suc-

cour, who descended on earth as a son of Kasyapa and Aditi in the form of a dwarf (वामनावतारः) He assumed the dress of a mendicant and having gone to Bali requested him to give as much earth as he could cover in three steps. Bali, who was noted for his liberality, unhesitatingly acceded to this apparently simple request. But the dwarf soon assumed a mighty form and began to measure the three steps. The first step covered the earth, the second the heavens, and not knowing where to place the third, he planted it on the head of Bali and sent him and all his legions to the Patala and allowed him to be its ruler. Thus the universe was once more restored to the rule of Indra. Cp छलयसि विक्रमणे बलिमद्भुतवामन Git. I; R. 7. 35; and Me. 57. Vishnu is said to still guard his door in Patala. He is one of the Chirangivins. The verbs are all pas. perfect. **जलधिर्ममन्थे** the churning of the ocean in the कूर्मवतार. second of the ten incarnations. In this avatara Vishnu is said to have assumed the form of a tortoise. The back of the tortoisə served the purpose of supporting the mountain मेरु which was used as the churning handle, the serpent Vasuki being used as the churning string. The result of the churning was the issuing, out of the ocean, of the fourteen jewels embodied in this verse: लक्ष्मीः कौस्तुभपारिजातकसुराधन्वन्तरिश्चन्द्रमाः। गावः कामदुघाः सुरेश्वरगजो रम्भादिदेवाङ्गनाः। अश्वः सप्तमुखोविषं हरिधनुः शङ्खोऽमृतं चाम्बुधे। रत्नानीह चतुर्दश प्रतिदिनं कुर्युः सदा मङ्गलम्॥ **जह्रेऽमृतं** 'the nectar was seized or wrested.' The fourteen jewels thus churned up were then distributed among various persons. Lakshmi was accepted by Vishnu and so on. In the act of distribution Rahu attempted to drink the nectar along with gods but he was detected by the sun and the moon who informed Vishnu of the fraud, Vishnu, thereupon, severed his head from the body and the nectar was then served to the gods. Vishnu had to assume the form of a woman to perform this

wonderful feat. **कल्पान्तदुःस्था** 'badly conditioned at the time of universal destruction.' The universal destruction takes place at the end of a Kalpa or one day of Brahma's consisting of 1000 Yugas being a period of 432 million years of mortals. The earth was being destroyed at this period when Vishṇu in his boar avatara (वराहवतार) rescued it from destruction and bore it up on the tusk. **एष भारः** 'this burden or responsibility' of killing demons, or according to J. M. and Bh. the protection of sages (मुनिजनरक्षणम्). भवति is to be understood.

 40 **मधुरं हितं च '**sweet and salutary.' A speech which is sweet and salutary at the same time is very cp. हितं मनोहारिच दुर्लभं वचः **आञ्जिहत्**— Cau. aor. 3rd Form of अञ्ज 'to go'— took' Rama to Mithila. **मैथिलयज्ञभूमिम्** 'the sacrificial ground of the king of Mithila, i. e. Janaka Mithila was the capital of the country called Videha lying to the northeast of Magadha. Mithila is the same as Janakapura in Nepal, **निजिघृक्षयिष्यन्**— fut. part. of the cau. of the Desi. गृह्— of wishing to have (the fame of the kings) eclipsed or obscured (by Rama). The fut. is used because this was to be done by Rama after his going to Mithila.

 41 **इतः स्म** 'here,' ' to this place' sc. आगतौ. स्म is a पादपूर्णार्थ word. vide note, Can. II 30. Some read सु instead of स्म which is not bad. It must be read along with मित्रावरुणौ as सुमित्रावरुणौ. The adoption of this reading would obviate the fault of निरर्थक. Bh, renders इतःस्म by अमुं देशं. **मित्रावरुणौ** 'Mitra and Varuṇa' Mark the Com. cp. सूर्याचन्द्रमसौ. मित्र is a Vedic deity, name of an Aditya or a sun-god. He is generally associated with Varuṇa. In the 7th Mandala Sukta 61 Mitra and Varuna are jointly addressed hymns to by the Vedic sage Vasistha. वरुण one of the fore-

most gods of the Vedic period. The duties assigned to him are of a superior kind. He is described as the moral and physical ruler of the world. He is thus endowed with all the powers of God. But in later mythology he is deprived of his higher duties and made regent of the ocean and of the western quarters represented with a noose in his hand. The following verse is expressive of the greatness of the Vedic god: त्वं विश्वेषां वरुणासि राजा ये च देवा ये च मर्ताः Rv. 2. 57. Vide also Mad. I Sukta 25, Mad. II. 28. **अश्विनौ **the two physicians of the gods who are represented as the twin sons of the sun by a nymph in the form of a mare. Cp. त्वाष्ट्रीतु सवितुर्भार्या वडवारूपधारिणी। असूयत महाभागा सान्तरीक्षेऽश्विनावुभौ॥ According to vedic conception, however, they are the harbingers of Ushas or the dawn; they are young, beautiful, bright, swift &c.; and according to Yaska, they represent the transition from darkness to light, when the intermingling of both produces that inseparable duality expressed by the twin nature of these deities. According to different interpretations they were heaven and earth,' day and night,' 'two kings, performers of holy acts,' which may be traced to their dual and luminous nature. Mythically they were the parents of Nakula and Sahadeva. They were celebrated for their active benevolence and curative power, Cp. Rv. I. 11,69.184. **सोमरसम्पिपासू**—dual of पिपासु desi. noun from पा—' desirous of drinking soma-juice.' Mark that genetive is prohibited in such cases, i. e. not सोमरसस्यापिपासू, cp. पुष्पचयंवर्षका. 37 *supra*. What this soma-juice was it is now difficult to say. But it was the fond beverage of the ancient Ṛishis and of the gods. It was also the most important ingredient in ancient sacrificial offerings, so much so that a separate Mandala of the Ṛigveda is devoted to the praise and description of this plant. cons. पिपासू with रुणौ and श्विनो though the former are rarely described as fond

of this drink. **औजिहतां **—3rd F. cau. of ऊह—'caused (them) to guess,' 'set (them) to conjecture.' When Rama and his brother came to Mithila, the people were put in doubt as to the personality of them. They thought that either Mitravaruna or the twin-Aswins have come there in person. So imposing was their lustre and beauty. The Alankara is ससन्देह (K P. X). नृसिंहौ vide note कुञ्जरेण I. 20.

 42 **दैत्यपुरं** 'the town of demons.' The chief demon here refered to is त्रिपुर. There were three cities of gold, silver and iron, in the sky, air and earth built for demons by Maya; these cities were burnt down, along with the demons. by Siva at the request of the gods. cp. Ku. 7. 48. **जिज्ञासमानः** (atm. pre. par. from the desi जिज्ञासते of ज्ञा ) ' desirous to ascertain.' **पिनाकी** 'an epithet of Siva, पिनाक being the name of his bow. **हसन्** shows that Rama had no difficulty in breaking it.

 43 **नदीष्णान्** (नदी + स्नान्) lit. bathing in rivers' and therefore clever in crossing rivers, नदीसन्तरणकुशलान्. अ is here the krit ter. before which the final vowel is dropped. cp. ज्ञः, प्रस्थः or उपघ्नः. **पथिकान्** (पथिकुशलान्, इक ter.) 'way-farers' i. e. men able to go on foot to long distances without being tired. आह्नायकान् 'messengers,' 'couriers.'

 The student will see that this description of the marriage of Sita is very meagre and differs much from its popular version. The popular version is that Janaka had vowed to give his daughter to him in marriag who would break the bow of Siva. Here there is no mention of Ravana while we know he was one of the competitors to her hand. This episode is very lively and deserves therefore a detailed descripiton. Kalidasa also does not speak of Ravaṇa. However Cp. R. XI, 32-49.

44 **क्षिप्रम्** adv. to अगच्छत्. **अध्वन्यतुरङ्गयायी** ' driving in a coach of speedy horses' अध्वन्य ' speeding on a journey,' अध्वन्+य (a krit. ter. showing capability) similarly we have अध्वनीन. अध्वनोयत्खावितियत् J. M. अध्वानमंलगामिनो ये तुरङ्गाते अध्वन्याः। अध्वानमत्यर्थं गच्छन्तीति अध्वनिकुशलो वा Bh. यायी— nom. of यायिन् इन् & krit. ter. before which roots in आ (ए, ऐ, ओ ), insert.य्. cp. स्थायिन्. Kielhorn's Gram, p. 245. It denotes an agent. **यविष्ठवत्** ' like a youth,' यविष्ठ super of युवन् **वृद्धतमः**, तम is also a super. term. Vide Kielhorn Chap. IV. **अग्लानयानः **In the translation we have unconciously omitted to give the sense of this word. नविद्यते ग्लानमग्लानम्। अग्लानं यानं यस्य। The king's journey or conveyance gave him no trouble since he had excellent horses. अन forms abstract nouns. The king was, of course, accompanied by his wives and sons and retinue. Cp. R. XI. 51.

 45 **प्रेष्ठं** ' the most beloved' of kings (वसुधाधिपानां), super. of प्रिय. Similarly वृन्दिष्ठं, गरिष्ठं, बंहिष्ठं and वरिष्ठं are super. of वृन्दारक, गुरु, बहुल and उरु respectively. These are adj. to तम् एतं ( who is come) **गुरुवत्** ' like Guru or the preceptor of the gods, otherwise called बृहस्पति; eon. this with गरिष्ठं. **सदृङ्महान्तं** —सदृशां मध्ये महान्तम्— 'highly illustrious among his colleagues.' सदृक् is a conventional word. रूढिशब्दश्चायम्। नात्र दर्शनक्रिया विद्यते। J. M. The com. take सदृक् as a separate word. It is mom, of सदृक् and means अभिजनादिभिस्तुल्यो जनकइत्यर्थः J. M. and सदृक् अर्थाद्दशरथस्यसमानइव दृश्यते योऽसाविति Bh; though the former is not very clear because immediately he proceeds महान्तं महानुभावं सदृशां मध्ये महान्तम्. Bh. also has सदृशानां महान्तमित्यन्ये। We like to join these words to give the sense we have proposed.

 46 **त्रिवर्गपारीणम्** 'who has orossed or went to the other side of three objects of wordly existence,' i.e. who has accomplished the threefold purpose of his

life. The three objects धर्म, अर्थ and काम. ईन् is a Tad. ter. **अध्यासयन्**—pre. par. of cau of अधि + आस्—' causing to occupy.' cp. Can. I. 3. and are its obj. Mark the acc. of भवान् the original agent **विवेकदृश्वत्वं **'discrimination,' 'discretion.' q is a krit. ter. विवेकदृश्वतो भावं विवेकदृश्वत्वम्। cp. पारदृश्वनः R. I. 23. **अगात् **verb to इन्द्रः The idea is that Dasaratha deserved to be on the same seat with Indra and the latter by paying him that honour showed to the world that he could recognise merits in others and reward them.

 47 **हिरण्मयी साललतेव** 'like a Sala creeper resembling gold by its colour.' साल is a tree which is usually very tall and stately. The idea of Sita being very tall and stately may be likely suggested by her comparison to the Sala creeper but her complexion was yellow—a true picture of beauty. To make the comparison complete हिरण्मयी is added to साललता, thus fancying it to be of gold. The best colour or complexion is described by the poets to be yellow. (Cp. Mar.. सुवर्णकेतकीसारखारङ्ग or ....... तानिच कनकलतिकायाम्). एतेन रामस्य सालवृक्षतुल्यत्वं दर्शितं Bh. **स्थास्नुः ** 'standing,' 'permanent.' The lustre of Sita's body was not as fickle and transitory as the flash of lightning which is therefore called अचिरप्रभा 'whose lustre is fleeting or transient.' The lustre is intense, no doubt, but it is short-lived, while the lustre of Sita was as intense as that of the lightning but was permanent. There is व्यतिरेक Alankara, i, e. in which the object of comparison is said to surpass the standard of comparison, (K. P. X). **अधिदेवताकृतिः** 'the presiding deity.' We think that the word आकृति is unnecessary or superfluous and we may, therefore, say that there is the fault of अधिकपद ( K. P. VII ). Cp. सारामणीयकनिधेरधिदेवता वा Mal. I. **मैथिली**—मैथिलस्यापत्यं स्त्रीमैथिली or मिथिलायानगर्याम् अर्थात् मिथिलाख्यभूभागे जाताऽयोनिसम्भवात् पार्थिवीत्यर्थः। अयोनिः

सम्भवत्वेन दिव्यत्वाल्लक्ष्मीवं सूचितं Bh. The student need not be told that Sita was found in a field. Rama's brothers were also married at this time. Metre वंशस्थ.

 48 विश्वजनीनवृत्तिः 'devoted to the good of the universe.' The student will remember that the incarnation of Rama as well as all the other incarnations were intended for the good of the world Cp. भुवनहितच्छलेन Can I. 1. जनीन (जन + ईन a Tad. ter.) जनायहिता. '**भर्मशोभां** adj. to तां 'bearing the splendour of the golden ornaments (भर्म), pearls and jewels.' J. M. construes सत् with शोभा (सतीउत्कृष्टाशोभा), but it is better, to our mind, to connect it with previous words, रत्न &c. भर्मणां शोभा यस्याः सा Vya. Bah. Com. Bh. reads भूषां and com. सद्रत्नानिमुक्ताफलानि भर्माणिभूषा (अलङ्कारः) यस्याः।

 49 **अभ्ययोध्यम्** adv. to अगात्. अयोध्याम्अभि Avya, Com. **हास्तिकाढयम् '**consisting of elephants, princes and horses.'अश्वीय (अश्व + ईय); राजन्यक (राजन्य् + अक), हास्तिक (हस्ति + इक) are formed to denote collections. The compound of these must be treated as singular. एषां सेनाङ्गत्वात् द्वन्द्व एकवद्भावः। J. M. Cp. पुष्पफलेन st. 20 supra. Cp. R. XI. 57.

 50 **विशङ्कटो वक्षसि** 'broad in his chest.' The broadness of the chest is a proof of the strength of man. Cp. Dilipa's description in R. व्युढोरस्को वृषस्कन्धः शालप्रांशुर्महाभुजः &c. I. 13. **सम्पन्नतालद्वयसः** 'as tall as a full-grown palm tree.' This description is evidently hyperbolical, only showing that Parasurama was uncommonly tall. This will put the student in mind of those fanciful people whom Gulliver met in his second journey. Vide note on गिरिकूटदघ्नैः 30 supra. **उपजान्वरत्निः** 'whose arms reached the knees. उपजानु (जानुनोः समीपमुपजानु) 'upto the knee.' अरत्निः 'an arm.'**रामम्ऐैतिस्म** 'encountered Rama' स्म, as added to the present tense gives the idea of the past. **जामदग्न्यः**

(जमदग्नेरपत्यम्पुमान् जामदग्न्यः ) 'the son of Jamadagni, his name being Parasurama, परशु being his weapon. Ac-cording to the *puranic* accounts he was the sixth incarnation of Vishṇu, undertaken to exterpate the warrior caste. While yet young he cut off the head of his mother at the command of his father, when none of his brothers was willing to do it. He defeated the king Kartavirya in a fight for the offence the latter had given by carrying off his father's cow. "The sons of Kartavirya shot Jamadagni dead, when The was alone in his hermitage, in revenge. Parashurama after his return home, determined to exterpate the Kshatriyas and is said to have done this for fourteen times. He was, however, defeated by Rama. He is one of the Chiranjivins. This encounter and fight are beautifully described by Kalidasa which see. R XI. 60-93.

 51 **मातियासीः** 'do not take your way without fighting with me,' i. e. do not disregard my challenge. 'The particle मा, as joined with the aor. gives a prohibitive sense. It is also joined with the Imper. and the Imperf. to give this same sense. The augment is, however, usually dropped. This explains the formation. अतियासीः which, otherwise, should be अत्ययासीः.

 52 **अतार्प्सीत्** vide note on पितॄनपारीत् Can. I. 2. It is imperative to fulfill this duty. The dereliction of this is a sin. Cp. R. I. 66-7. **नृपरक्ततोयैः** 'with water in the form of blood of the kings' (you have destroyed). The पितृयज्ञ or तर्पण as is to be performed with water (तिलाञ्जलि). The purpose of water was in this case served by the blood spilt during the bloody carnage of the kings, in revenge, for the death of his father by Parasurama. **सङ्क्षिप्य**—Imper. 2nd per. sing —'please, set aside your anger (संरम्भम्), **असद्विपक्षम् **—असन्नविद्यमानो विपक्षो यस्मिन् —' which has no enemy' for its.

exercise, since you have conquered them all. **कास्था **(का + आस्था) why should you be anxious to conquer Rama who is still in his teens, a mere boy. Dasaratha urges the boyhood of Rama as a sufficient reason for Parasarama to take no notice of him. To him who had conquered and destroyed even mightier foes Rama was an insignificant enemy, if an enemy he might be called. The use of राम twice to mean परशुराम and राम denotes, according to Bh., रामपदद्वयेन नामसाम्यादपि क्रोधो नोचितइति व्यज्यते।

 53 **व्यकार्क्षीत्**— 4th F. of वि + कृष् —'stretched' (his bow). The force of the preposition is to show completeness; Ruma stretched his bow to its utmost capacity. This denotes his preparation to fight. **लोकान् **It is not quite clear what this word is meant to convey. लोक means 'a world' and accepting this meaning we have to surmise that Parasurama had conquered all the worlds. J. M. means by the luster which Rama destroyed ; तस्यसर्वन्तेजोऽपहृतम्। Bh. has लोकान्स्वर्गान् ‘the heavens', and तत्रगमनं निषिद्धवान्। Both the senses may be adopted so as to agree with Kalidasa's description of the same. Cp. R. XI 81 and 88.

 54 **सुमनीभवन्ति** (plu. of सुमनीभवत् n.') ' with their minds at ease, which were before troubled by Parasurama's challenge to Rama to fight. **अशङ्कम् **adv. to जगाहिरे 'fearlessly.' **अनेकमुखानि** 'separating themselves into various parties. The army had gathered together through fear but when it found that there was no more cause for fear, it again proceeded in groups.

 55 **नेदयत्**—pre. part. cau. of नेद् I. P.—' bringing near **दवयत्** —pre. par. of Den, B. of 3 I P.—making distant,' removing to a distant.' **अचेतत्** 'ignorant' of the distance they had journeyed. **नीरजीकारिताक्ष्मां**

—नीरजीकारिता जलसिक्ताक्ष्माभूतलं यस्याः—'the ground of which was sprinkled with water.' It appears that the practice of watering roads and cleansing them is as old as the time of our poet, if not older. For सुमनी॰ and नीरजी॰ vide Kielhorn's Gram. p. 213 art. 489. This stanza gives a fine picture of marching of great velocity, cp. Sakunta act I.

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

**CANTO III.**

 1 **क्षत्रान्तकस्य '**of the killer of the Kshatriyas,' i. e. परशुराम. क्षत्र 'a warrior of that caste=क्षत्रिय.' Kalidasa gives a fanciful derivation of this word when he says क्षतात्किल त्रायतइत्युदग्रः क्षत्रस्य शब्दः भुवनेषु रुढः। This word occurs in Veda and comes from to bear." A kshatriya is therefore one who ean endure, who has physical strength. In this original sense as said above, it occurs in Rigveda cp. Mal. I, Suk. 25. st. 5. **आढयम्भविष्णुः** becoming eminent,' attaining to greatness.' The nasal is inserted in such compounds. cp. द्विषन्तपः परन्तपः **कुमारः** Rama is called कुमार though he was married since his father was living. In Can II. 53 this epithet is used upon which J. M. पुत्रः पितरि जीवति कुमार इति व्यपदिश्यते। **प्रियम्भविष्णुः** ' becoming an object of affection' of his subjects; winning their love ॰करिष्णु Can I. 19. Cons. and esteem. Vide note on यशसा with आढयम्भविष्णुः। Cons, यस्य न प्रियम्भविष्णुः स नासीदेव सर्वैस्यैव प्रिय इत्यर्थः Bh. एव is taken with नामीत् or चैवशब्दो निपातसमुदायः समुच्चये।

 2 **सुचेतीकृतपौरभृत्यः** 'who has tranquilled the minds of his subjects and servants,' by his good government. On Dasaratha's ascending the throne of his father, the people had misgivings as to the nature of his regime, whether it would prove kind or oppressive.

But by his good government the people were satisfied since during his rule their condition was all they wished for. Vide note on सुमनीभवन्ति Can II. 54. अस् of चेतस् and मनस् is irregularly dropped before thie augment ई. **अभिषेक्ष्ये '**I will crown him as a sovereign.' The ceremony of investing the prince royal with the office of the king was performed by pouring upon his head holy water accompanied by sacred Vedic Mantras. The coronation was then legally sanctioned. The form is Future of अभिषिच्.The hearts of his subjects were over again pacified (सुमनीचकार) by this proclamation. Cp. R. XII 2.

 3 **आदीप्तकृशानुकल्पम्** 'resembling fully-inflamed fire,' in point of lustre. For कल्प see note Can. I. 5. This much lustre was to be imparted to the throne by bedecking it with innumerable jewels &c. **सपादपीठम् **(पादपीठेनसहीतम्) 'with a foot-stool;' i. e. a small tool on which the feet are to rest, while occupying the throne. **सन्तप्तचामीकरवल्गुवज्रम्** ' set with beautiful diamonds and polished gold-plates.' सन्तप्त 'well-polished,' चामीकर 'gold' वल्गु 'beautiful,' वज्रम् ' a diamond.' That the throne was of gold nobody could doubt and moreover it was set with diamonds. We like to differ from J. M. in the explanation of this expression by him. He says that the diamonds which were set therein were of the colour of heated gold (सन्तप्तचामीकरवर्णानि उत्तमसुवर्णवर्णानिवज्त्राणियस्मिन्) and hence the firy lustre. We do not know if the diamonds are yellow like-gold. And in addition to this there can be no reasonable objection to believe that the throne was golden or at least set with gold plates. We therefore prefer to dissolve the expression thus सन्तप्तचामीकरं (॰पत्राणि) वल्गुवज्त्राणि च यस्मिन् which gives the meaning we have proposed, Bh, agrees with us अग्नितुल्यसुवर्णशोभितहीरकम्. **रत्नम्** 'having precious jewels set in the intervals.' The aim in the preparation of the

throne was to give it lustre and beauty and therefore it was set with precious diamonds and jewels,

 4 **पूगकृतान्** 'formed into bands or companies.' **स्वषोषम्पुष्टान्** 'well nourished (and therefore strong) with his own food,' i. e. his attendants, (Vide Apte's. Guide for the form). This sense is decidedly better, as serving an obligation to these men to work for the king, than Bh's which is स्वघोषं यथास्यात्तथापुष्टान् स्वानाञ्ज्ञातीनां षोषनं यत्र क्रियायाम्। He, however, gives our view also. तन्मते स्वेनधनेन पुष्टानित्यर्थः। **प्रयत्नात्** 'with great care,' i. e. paying compliments to these men. It is used as an indeclinable, construed with प्रास्थापयत् 'despatched.' **पत्काषिणः** inured to hard walking,' lit. 'accustomed to give trouble (कषितुं) to their feet (पद्=पाद 'a foot'). पद् is substituted for पाद according to पापिनी or ac to Bh. पद् is a separate word. The ter. shows 'disposition.'

 5 **उक्षान् प्रचक्रुः** 'had (the roads) watered or sprinkled with water. According to J. M. उक्ष is a noun from उक्ष् formed by the ter. अ (अच्) to show 'possession' (अस्त्यर्थे). His com. उक्षणमुक्षा। गुरोश्च हल इत्यकारः। सा विद्यते येषामित्यर्शआदिभ्योऽच्। इजादेश्च गुरुमत इत्यादिना आम्प्रत्यये प्रचक्रुरित्यनुप्रयोगो न घटते कृञ्चानुप्रयुज्यते इत्यनुशब्दस्य व्यवहितनिवृत्त्यर्थत्वात्। Bh. reads उक्षाम्प्रचक्रुः evidently making it the perfect in a which J. M. does not sanction as it appears from his Com. कृ is no doubt used to form this perfect but a preposition cannot be used along with it. It is better to follow J. M. who is a follower of Paṇini. वीञ्जादिव्याम् म्बरक्रन्वाम इति सुत्रेणाम् इतिपञ्चम्यैवेष्टसिद्धौ अनुग्रहण मुपसर्गक्रियाविशेषणव्यवधानेऽपि तदनुप्रयोगज्ञापनार्थमिति रामानन्दाचार्येण व्याख्यातं तेनात्र तेनैवसोपसर्गस्य कृञोऽनुप्रयोगः। क्रमदीश्वरेण तु समादिकृम्बस्तिमिश्चेतिसूत्रं कृत्वा अयमेव श्लोको निदर्शितः। केचित्तु नगरस्य उक्षां सेकं प्रचक्रुः। Bh.

 6 **मातामहावासम्** 'the abode of his grand-father'"-

('mother's father) मातुः पिता मातामहः पितृव्यमातुलेत्यादिना डा (आ for ऋ) महच् (मह for महत्), J. M. This change is irreguler निपातनात्। तस्य आवासः (an abstract noun, अ being a krit ter. The penultimate a takes Vriddhi cp. हारः, त्यागः) **उपेयिवांसम्**—acc. sing of उपेयिवस् pre. par. from the perf. of उप + इ — 'residing' **तत् '**the coronation of Rama, obj. to सोढुं (Inf. of सह) 'to bear.' **बबार** (perf. of वृ to choose) It should be borne in mind that Kekayi had rendered invaluable service to her husband in one of his wars by holding intact, with her hand, the broken axis of his chariot. The king was so pleased with her gallant action that he promised to grant her two boons, which she said, she would ask when necessary. From other accounts we learn that Kekayi was not less rejoiced than Kousalya at the project of installing Rama as heir-apparent. But her wicked nurse Manthara who long. owed a grudge to Rama and saw that an excellent opportunity had come for her revenge, so completely perverted her mistress' mind that she was prepared to ask of the king the two boons he had granted her, on the former occasion, above alluded to. By one of these boons she asked for the installation of her son Bharata (who, it will be seen later on, was deadly opposed to this sinister project) and by the other, the banishment of Rama for fourteen years. However reluctant, Dasaratha had to grant her boons. Cp. R. XII 6. **वनप्रयाणम् '**exile to forest.' J. M. is in favour of a Dative Tat. Com. i e. वनायप्रयाणम्। गत्यर्थकर्मणीत्यादिना चतुर्थी (i e. चतुर्थी is used with a root meaning 'to go' to denote the obj. of place) परत्वात्कृल्लक्षणयाषष्ठ्या भवितव्यमितिचेन्न। पुनर्द्वितीयाग्रहणात्परामपि षष्ठीं बाधित्वा द्वितीयैवयथास्यादिति। यद्येवं द्वितीयेवस्यान्न चतुर्थी। नैषदोषः द्वितीयाग्रहणस्योपलक्षणार्थत्वात्। तथा च वृत्तावुभयमुक्तं ग्रामं गन्ता ग्रामाय गन्तेति। J.
