M. Bh. has वनायवनस्य वा प्रयाणम्।

 7 **कर्णेजपैः** 'by secret traducers,' सप्तमी aluk Tat. Com. It is also written कर्णजपः cp. स्तम्भेरमः। मन्थरादयः Cons. with लोभा. **स्त्रैणेन लघिम्ना** 'by her base feminine nature,' 'on account of baseness or levity of mind natural to woman.' The poet attributes frivolity and lowness of mind to Kekayi, which cannot be denied. But we are not prepared to agree with him if he charge the entire class of women with the fault. Such a reckless charge is made against women by Bhartṛihari, (whose identity with भट्टि is suspected), however justified he may be by the vicious conduct of his wife Cp. अनृतं साहसं माया &c. To be cons. with **विकृतिं नीता' **carried to this change of mind,' 'perverted.' नी is used with various substantives in the sense of 'to reduce or bring a person to any state or condition.' This use is idiomatic, cp. वशन्नी, दुःखन्नी, अस्तन्नी &c. The Alankara is काव्यलिङ्ग an as the first line speaks of the reason of her mental blindness.

 8 **सङ्गिरमाणः** (Atm. pre. part. of सङ्गृ) 'promising' wealth and countries in order to retract her mind from her purpose. **विषादशङ्कुः** 'the dart of disappointment.' Both भरताभिषेक and this are subjects to निचख्ने. She set her heart on the coronation of Bharata and her disappointment in case of the king's refusal, she thought as a dart or wound. J. M's reason for the granting of two boons is सङ्ग्रामात्किल परिश्रान्तमागतं दशरथं केकयी परिचचार which differs from ours. Bli's optional explanation which connects भरताभिषेकः with the mind (मतौ) of Dasaratha is not so good.

 9 **प्रविव्राजयिषुः **(desi. of the cau. of व्रज् with प्र) 'wishing to send' to the forest. **अभिगमं वनाय **shows that in the dissolution of वनप्रयाण in St. 6, dative is preferable. Some trans. as वनं गन्तुं. **नुचरस्य **'accompanied by Soumitri and Sita.' सौमित्रि is put

first to show respect, अभ्यर्हितत्वात्पूर्वनिपातः। अनुचरतीत्यनुचरः। अ (टः) is a krit ter applied to सेना, भिक्षा &c. अनुचरश्चानुचरी च। पुमान् स्त्रिया। अनुचर is a एकशेषद्वन्द्व like पितरौ, माताच पिताचपितरौ; हंसौ, हंसश्चहंसी हंसौ &c. तावनुचरौ सौमित्रिसीतेऽनुचरौ यस्य। Bh. suggests another dissolution सौमित्रिसीताभ्यामनुचर्यतेयः। Bh's reason of putting सौमित्रि first is प्राग्भावस्य विवक्षाधीनत्वात् सौमित्रेः प्राग्भावः। He gives also the reason we have given above. तन्मते सदा सहचरत्वेन सौमित्रेरभ्यर्हितत्वम्। **सुमन्त्रनेत्रेण** 'whose eye was Sumantra.' Sumantra was the charioteer of Dasaratha. It is easy to mark the appropriateness of this designation (नेत्र) to him when we see that the word is derived from नी 'to carry.' The duty of the charioteer is to carry the chariot and he can therefore be called figuratively the eye of the chariot. नेत्र is taken in the literal sense of नेता by Bh.

 10 **अप्रशान्तम्** (lit) ' one whose passions were not satisfied,' and therefore as the Com, say ' uxorious, 'वृद्धभावेऽपिस्त्रीवशम्। Mark the works केचित् and केचन. चित् चन, अपि, चिदपि or स्वित् applied to किम् gives the latter an indefinite sense. **माया** 'fraud,' 'deplomatic feat.' Some thought that Bharata was at the bottom of all this mischief, मातरमेवराज्यलोभाय नियुज्यस्वदोषहरणार्थं मातामहगृहं गतवानितिमायार्थः Bh. **धिक्केकयी** 'fie upon Kekayi' or 'woe to her.' धिक् is usually used with ace. धिक्ताञ्च तञ्चमदनञ्च &c., but sometimes with nom., voc., and gen. also; धिङ् मूर्ख, धिगर्धाः कष्टसंश्रयाः, धिगस्तु हृदयस्यास्य &c. The verbs are all Perf. Bh. defends the poet against a charge (दोष) of 'breaking natural order' (प्रक्रमभङ्ग K. P. VII) which some may attribute to him for first speaking of a large number (केचित्) and lastly of a few (अपरः). We should first speak of a small class, then of a large and so on. His Com. is अपर इत्यत्रैकवचनादल्प एव लोकः केकयीं निन्दति बहवस्तु राजानम्। केकय्याः स्त्रीत्वेन स्वभावतो मन्दबुद्धित्वं नृपस्य तु तथाविधस्यापि स्त्रीवचनान्मतिभ्रंश इतिमहान्दोष इतिव्यज्यते। तेन प्रक्रमभङ्गोऽत्र न दोषावहः।

 11 **श्वोभविता '**would be going' The future action is spoken of as past because it was sure to take place. It might be taken as done. गतइतिभूतकालः श्वोभवितेति भविष्यत्कालेन सम्बध्यमानः साधुः। धातुसम्बन्धे प्रत्यया इति। J.M.; Bh. **देह**—3rd per, sing atm. perf. of burnt with grief. **अतिमात्रम्**—अतिक्रान्ता मात्रा, अतिशयितामात्राप्रमाणं यथास्यात्तथा—'excessively.'

 12 **प्रस्थास्यमानौ** —fut. par. from प्रस्था—' about to set out,' thus showing that the action was soon to begin **उपसेदुषः**—acc. plu. of उपसोदेवस् from the perf, of उपसद्—'who have approached them.' Cons. मानौ तौ दुषः मानांस्तानिदमूचतुः। **शोशुच्यमानान्** — aec. plu. of. the atm. par. adj. from the freq. base of शुच् —'weeping incessantly.' **अभ्युदये '**in our prosperity' 'in our good fortune.' Rama means that their exile is not an event to be regretted for because thus they have been enabled to show their pure love to their father and give him an apportunity of fulfilling his promises to Kekayi. Instead of lowering them in the estimation of the people this noble conduct of theirs will be an object of universal praise and fame. **नियोगलाभेन** ‘by getting permission' to go. **कृतार्थान्** 'those who have secured the best object of their life.' No object could be more laudable than to have an opportunity of obeying the father's command. Filial duty stands at the head of all duties.

 13 **अपुषत्स्वपोषम्** vide note on st 4 of this Canto **मोक्षः** 'discharge of obligation' **वनस्य** the genetive is thus accounted for by J. M. वनस्येति शेषसामान्ये षष्ठी। कृल्लक्षणायास्तु षष्ठ्या गत्यर्थकर्मणि चतुर्थ्या बाध्यमानत्वात्। See note on वनप्रयाण st. 6 *supra*.

 14 **विद्युत्प्रणाशं प्रनष्टः** 'dead as a flash of lightning,' i.e. just after death. As lightning disappears immediately after its flash, thus life should cease to move

immediately after birth. Besides comparison the cognate sense is given by the gerund. विद्युदिवोत्पत्त्यनन्तरमेव विनाशं गतः। **ऊर्ध्वशोषं विशुष्कः** 'completely dried up or withered away.' The student will mark the magnanimity of Rama's character. He is a unique picture of filial duty. No grander conception of a character so sublime has ever been formed. Mr. Griffith's enconiums upon the Ramayaṇa deserve perusal. See his translation.

 15 **शोकापनुदाः** 'removers or destroyers of his sorrow.' Instead of following me, says Rama, your duty is to go to my father and try to alleviate and remove his sorrow. **भवेत** (potential 2nd per. plu.) be pleased to become,' cons. with शोकापनुदाः. Rama may either entreat the people to do what he wishes they should, or ask them to look to their duty which is to console their beloved king. **मादर्शत** ( = अदर्शत the augment अ being dropped since it is used with मा 2nd per. plu. 2nd Form. दृश् also takes fourth Form), 'do not look upon.'

 16. **इङ्गितैः **‘by their gestures,' suited to betray their internal feelings. Some of the wise men, who would not return even after Rama's importunity, showed by the gesture or motion of their various limbs their intention to follow him at all hazards. Note आकारैरिङ्गितैर्गत्यागृह्यतेऽतर्गतम्मनः Ms. 8. 26 "इङ्गितं हृद्रतो भावो बहिराकार आकृतिः" इतिसज्जनः **गत्वरता**—गवरस्यभावः 'disposition or inclination to go.' **रजनीं** acc. is used because time is meant. कालाध्वनोरितिद्वितीया J. M Cp. द्वादश वर्षाणि न ववर्ष शतक्रतुः। **वनेवासकृतात्** 'showed by the dweller of the forest,' i. e. the lions &c. वनेवास इति सप्तमीतियोगविभागात्समासः। शयवासवासिष्विति विभाषा सप्तम्या अलुक्। J.M. वनेवास is an optional form; we have also वनवास. The Com, is Loc. Aluk. Bh. has स्वमते 'सरसिज' मित्युदाह-

रता क्वचित्समासे विभक्तेरलुगितिसूचितम्। **छलेन** 'under some pretext' सन्ध्यावन्दनादिव्याजेन।

 17 **कवोष्णं न्यश्वसिषुः '**breathed heavily,' 'gave out lukewarm sighs' "कोष्णं कवोष्णं मन्दोष्णं कदुष्णं त्रिषु तद्वति" इत्यमरः The prefix कु here shows 'littleness.' Its various substitutes are कद्, कव, and का. Cp. R. I. 67. **पराङ्मुखैः मनोभिः** This means that though the people returned to Ayodhya after great reluctance and deep sorrow their hearts were away from them. Their hearts were after Rama though physically they returned. This shows their deep love to Rama.

 18 **आत्मानं** obj. to पवित्वा ' purifying himself,' बाह्यमन्तरं च ac. to J.M. This shows that he carried Rama as far as the Ganges, and then was asked to return. **कदुष्णं** vide note on कवोष्ण above. **अधीयन्** 'remenbering (with regret), used with gen. राघवयोः कर्मणिषण्ठी। CP. रामस्य दयमानोऽसावध्योति तव लक्ष्मणः। Can. VIII. 119. अधीयन्त्युपकाराणां.......च। Can. 18. 38. ममैव्यध्येति नृपतिस्तृप्यन्निव जलाञ्जलेः Ki. 11. 74.

 19 **प्रतीय** 'having returned,' gerund of ई. प्रतीय इति ईङ्गतावित्यस्य रूपं, न पुनरिणः (इ 'to go') तस्य हि तुकि प्रतीत्येतिस्यात्। J. M. Bh. षत्वतुकारेसिद्ध इत्येकादेशस्यासिद्धत्वात्। तनागमप्रसङ्गात्। Another reading is प्रतीयुषा (Ins. of प्रतीयिवस्) adj. to जनेन. It gives the same sense. **कृतेव,** the idea expressed by the poet runs thus: Ayodhya is likened to the heaven divested of its sun and moon since Ayodhya was now devoid of Rama and Lakshmaṇa who are compared to the sun and moon respectively. But even when the sky is seen without these two great luminaries there are stars seen in their dim lustre. In order, therefore, to make the comparison complete the petty princes in Ayodhya are likened to the petty stars in the night, राजन्यनक्षत्रसमन्वितापि. Now in the darkness of the night there is a cessation of all activity which was also witnessed in Ayodhya on

account of the darkness of grief, i.e. the people being greatly overpowered with grief had stopped their activity. यथाद्यौर्नक्षत्रसमन्वितापि रात्रौ भानुचन्द्राभ्यो विनाकृता रहिता अन्धकारच्युतसर्वचेष्टातद्वत्सापि भानुचन्द्रस्थानीययो राघवयोर्विरहात्। Bh. J.M. Cp. R. VI. 22. The Alankara is उपमा.

 20 **सत्वात् अच्योष्ट** 'lost his nature,' i. e. consciousness; he became almost mad. स्वभावात् व्यवसायाद्वा अच्योष्ठच्युतः। **च्युताशः** (च्युताआशायस्य) Dasaratha had some hope that Rama would return home at the entreaty of his subjects but all hope was lost when Sumanta came alone. ऐषीत्—5th F. व्यलिपत्—2nd F. and व्यवसिष्ट—5th Form Atm.

 21 **आसिष्ट**—5th Atm F.—'sat' **व्यरंसीत्** — 4th F. of रम्—‘desisted from.' Mark that रम् is Paras. when preceded by वि, आ, परि and उप. Cp. विरमविरम साहसा दमुष्मात्. **कृताकृतेभ्यः **'half-finished.' कृतावयवसम्बन्धात्कृतम् अकृतावयवसम्बन्धादकृतमिति एकार्थत्वात् कर्मधारयः। Bh. lit partly done and partly not done. **क्षितिपालभाग्भ्यः** 'relating to the king or regal,' e.g. दूतप्रेषण &c. भाग्भ्यः is obl. plu. of भाज्. **अगात् द्युनिवासभूयम्** 'went to the state of the dwellers of the heaven or gods,' s. e. the king died. As a good king he is described as going to the godly state after his death. भूयम्=भावम्.

 22 **महिष्यः** 'crowned queens.' 'The king was allowed to marry many wives but only those of his queens, who were crowned with him, were entitled to be called 'the crowned queens' = महिष्यः कृताभिषेकामहिषीतिहैमः कोषः। **विभूषणानि '**neck ornaments,' such as necklaces of pearls, sacred necklace (मङ्गलसूत्र) &c. The verbs are all in the perfect.

 23 **भरतप्रतीक्षा** 'waiting for Bharata.' भरतं प्रतीक्षते, fem. noun from प्रतीक्ष्. **न्यक्षिपत् तैले** It seems that oil was used as a preserver against corruption of the

dead body. Whether it was ordinary oil or some special preparation we are not in a position to determine. This procedure was needful because the corpse would remain in the house till Bharata's arrival which must take some time—a day or two. **आनिनीषून् **'willing or wishing to fetch him.' It was essential to despatch such messengers as would be willing to fetch Bharata. Their aversion to Kekayi must not come in their way. यूनः acc. plu, of युवन्, because they must be able to undergo the troubles of a long journey.

 24 **विवस्वन्तम्** 'the sun.' अधःस्फुरन्तम् 'shooting downwards.' The observation of such phenomena in the dream or in the wakeful condition is considered ominous. A similar remark is made in the मृच्छकटिकनिरीक्षाञ्चक्रे 'saw,' the Perfect is used to show the dreamy state of the mind and its consequent perturbations. This use is confined to the First person. उत्तम विषये सुप्तप्रमत्तावस्थायां चित्तव्याक्षेपात्परोक्षे लिट् J. M. Bh. gives no such limitation स्वमते नियमाभावात्।

 25 **आर्शश्रवन्** —3rd F. of the cau. of शृ— 'caused him to hear,' 'acquainted him with.' **आत्ययिकम्**—अत्ययः नाशः प्रयोजनमस्येति — 'disaster or referring to the disaster.' The messengers did not, as will be seen later on, tell him of his father's death. That was undesirable. But they only said that his father was insensible and wanted to see him पिता ते म्लानस्त्वां द्रष्टुमिच्छतीति आत्ययिकं वचनम्। J. M. इक is the Tad. ter. showing 'purpose.' The first vowel takes Vriddhi. Kalidasa also gives a similar description. According to him the news of the king's death was communicated to Bharata on his arrival, Cp. R. XII. 12 and Malli. thereon, Bh, takes न thus making it a negative assertion which is, however, not good. एत्य 'after having come;' inf. of अ + इ, य being substituted for त्वा as the preposition precedes. See note on प्रतीय

*supra*. **अर्थम्** substantive to आत्ययिकं and along with तं object to the causal अशिश्रवन्. "अर्थोऽभिधेये शब्दानां धनकारणवस्तुषु। प्रयोजने निवृत्तौ च विषयेचप्रयुज्यते”। Bh. आत्ययिकम् अर्थे 'evil news.' राज्ञो मरणं is Bh's meaning which is not good. Instead of अर्थं some read अमुं which is then obj. to **प्रयियासयन्तः** pre. part. of the desi, cau. of प्र + या—'(thus) inducing Bharata to come to Ayodhya. The desire in Bharata to go to Ayodhya was due to the information given by the messengers. **आंहिष्ट**—5th Form of अंह् I Atm. 'to go'—'went.' This root is used in many places in the poem; cp. 46 of this can; Can. 14, 51., 4. 4. in the simple and in 2. 40, 15. 75. in the cau. form. **जाताञ्जिहषः** (जाता अञ्जिहिषा यस्य Bah. Com.) 'with a desire to go' अञ्जिहिषा is noun from the desi, base of अंह्. **उत्कठमानः** 'longing for his elders,' i. e. yearning to see his father and elder brothers. The form is Atm. pre. par. of the Den. of उत्कठ. The Com. give as the meaning of this word and under गुरूणां they include Bharata's grand-father &c. but the meaning J. M. proposes on the strength of अनेकार्थत्वाद्धातूनां is not called for. The usual meaning is highly appropriate as it shows his longing to see his father and brother. It is not therefore necessary to include पितामहादि under गुरूणां. Rama and Lakshmaṇa can very well deserve that epithet. Our meaning is therefore preferrable to that of Com. गुरूणां is कर्मणिषष्ठी. See note on अधीयन् above.

 26 **आसेदुषः** ace. plu. of आसेदिवस् per. par. of आसद् 'meeting with;'
अपायम् आसेदूषः 'meeting with some danger or evil'. To suspect danger to one's relatives is very natural. The flurried state of Bharata's mind is well described in this verse. cp. अतिस्नेहः पापशङ्की. The simultaneous occurrence of the four causes contributed to upset Bharata's mind. He had bad dreams, the king's messengers came to him unexpectedly, his

was an affectionate heart and he was all flurried. The result was his fear about the welfare of his brothers. **गोमायुसारङ्गगणाः** 'herds of deer and jackals.' The going of jackals to the right from the left and that of the deer from the right to the left are held to be ominous, as is their howling and crying. Vide note अभिमतफलशंसी Can. I. 27 and मृच्छकटिक Act IX and not II as is misprinted there. **अरासिषुः** 'howled and cried.' 3rd per. plu. of 5th Form of रस् 'to make sound' and not of रास् which is Atm.

 27 **प्रोषिवान्** 'sent on a journey.' pre. par. of प्र + वस् = प्रोषिवस्. **पणायान्** ac, to J. M. Bh. ‘the gain of the traders' (पणलाभान्). पण means, ac, to them, commercial transaction, पण्यन्त इतिपणाः। नित्यं पणः परिमाण इत्यप् (अ ter. m.) व्यवहर्तव्याः। and अय 'gains,' 'profits,' ईयन्ते प्राप्यन्ते वणिग्भिरित्ययाः लाभाः। Therefore the whole means 'the profits of commercial transaction.' But in our opinion it is not necessary to go so deep. Bharata had no means to see the profits of the traders, nor was this his intention. The expression means (पण 'commerce,' 'trade;' and अयः 'going') 'the going on of the trade, i. e. the transaction of commercial business which was at a stand-still on account of the royal death. Bharata saw on his entry into the town that the shops had been shut and all commerce was therefore in dead-lock. The reading पणायां mentioned by J. M. or पणायाः adopted by Bh. mean the sare and is equally good, क्रयविक्रयव्यवहारान्। You need not take it in its other sense of praising as J. M. does. वणिजां स्तुतिं संव्यवहारविषयाम्। प्रलापान् would also do. This refers to the words of the traders with their customers. Bh, mentions another reading वणिगापणयां which gives the same sense.

 28 **अभ्यर्णम्** 'approaching, drawing near,' (अभि + अर्ण p. p. of अर्द् 'to go'). **पुरोहितामात्यमुखाः** ' headed by the family priest and the ministers of state.'

पुरोहितामात्याः मुखं प्रधानं येषा Bah. Com: Vasistha was the family priest of the solar race. पुरोहित is placed first in the com. to show respect that is due to his personality. अमात्यः = अमा i. e. सह राज्ञा कार्येषु भवतीति. It is not. necessary to suppose only one अमात्य which the Com, do by saying पुरोहितामात्यौ मुखं येषाम्।

 29 **दिदृक्षमाणः **desi. pre. par. of दृश् Atm, 'wishing. to see.' **परितः** 'all round.' Note that अभितः or परितः is usually used with a noun in the acc; but sometimes it is used by itself as in the present case. **रोरुद्यमानः **pre. par. from the freq. base of रुद्, 'weeping hard.'

 30 **॰विभङ्गः** with a fierce contraction of his eyebrows,' आबद्ध p. p. of आबन्ध् ‘formed.' भ्रुकुटी (or भ्रुकुटिः and भ्रूकुटी-टिः) 'contraction or bending or knitting of the eye-brows,' i. e. frowns. The usual phrase is भ्रूकुटिम्बन्ध or रच् 'to knit the eye-brows,' to frown.' This is indicative of excessive anger. cp. भ्रुविभङ्गकुटिलं च वीक्षितं R, 19. 17. **॰रौद्रनेत्रः** (शेश्वीयमान् Atm. pre. par. of the fre, base of श्वि 'to swell') 'with his red and terrible eyes swollen.' Bharata was overpowered by the two feelings of anger and distress of which the redness, fierceness are highly indicative. The poet is very happy here in expressing the भाव by means of the अनुभाव. The effects of a feeling give us knowledge of the feeling itself. **मुहुः** The Com. take it with उपालब्ध. This is far-fetched and therefore naturally goes with न्यमाङ्क्षीत्—4th Form of निमस्ज्—, though thus there are two adverbs construed with not much differing in sense. We shall, however, try to give sense to both and translate 'repeatedly and continuously. The weeping was not only repeated but it was continuous.

 31 **शोच्याः** 'deplorable'. We are indeed deplorable, i. e. our condition is highly deplorable and pitiable. The reading शङ्क्याः is more direct and gives

good sense. Bharata means that he would be suspected of being an accomplice, in this most wicked deed. But शोच्याः makes his position more clear. He says not only would he be suspected of being a party to this but this would make his position deplorable. The subjects will hate him on that account and call him a regicide and a parricide **लघुत्व** see note on लविग्ना st. 7 above. **केकय्युपज्ञम्** adj. to लघुत्वं, ' known to-Kekayi,' i e. Kekayi alone had thought of this mean project; nobody had knowledge of this. The student will remember that Kekayi was not the first to conceive this plot; she was allured by the machinations of her attendants (vide st. 7). But Bharata, being altogether ignorant of this, says that she alone was the originator of it.

 32 मत्कम् 'belonging to me or mine.' This plot does not proceed from me, I am not its instigator, **उद्वाश्यमान** 'calling loudly,' atm. pre. par. of उद्वाश् 4th conj. Mark the cognate use शपथानशप्यत्.

 33 **सुस्थयन्तः **(deno, base) 'consoling or pacifying. **दिधक्षयन्तः** (cau, desi of दह् 'to burn') inducing Bharata to burn his father.' After the pacification of his sorrow Bharata was willing or wished to immolate his father and the ministers induced him to do it. **समुदूहुः **perf. 3rd per. plu. of समुद् + वह्, 'bore or carried.' **अन्त्याहुतिं** 'the last oblations, i, e. the oblation that is offered to the dead at the time of burning. It is otherwise called तिलाञ्जलिः as sesamum seads are offered. **हावयितुं** (cau inf.) 'to offer.' There is no particular reason for a causal form, because even the ministers were free to offer the last oblation. **चिचीषयन्तः '**setting to work those who were willing to gather' Such derivative bases are rarely used in the classic books, except to illustrate a possible grammatical

form. **अध्वरपात्रजातम्** 'a collection of sacrificial requisites, in this case sacrificial ladles (दर्भ) and many other things such as sesamum seeds &e.

 34 **उदक्षिपन्** — Imperf. 3rd plu of उत्क्षिप्— 'raised', 'lifted.' We are to understand as the subjects of these several verbs, those who were appointed to these duties वेणुमृदङ्गकांस्यम् 'flutes, tabors and cymbals.' Note that the com, is singular to show the same kind. All these musical instruments form one species and as such are regarded as one kind, अप्राणिनां जातिः The singular is used not because these instruments are the limbs or parts of the kind. In that case द्विगु is possible when a प्राणिन् is compounded with one of these; cp. मार्देगिकपाणविकम्। अप्राणिजातित्वात्समाहार इति कालापाः तूर्योगत्वादिति वासवताः। सर्वो द्वन्द्वःसमाहार इतिप्राञ्चः। रवमते (Bh. view) इतरेतरयोगे च समाहारे चचो द्विधेति सामान्येन द्विविधो द्वन्द्व उक्तः तत्र क्वचिदितरेतरः क्वचित्समाहारोऽभिधाना द्वोधव्यो यदुक्तं कृत्तद्धितसमासानामभिधानं नियामकमिति। **कम्बून्** 'conches or shells, **तारान्** adj. to कम्बन् ‘high,’ denoting their high pitch or sound.

 35 **॰नासम्** the singular is used because these constitute the limbs of the body; प्राण्यं गत्वादेकवद्भावः। Such compounds are always neuter. Bh., as quoted above, does not like this view. He says it is समाहारद्वन्द्वंः। इतरेतरद्वन्द्वंः is also allowed. श्रोत्रेत्यादि प्राण्यङ्गत्वात् द्वन्द्वैकत्वं क्लीवत्वञ्च नित्यं भजत इति परः। स्वमतेऽत्र वेणुमृदङ्गकोस्यमितिवत् समाहारो द्वन्द्वः। इतरेतरोऽपि दुर्निवारः। He quotes one verse to support his view। यथा। ग्रीवाकुक्षिललाटेषु नित्यं खेदः प्रशस्यते। गण्डे चुम्बं ललाटाक्षिकक्षोरुभगमूर्धसु इत्यादि दर्शनात्परमतं हेयम्। Bh. **सरुक्मं** 'with gold,' i. e. pieces of gold were placed on these everal limbs. पात्राणि 'Jadles' &c.

 36 **॰तेषु॰** सञ्चयेषु is an instance of a locative absolute, showing the prior execution of the necessary rites, v. e. after they were offered &c. **प्रत्यानिनीषुः** wishing to bring back The necessity of taking his

subjects with him was to make his request more effective. His importunity together with that of the citizens would be more effective than his own,

 37 **शीघ्रायमाणैः** (atm. pre. par. of Den. of शीघ्र) 'hastening.' **अश्नुवानैः** (atm. pre. par. of अश्) 'реrvading or occupying.' **अपन्थानम् '**not to the end of the road' seems to be the sense intended. The journey was long and Bharata and the citizens were benighted on the way. It was natural, therefore, for them to pass the night on the road and in the morning to resume their journey. Mark that the objective अपन्थानं is used though अपथम् is equally correct; अपथं-थः and अपन्थाः being the two forms in the negative compound. **मिश्रैः **(नागेन्द्ररथाश्वं, the singular should be used as these form the constituent parts of the army), 'accompanied by &.' Bh. allows इतरेतरद्वन्द्वः

 38 **उच्चिक्यिरे**— perf. of चि, also चिच्यिरे, the Atm. is used since the fruit of the action accrues to the agent, — 'gathered,' 'gleaned.' **वनानि** sc. विघटयन्तः 'going through the forests.' **आरेमुः** —रम्. with आ is Paras—Some read आरेटुः, आरेमुः is better.

 39 **तमसापगायाः** 'of the river Tamasa,' आपगा 'a river' अपां समूह आपं तेन गच्छतीति. •**भाजः** 'obtaining purity or purified by her contact with the Gangetic waters.' Here was a confluence of the Tamasa with the Ganges, which imparted purity and holiness to the waters of the former, natural to those of the latter. यस्याः स्मरणात्पापं ताम्यतिसातमसा (J. M.) appears to be a fanciful derivation. Some read तरसा which evidently modifies सम्प्राप्य. तत्र तरसा वेगेन आपगाया अर्थात्तमसायाः ...... कूलं सम्प्राप्य। But तमसा is a better reading as it helps us to know the name of the river. **यामुनं**—यमुनाया इदं — 'of the river Yamuna.' **निरुद्धश्रमवृत्तयः** 'whose propensity to exhaustion has been restrained,' i. e, whose fa-

tigues were at an end on account of the rest they enjoyed, as described in the last stanza. **पुण्यं**—पुण्यहेतुत्वात्पुण्ययुक्तत्वाद्रा J. M. The student can do well to mark the course of the journey of Bharata with his followers.

 40 **यस्मिन्** Mark that तं is not used since its correlative यस्मिन् follows. See note on येन Can. I. 22 above. **च्युताशनायः** 'whose hunger was satisfied,' च्युता अशनाया यस्या। अशनाया is a fem. noun from the Den. of अश्। अशनमिच्छति अशन क्यच् (Den. य) स्त्रियां भावे अ। **फलवद्विभूत्या** 'with the abundance of fruit trees.' In the forest Rama would satisfy his hunger with the fruits, of the trees which thrived in abundance thereiu, **व्यस्यन्** pre, par, of वि + अस् 4th Conj., 'removing,' 'satisfying.' **उदन्यां** fem. noun, derived like अशनाया, from the Den, base उदन्यति.

 41 **वाचंयमान्** 'who restrain their speech. 'वाचं यच्छन्तियमयन्तिवा। The nasal is retained. See note on परन्तप Can. I. 1. Restraint of speech is one of the conditions of the life of a योगी. Sometimes complete silence is observed. Cp. R. 13. 43. There are eight means of attaining Yoga यमनियमासनप्राणायामप्रत्याहारधारणाध्यानसमाधयोऽष्टावङ्गानि। **स्थण्डिलशायिनः** 'sleeping on the sacrificial ground. **युयुक्षमाणान्**—atm. pre. par. from the desi. युयुक्षते of युज्— 'wishing to practice Yoga.' Yoga, in its simplest idea, is the concentration of the mind on the Supreme Spirit, to be united with whom is, accoording to the Vedantins, final beatitude. The Yoga Philosophy which exclusively treats of this. lays down elaborate rules to effect this union Two modes were in vogue: राजयोग and हठयोग which is: more particularly concerned with self-mortification. Read Swami Vivekananda's Lectures on Yoga Philosophy.

 42 **परिनिर्विवप्सोः** 'of him who was desirous to ef-

fect. (Desi. adj.) **योगबलेन **'on account of his supernatural powers'. It is believed that the practice of Yoga confers supernatural powers on the practiser. He can command nature, can assume various forms &c. The supernatural powers of Siva, which the practiser of Yoga can also acquire, are said to be eight; अणिमा गरिमा प्राप्तिः प्राकाम्यं महिमातथा। ईशित्वं च वशित्वं च तथा कामातसायिता॥ In the *S'a'kuntala* and the *Ma'lati-Ma'dhava* the student will find such instances. **धामप्रथिम्नः **'of him who was great by his lustre, धाम्ना तेजसापृथुत्वं यस्य प्रथिमन्—पृथोर्भावः प्रथिमन्' इमन् is a Tad. ter. showing 'state.’ स्रोदमान्वितानि ‘very roft' मृदोर्भावः (vide above) **द्राघिमवन्ति **"very long,' दीर्घस्यभावः प्रथिम्नः is ablative ac, to Bh thus making it a reason of the trees giving out clothes &c. But it is better to make it an adj, to मुनि since योगबलेन serves that purpose.

 43 **सरागम्** 'with musical harmony or melody.' The singing was scientific. There are six primary. *ra'gas*, भैरवः कौशिकश्चैव हिन्दालो दीपकस्तथा। श्रीरागो मेघरागश्च रागाः षडिति कीर्तिताः॥ Each *ra'ga* has six raginis regarded as its consorts, and their union gives rise to several musical notes. The form is adverbial. **सहावम् **'with feminine coquettish gestures.' These gestures are calculated to excite amorous sensations, 'dalliance of love.' हाव it thus defined by उज्ज्वलमणिः— ग्रीवारेचक्रसंयुक्तो भ्रूनेत्रार्दिविकासकृत्। भावादीषत्प्रकाशो यः सहाव इति कथ्यते॥ vide साहित्यदर्पण 117. also. हाव forms a part of नृत्तं (vide Can. II. 16).

 **तिलोत्तमा '**N. of an Apsaras.' It appears from this description that the Ṛishi could command even the courtesans of Indra's court. The verbs are all in the Perfect.

 45 **समध्वा** (सङ्गता अध्वनइति) 'travelling in company. **रथवाजिनागैः '**with chariots, horses and elephants.' As

the form is plural it is necessary to dissolve it as given by J. M. रथवाजितेन- सहितानागास्तैः coming under the class of compounds like शाकपार्थिवः. Otherwise the Com. must be singular as the three form the components of the army. Bh. differs as usual. It is इतरेतरद्वन्द्व ac. to him. **रजनीं** is acc. of time. **मन्दाकिनीं** It is not easy to determine which river is meant to be designated, J. M. gives no particular information on this point. Bh. has चित्रकूटवर्त्मनि नदीविशेषो नर्मदेति प्रसिद्धा। गङ्गामात्रे मन्दाकिनीति केचित्। In the रघुवंश a description of this river occurs, ....मन्दाकिनी भाति नगोपकण्ठे मुक्तावली कण्ठगतेव भूमेः॥ Can. 13. 48, whereon Malli, has मन्दाकिनी नाम काचिच्चित्रकूटनिकटगा सरित्। evidently meaning not the great Ganges. We are inclined to believe that मन्दाकिनी is a river different from the great Ganges though, no doubt, it forms a tributary of the latter. This river appears from the description here and in R. to take its rise in the Chitrakuta mountain which is a hill near Prayaga or modern Allahabad. Kalidasa even intended a different river to be understood since in the same Can, he gives a very beautiful description of the Ganges (vide Can. 13. 54-57), thus distinguishing Mandakini from the Ganges.

 46 **वैखानसेभ्यः** 'from the hermits.' These are वानप्रस्थ i.e. the third stage is reached by them. **॰सङ्घम् **(विशिञ्जानां पतत्रिणां सङ्घ यस्मिन्) 'on which there are numerous birds sweetly warbling,' see note on ॰शिञ्जम् Con. 11. 24. विशिञ्जान is atm. pre. par. **अभ्रंलिहाग्रम्** (अभ्रंलीद्वि अग्राणि यस्य Bah. Com.), 'whose summits touch the clouds.' See note on परन्तप I. I. **अद्रिं** the acc. is used because the preposition प्रति governs an acc. Great mountains are described to obstruct the sun's path by their lofty summits, though Chitrakuta could not be so high.

 47 **वितत्य** inf. of वितन्, पिनह्य inf. of अपि + नह, the अ

of अपि is optionally dropped in the case of नह्, धा; cf अतिपिनन्द्धन वल्कलेन S. I. सौमित्रिः (सुमित्राया अपत्यं पुमान्) 'the son of Sumitra,' i. e. Lakshmaṇa who prepared himself to fight when he observed a large army. coming, which belonged, as we know, to Bharata, and was therefore friendly but which he took for some hostile army. **अक्षिभ्रुवम्** (अक्षिणीचभ्रुवौच) this is irregular.

 48 **समन्यून्** 'sorrowful.' This word, as remarked before, is frequently used in this sense by the poet. **दाशरथिः** the son of Dasaratha,' s. e. Lakshmaṇa who first thought them to be enemical hosts.

 49 **समूलकाषं चकषुः** 'scratched (the earth) completely, sc. भूमेरधोभागम् ac. to J. M or रामान्तिकं रामसमीपदेशं ac. to Bh. It is better to follow J. M. since the sense 'into the presence' of Rama shows that they had approached him which intensified their grief. The object to the verb चकषुः can be easily understood. Mark the Sandhi चकषूरुदन्तः। रामान्तिकं can be construed with ॰वेगाः They were crying but their lamentations increased in the presence of Rama. समूलकाप्रं is a gerund in अम् and gives the idea of 'thoroughness. We have also निमूलकाषं कप्रति. Ac to Bh. it is adverbial to चकषुः, समूलस्य साधोभागस्य काषः पेषणं यस्मादिति कषणक्रियाविशेषणम्। समूलघातवत् चणम् (gerund) वा। For what purpose they scratched the earth is not clearly expressed but it appears that the scratching of the earth is a sign of overwhelming grief. J. M's explanation of the gerund, ac. to Bh, makes it a prior action केचित्तु समूलं भूमेरधोभागमपि कषित्वा पुनः पिष्टवन्त इति व्याख्याय चणमन्तस्य पूर्वकालवमाहुः। अन्येतुणमन्तस्यात्र पृथगर्थाभाव माहुः (the gerund has no separate sense) तेन समूलकाषं चकषुः समूलं चकषुरित्यर्थः।

 50 **गोत्राभिधायं** We inadvertently read गोत्राभिधायां in giving the translation in the text, thus making it a river by name Gotra to be identified with modern

Gogra but as all the copies read गोत्राभिधायं we change our meaning and translate: 'with a mention of the family' गोत्राभिधायं यथास्यान्तथा प्रत्तम्। The oblations were offered with a mention of the family, i. e. with some appearance of ritualism. **द्व्यञ्जलम्** (द्वौअज्जली जलं विगृह्य.) 'with two cavities of water.' Rama and Lakshmaṇa each gave a cavity-full of water to their dead father as oblation.

 52 **वृद्धमतेषु** serves the purpose of the acc. = वृद्धमतान्. It is therefore कर्मणिसप्तमी 'the precepts of the old' i. e. learned precepts. You have heard what the precepts of the wise are and you have moreover acted up to them.

 53 **जहीहि '**give up or abandon,' 2nd per. sing. Impera. of हा, other forms are जहाहि and जहिहि. **शाधि **2nd Impera of शास्.

 54 **वृद्धौरसां **'for which there is an elder heir' औरसः a legitimate son,' (उरसानिर्मितः). Cp. R. 12. 16, **धर्म्यम्** sc. वचनं प्राह।

 56 Mark the change of the metre. It is मालिनी. Bharata after taking the sandals of Rama did not go to Ayodhya but living at Nandigrama he ruled for his brother. Cp. R. 12. 16.

**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

**CANTO IV.**

 1 **धीमान् '**prudent or wise.' Rama thought it desirable to shift his residence lest Bharata would once more come back. In this he showed his prudence. **प्रपेदे** 'reached,' 'went to' (Perfect of प्रपद्). **दण्डकारण्यम् '**the forest named Dandaka.' It is the name of situated between a celebrated district in the Deccan the rivers Narmada and Godavari. In the time of

Rama this vast district appears to be untevanted except by a few sages who loved such solitude. The commentator cites a mythical story which gives the origin of the forest. According to him, there was a king of the Bhoja family, by name Daṇdakya who carried off the daughter of the sage Bhargava. By virtue of the latter's curse the king was destroyed with his relatives and kingdom and the devastated country was changed into a forest.

 2 **अरण्यानीं** 'a large forest.' हिम and अरण्य form their feminines हिमानी and अरण्यानी respectively; greatness is to be indicated. अटाट्यमानः 'roaming frequently,' pre. par. of the fre. of अट्. **भीमेनरक्षसा '**by a terrible demon.' The name of this demon was Viradha, who had been originally a Gandharva by name तम्बुरु but who was transformed into this form of a demon through the curse of the sage Vaisravana, According to R. it was Sita who was uplifted by the demon, Cp. R. 12. 29.

 3 **अवाक् शिरसम्** (अवाक् अधः शिरो यस्य) ' with his head downwards.' **उत्पादम्** (उद्गतौ पादौ यस्य) 'with his feet uplifted.' **दुर्दमम्** difficult to be chastised.'

 4 **रघुव्याघ्रौ '**the tiger-like descendants of Raghu.' This comparison is meant to express their great strength. Vide Verse 20 Canto I. **शरभङ्गाश्रमम् **the hermitage of the sage Sarabhanga. This sage was well-known for his terrible austerities and offered his body, as is related in the next verse, to the fire. A similar description occurs in Kalidasa's Raghuvamsa Can. 13, Verse 45; अदः शरण्यं शरभङ्गनाम्नस्तपोवनं पावनमाहिताग्नेः चिरायसन्तर्प्य समिद्धिरग्निं यो मन्त्रपूतां तनु मष्यहीषीत्॥ **बाह्या '**belonging to the Brahmana, i. e. to the sage. This lustre (श्रीः) was due to his vedic knowledge and great Penance; (ब्रह्मणइदम्). **शरण्यम्** 'a place of refuge' (शरणे साधु) 'which offers protection to all' as if it were a

sanctuary; for the use of this word Cp. the verse quoted above and असौ शरण्यं शरणोन्तुरवानाम् R. 6. 21.

 5 **सुतीक्ष्णमुनिकेतनम्** 'the abode of the sage Sutikshaṇa.' The Raghuvamsa their describes the sage: —हविर्भुजामेधवतां चतुर्णामध्ये ललाटन्तपसप्तसप्तिः॥ असौ तपश्यत्य परस्तपस्वी नाम्नासुतीक्ष्णश्चरितेनदान्तः 41 Canto XIII; vide 42 verse also.

 6 **समैष्यथ** 'shall come' (Future 2nd pla. of इ 'to go'). **इति** = इति हेतोः 'with this object in view.' **आसिष्महि **(5th V. Atm. 1st pers. plur.) have resided.' **वः** 'to you' Remember that स्वस्ति and नमः govern the dative of the noun.

 7 **कृशानुसाद्भूते **'reduced to ashes;' an instance of the locative absolute **उवास** (perfect 3rd Sing of वम्) 'dwelt.' It appears that Rama, on his approach here, prepares for him a permanent abode, where to live during the days of his exile. **आश्रमान्** sc. मुनीनाम्.

 8 **वासतेयेषु** 'habitable' (वसतौ साधु = वासतेय ' fit for habitation'). **पर्णसंस्तरः** 'whose bed is of leaves,' (lit leaves are whose bed, पर्णानिसंस्तरो यस्य. **शय्योत्थायम्** 'having risen from his bed;' उत्थायम् is a gerund (णमुल्) in अम्. Mark the words अतिथेय, वासतेय, पाथेय.

 9 **सामन्यान्** 'well-versed in the Sama Veda;' (सामसुसाधुः). **देवसात्कृत्वा **‘(first) offering a part of it to the Gods.' This is what is called देवयज्ञ or sacrifice in honour of the Gods. Vide the first few verses of the Canto I for the number of such sacrifices enjoined as religious duty. **शूल्यमुख्यं** 'flesh.' It is so called because it is roasted on a spit; (शूले संस्कृतं). Cp. शूल्यमांसभूविष्ठ आहारोऽश्यते S. 2; therefore best roasted meat.'

 10-11 These two verses are explained together because they form one idea and one grammatical sentence. This is called a युस्मकम् i. e. a pair of stanzas

forming one grammatical sentence; (द्वाभ्यां युग्ममितिप्रोक्तम्). **वसानः** 'wearing, pres parti. Atm of वस्, आन and मान being the two terminations used to form such present participles. **तन्त्रकनिभे '**resembling a new garment;' तन्त्रक 'garment' this is new and unbleached, freshly taken from the loom. निभ, at the end of a compound, involves a comparison, Cp. उद्बुद्धमुग्धकनकाब्जनिभं वहन्ती Mal. 1. 40; also चन्द्रनिभानना. **काण्डीरः** — खाङ्गिकः —शाङ्गीं. These words are formed by the addition of the Tad. (तद्वित) terminations ईर (ईरच्), इक (ठन्) and इन् (इनि) respectively showing 'possession,' as has been elsewhere stated. **तनुत्रवान्** (तनुत्र + वान्) 'bearing an armour. The armour is तनुत्र because it protects the body against hostile attacks.

 11 **आशितङ्गवीनानि** (आशिता अशनेन तृप्ता गावोयत्र, गवीन is from गो + इन a Tad termination as is महाकुलीन, the augment is added as in रात्रिञ्चर, स्तनन्धय &c.) formerly grazed by cattle.' viz. forests (अरण्यानि) already grazed by the cattle. **आशितम्भवम्** (आशितोऽनेन तृप्तोभवत्यनेन, the augment being used) 'satisfaction' (of hunger). **दन्तशूकारिः '**the enemy of the demons' vide Can. I verse 26. **आनभ्र** (perfect of अभ्र) 'roamed.'

 12 **व्रातीनव्यालदीप्रास्त्रः** 'whose missile was resplendent against beasts of prey and men living by violence.' **व्रातीन** 'one who lives by violence' like the Thugs of very recent times; व्याल ' a beast of prey' Cp. वनं व्यालनिषेवितं Ram; अनियतद्वृत्तयः शरीरमायास्य ये जीवन्ति ते व्रातास्तेषां यत्कर्म तदपि व्रातं तेन जीवन्तीति व्रातीनाः। J. M., Bh. The com. do not take व्रातीन and व्याल as differenf words. They have ॰तेषाम्मध्ये ये व्याला उपघातका तेषु &c. But it is better to translate as we have done. The forests were inhabited by high-way robbers and beasts of prey. **सुत्वनः **the Commentators translate 'those that drink Somajuice (सुतवतःः) but it appears to me that such men belonged to the Vedic period and therefore this sense

of the word is rather antiquated. We propose, therefore, another meaning 'performers of ablutions' (subsequent or preparatory to a sacrifice). is a krit ter., as in धीवन्, यज्वन् before which the augment त् is inserted. **षर्षद्वलान् **'members of an assembly,' i. e. who live together by forming assemblies. बल is a Tad, ter, showing condition and applied to रजः &c.; रजः कृष्यासुतिपर्षदो बलजिति तदापर्षद्विद्यते। J. M. Therefore we have रजस्वला, कृषीबल, आसुतीबल and पर्षद्बल. पर्षद्, ac. to him, is from पर्षस्नहने अस्मात्पर्षतोस्निह्यतीति, with the ter. अद्. Ac. to Bh. पर्षद् is irregular form of परिषद्, इ of परि being dropped.परिषद्बलान् is his reading also noticed by J.M. which is from परि + सद् (= सीद् ). Cp. परिसदप्येषागुणग्राहिणी S. 1. There is no fault in the metre with this reading. नवाक्षरपादस्यापीष्टत्वान्न चात्र छन्दोभङ्गः। Bh. We have taken महाब्रह्मैः with पर्षद्बलान्, Bh. agrees with us but J. M. takes it with आट, तैः सहाट which is however not good since we cannot expect Brahmanas with Rama. Some take महाब्रह्मैः to mean महातपोभिरुपलक्षितान् for the reason noticed in st. 4 Can. I but it appears that this rule is not uniformly followed. **नैकटिकाश्रमान्** 'the hermitages of the ascetics.' नैकटिक (the form is to be derived from निकट and the Tad, termination इक before which the first vowel undergoes Vṛiddhi) is (lit) one who lives near.' An ascetic or Bhikshu is enjoined by scripture to fix his abode two miles distant from the village. ग्रामस्यान्तिके क्रोशमात्रं तक्त्वायतयो भिक्षवो ये निवसन्ति ते नैकटिकाः J.M.

 13-14 These two verses also form what is called युग्मक i. e, a pair of verses giving connected sense. They are therefore a syntactical whole. **प्रियभावुकतां-आगात् '**earned the favour of' (Vide stanza 1 Canto iii for प्रियम्भविष्णुः). Com. पूर्वं प्रियाप्रियस्वभावनिर्मुक्तत्वादतथाभूतः सन् प्रियो भवतीति प्रियम्भावुकः **वृद्धिक्षयौ** 'prosperity and adversity' obj. to चिन्तयन्. Rama always looked to their prosperity and prohibited their destruction.

 14 **आतिष्ठद्गु **(तिष्ठन्तिगावोयस्मिन्कालेतमनतिक्रभ्य) 'upto the time when cows stand to be milked,' i. e. after an hour or an hour and a half after evening. गावोहि रात्रीप्रथमयामस्य नाडिकाया (= घटिका or 24 minutes) मतीतायां विश्रान्ताः सत्य उत्थाप्य दुह्यन्ते. J. M. गो is changed to गु. **सन्ध्यां** (सम्यग्ध्यायन्ति अस्यामिति) 'twilight adoration.' **प्रक्रान्तां** 'begun,' ‘commenced;' construed with आयतीगवम्. **आयतीगवम्** 'at the time when cows return' (आयत्यः आयान्त्यो भवन्ति यस्मिन्काले गावोऽस्मिन्नायतीगवं J. M., Bh.) Cows return home at the time of twilight. Com. गावोऽपि गोचराद्गोष्टमायान्ति दिवसस्यार्धनाडिकावशेषे सन्ध्यापितदैव प्रवर्तते. J. M. It is adverbial. **प्रातस्तरां पतत्रिभ्यः** 'earlier at the dawn than birds.' Birds are known to rise at the time of dawn but Rama left his bed earlier than the birds even. तरां is the termination of comparison applied to verbs and indeclinables. The usual form applied to adjectives is तर.

 15 **ददृशे** (pas. perfect of दृश् ) 'was seen.' **अभीकया '**lustful,' ‘libidinous' cp. अपिसिञ्चेः कृशा नौ त्वं दर्पं मय्यपि अभिकः Can. 8, 92. अभीक is also अभिक. It is an irregular form, (निपातोऽयं ). A similar form is अनुक (अनुकामयते इति अनुकः). **भार्योढं** (ऊढाभार्या यस्य) 'who had taken a wife.' ऊढं is here placed after भार्या optionally. ep. अग्न्याहित or आहिताग्निः We may therefore also write ऊढभार्यम्; ऊढ p. p. of वह. **असकौ** = असौ ‘this or that'. This form is expressive of contempt. **तस्थे** (atm. perfect of स्था ) 'stood' before him disclosing her desire for intercourse. स्वाभिप्रायं मैथुनायाविष्कृतवती. J. M., स्वस्थित्या मैथुनाभिप्रायं प्रकाशयामास Bh. स्था, in the atm has this sense. It is then used with Dative. प्रकाशनस्थेयाख्ययोश्चेतिप्रकाशने तङ् (Atm); प्रतिज्ञानिर्णयप्रकाश इतिमं (Atm ) J. M. Bh. यस्मै दित्सेत्यादिना चतुर्थी। Cp. गोपी स्मरात्कृष्णाय तिष्ठते Sk.

 16 **बलीभं** 'full of wrinkles' (= वलिभ, बवयोः सादृश्यं) भ shows possession. Other terminations used are न and

ल. cp. बलिन; तुन्दिल, तुन्दिभ also तुन्दिक. The wrinkles on the belly of a woman are regarded as a mark of beauty. cp. मध्येनसा वेदिविलग्नमध्या बलित्रयं चारु बभारबाला ku. 1. 39.; शिखा धूमस्येयं परिणमति रोमावलिवपुः K. P. X.; रराज तन्वी नवलोमराजिः Ku. 1. 38; also cp. si. 9. 22. **कर्णजाहविलोचना **(कर्णजाहयो विश्रान्ते विलोचनेयस्याः the Comp. is मध्यमपदलोपी Bahuvrihi) 'the eyes reaching the ends of the ears.' This is likewise a mark of beauty. Cp. अत्रान्तरे किमपी वाग्विभवातिवृत्त......आयताक्ष्याः &c. Mal. 1. 29.; दीर्घाक्षं शरदिन्दुकान्ति वदनं &c. M. 2. 3. For जाह cр.अपिकण्ठजाह.......&c. Mal. 5.8 **वाक्त्वचेन** 'with her tongue and skin.' i. e. with the sweetness of her speech and the tenderness of her skin or body. Mark the sing, प्राण्यङ्गत्वादेकवद्भावः J. M. Com. वाक्त्वचेन वाङ्मयेन माधुर्येण मार्दवेन चासाधारणेनोपलक्षितेनेत्यर्थः The adj. प्रियंवदा given to her in 19 (*in fra*) justifies the first. Her likeness to चन्द्रलेखा shows her tenderness. She was a तन्वङ्गी. Delicacy of limbs is also a mark of beauty cp. इयमधिकमनोज्ञा वल्कलेनापि तन्वी s. 1. 20. **अतिसर्वेण **(सर्वमतिक्रान्तेन, सर्व being placed next.) 'surpassing all.' The अलङ्कार in the second line is उपमा. Stanzas 16-19 both inclusive form one synthetical whole and are therefore an example of what is called कलापकम् i. e. a series of four stanzas on the same subject and forming one grammatical sentence, (चतुर्भिस्तुकलापकम्). Cp. Ki. 3. 41-44

 17 **सुपाद्** ‘having handsome feet' (शोभनौ पादौ यस्याः) पाद compounded with a numeral and or सु when the first member is used as a standard of comparison, but is a word other than हस्ति, e. g. व्याघ्रपाद् drops its final vowel optionally; cp. द्विपाद् or द्विपाद. Even separately पाद optionally substitutes पद् in cases beginning from the Acc. plu. पादान् or पदः acc. plu.; पादेन, पदा Ins. Sing. &c. The feminine base is also सुपदी. **द्विरदनासोरूः '**having thighs (as slender and beautiful) as the trunk of an elephant.' It is a Bah. Com. (द्विरदस्य नास्रे

इव ऊरू यस्या) involving an उपमा. द्विरद 'an elephant' since he has two tusks (द्वीरदौ यस्य). The form ॰सोरूः is admissible but the former is more usual. That the thighs of woman are described as resembling either the back of the fore arm (करभोरूः), a trunk of an elephant as in this stanza, or a plantain tree, is poetically too well-known. Cp. अङ्के निधाय करभोरु यथामुखं ते S. 3. 21., पिबोरुरम्भातरुपीवरोरु N. 22-43, also R. 6, 83, Ku. 1. 36. ॰**तलाङ्गुलिः** ac. to J. M. this must be dissolved thus; तलं चाङ्गुलश्चेति द्वन्द्वः (समाहार प्राण्यङ्गत्वे Bh.) पाण्योस्तलाङ्गुलिः मृदुः पाणितलाङ्गुलिर्यस्या। मृदु पाणितलं चाङ्गुलिश्चयस्याः Bh. **जघनेन** sc. उपलक्षितासा (प्रार्थयाञ्चक्रे st. 19). Plumpy loins or buttocks are considered a sign of beauty Op. यातं यच्च नितंवयोर्गुरुतया मन्दं विलासादिव. S. 2. 2; मध्यः पाणिमितो नितम्बिजघनं M. 2. 3.

 18 **उन्नसं** this and the following two are adj. of वक्रं (उन्नता नासिकायस्मिन् or यस्य). नासिका is changed to नस् in such compounds; 'having a prominent nose.' Ac. to Bh. नस is a form of नसा; नसा, नासा नासिकेति कोषान्तरम्. **दधती **adj. fem. of दधत् pre par from धा. **शुध्ददत् **"having white teeth.' शुद्धा दन्तायस्मिन्. दन्त is changed to दत्. Cp. सुदत् (fem. सुदती). Bh. recognises दत् as a different word. **शंयुन् **(श 'happiness' यु is a possessive termination) Mark that the nasal is retained as in many other words. शं सुखं यस्यास्तीति Another word thus formed is from कं 'happiness,' कंयु. Mark that in नाक get the word. J. M. gives another पदच्छेद which is possible e.i. कुर्वाणा अपश्यतः and writes अपश्यतो वाशंयून् कुर्वाणा पश्यतां तुपीडाकरी। The sense thus given is, to our mind, not a good one. It is impossible for a man to be affected either way without seeing her. Moreover here the author has given us an elaborate description of her beauty and form and it is therefore in keeping with the whole to say that her presence was a pleasant sight. It must be borne in mind that there राक्षसी had assumed a most attractive form. It is a well known fact that demons of both sexes were able to change

forms at their sweet will. For a similar idea in the foreign literature cp. Spencer's Faery Queen Bk. I. Our राक्षसी showes her real form in St. 33. Her body was terrifying (भयदं वपुः) which in her changed form was fascinating (पश्यतः शयन् कुर्वाणा). **स्रग्विणी** (fem. of स्रग्विन्, विन् is a possessive termination like मिन् cp. गोमिन्, पयस्विन्, यशस्विन्. इन is another termination showing possession us in धनिन् दण्डिन्); 'having a garland.' **सुहसानना** (शोभनो हसः kar; सुहस्रं = शोभनहसमाननं यस्याः सा Bah.) 'having a smiling face.' अ is a mas. termination to form nouns from verbs; cp. स्वन्ः, करः. The metre of this stanza is अनुष्टुभ्.

 19. **चञ्चूर्यमाणा** (At pre. par. from the fre. of चर्) 'gesticulating indecently' (vide Kielhorn's Grammar). **पतीयन्ती** (fem of the denominative base from पति cp. पुत्रीयती) 'desirous of having a husband' **अनुका** vide note on अभीका St. 15. **प्रियाकर्तुं** (प्रिय+कर्तं, आ is the augment डाच् ) 'to favour,' i. e. by marring her. cp. सुखाकर्तुम्.

 20 **उपायंस्थाः** (aorist 4 v of उपयम् ' to marry') 'should marry,' showing desirability. It is At in this sense. cp; भवान् मिथः समयादिमापुयंस्त S. 5. आत्मानुरूपां विधिना उपयेमे. **कम्म्रा** ‘beautiful' र् is joined with कम् and नम् to form adj; कम्र and नम्र. It is a krit possessive termination. **इच्छुः** 'desirous.' It is an irregular form (निपातितः cp. विन्दुः, उ being the krit termination). The woman emphasies the point that Lakshman being single, must be desirous to marry. The unmarried life of Lakshman will induce him not to lose the opportunity which is so fortunately (as she thought) being offered to him. **वशं वदाम् **'voluntarily offering her person,' अहं ते वश्येति वदन्तीम्. Op. प्रियंवदा above. वद् is compounded with वश and प्रियं, nasal being inserted. **त्वद्भोगीनां **'advantageous to your person' (त्वच्छरीराय हितां). The Com. assigns one reason for the demoness to characterise herself as being of special advantage

to him who marries her. The reason is that she is free from widowhood अवैधव्यादिलक्षणयोगात्. The demoness says that she is above the conditions of human existence and as such her husband would be blessed with an uncommonly long life and all possible happiness which an ordinary woman is unable to give him. This is an additional reason to marry her. ईन is the krit termination. Cp. विश्वजनीन and आत्मनीन in Can. II st. 48. Bh. reads सुभोगीनां = सुभोगाय हितां. **सहचरीं **fem. of सहचर from सहचर्, अ being the krit affix, cp. सेनाचर, भिक्षाचर &e. which are similarly formed. ‘female companion' (lit) one who walks in company i. e. one ready to partake in the joys and sorrows of her husband. **अशङ्कः** 'without any doubt,' as to my motives which are altogether pure. I shall never deceive you. **पुरुषस्युषम्** 'till human existence' i. e. for 100 years which is the fixed number of years of शतायु वै पुरुषः, The form is adverbial (पुरुषस्य आयुर्यावत्). Cp. अकृपणमतिः कामं जीव्याज्जनः पुरुषायुषं Ve. 6. 44; पुरुषायुषजीविन्यो निरातङ्का निरीतयः R. 1. 63. The acc. is used to show tine द्वादश वर्षाणि न ववर्ष दशशताक्षः Dk. (vide Apte's Guide):

 21 **गोष्ठीने** 'having formerly cowpens.' It is a derivative word (ईन being the Tad. termination) from गोष्ठ ‘a cowpen.' This form is used to show the former existence of cowpens in this forest which is not now visited by the cattle. गोष्ठीने वने गोष्टं भूतपूर्वं यस्मिन्वने ईदानीन्नामापिनज्ञायते गोष्ठात् खर्ज् (ईन termination) भूतपूर्वे (to show former existence) इति रवज् J. M. गोष्ठीने भूतपूर्वं गोष्ठं यस्मिन् सम्प्रति गोसञ्चारोऽपि नास्ति; गावस्तिष्ठन्ति अस्मिन्निति गोष्ठं निपातनात् विकारसङ्घेत्यादिना भूतपूर्वेऽंर्थें गोष्ठात्नीतः Bh. **स्त्रीपुंसभीषणे** 'terrifying to men and women.' स्त्रीच पुमांश्च स्त्रीपुंसौ तयोर्भीषणे. It is no wonder that the forest was terrifying to human beings when even the cattle had left it. Mark the declension of पुंस, पुमान्, पुमांसौ, पुमांसः Nom.; In पुंसा, पुम्भ्याम्, पुम्भिः &c.; to पुमन्. The form of the word in this compound is peculiar; अ being added. But generally

the ending स् is dropped, eg पुमर्थः, पुङ्गवः, पुंसवन; &c. भीषण noun from the caus. of भी 'to fear; the causal forms are भाययति, भापयते and भीषयते; अन is the termination to form abstract nouns from verbs. Cp. जनन, मरण &c. **असूर्यम्पश्यरूपा** 'whose form is not to look at the sun, i. e. who is not allowed to expose her person cven to the rays of the sun. being closely shut up in the harem (अतिगोपनीयतया). This is the terrible aspect of what is now called the purdah system. Mark that the nasal is inserted before this krit termination (अ) Cp. ललाटन्तपः; सूर्य मपिनपश्यति असूर्यम्पश्यंरूपं यस्याः सा. J. M. सूर्य मपिनिषिद्धदर्शनं नपश्यतीति। सानपश्यतीति रूपम्मापन पश्यतीत्युक्तम्। cp. ललाटन्तपस्तपतिसूर्यः Mal. 1 for ललाटन्तपः and उग्रम्पश्य॰ in st. 23 infra. **अभीरूः** 'not timid' i. e. bold. This adjective hints at the unhumanly nature of the woman. She may be a demon in disguise or a supernatural being which as Lakshmana suspects, she was not. Vide next stanza. is the krit termination showing liability. **अरार्यसे** (fre. 2nd pers. sing of ऋ 'to go' 'wanderest' (**अत्यर्थं भ्रमसि**).

 22 **रोचिष्णुः** 'blooming' or 'gaily dressed.' ष्णु is a krit termination showing tendency or disposition. Cp. Can. V St. I for more examples. This is from रुच्. (= रोचनस्वभावा). **दिव्यधर्मिणी** (fem. of दिव्यधर्मिन्, इन् is a possessive termination, e. g. अर्थिन्), 'possessing divine nature.' दिव्या (दिविभवाः दिव्या, य is a termination to show 'belonging to' cp स्वर्ग्यः, सभ्यः &c.), 'heavenly' (=देवाः). The woman of whom this is said is as we know a राक्षसी but even demons are called दिव्य on account of their heavenly origin (राक्षसा अपि देवयोनित्वात् देवाः दिव्याः). Dissolve दिविभवादिव्या स्तेषां धर्मः स्वभावः सोऽस्या अस्तीति. The student will remember that demons were mythologicaily the sons of Kasyapa by his wife दिति. **अप्सरायमाणा** (At adj. from the denomi-base of अप्सरा). 'acting like an an Apsaras (अप्सरा इव आचरन्ती). This epithet reveals the true nature of the woman. She is not a nymph

by nature, but a demon. Her true nature she thus tries to hide by her assumed form; राक्षसभावं गोप्तुमिति भावः **स्वतन्त्रा** 'free,' 'unrestrained' स्व आत्माप्रधानंयस्याः। अपराधीनत्वात्। अनयोक्त्या राक्षसीत्वं दर्शयति। J. M.

 23 **उग्रपश्याकुले** (उग्रं पश्यन्तीति उग्रं पश्यास्तैराकुले व्याप्ते) 'inhabited by the fierce-looking,' i. e. lions, tigers &c. and mountaneers like शबर, भिल्ल &c. The fierceness of the latter is due to their sin in the former birth; सिंहव्याघ्रादयः Bh. पापाशयत्वाच्छबरादयः J. M., Bh. उग्रं पश्य cp. असूर्यम्पश्य in st. 21; अ is a krit termination before which a nasal is inserted; cp. also प्रियंवदां वशंवदां in st. 19. 20. **शालीनत्वविवर्जिता** 'devoid of bashfulness;' शालिनत्व abstract noun from शालीना 'modest,' (शाला प्रवेशमर्हतीति J. M., शालां प्रवेष्टुमर्हतीति Bh., ईन being the possessive termination). Dis. शालीनाया भावः शालीनत्वं. Mark that the word प्रवेश or प्रवेष्ठुं is dropped in the formation of the word शालीना. cp, शाकपार्थिवः; विवर्जिता (p. p. of वृज् with वि, विशेषेण वर्जिता) ‘freefrom.' ॰**पट्वी** fem. of पटु 'expert,' 'clever;' पटु is also feminine base, cp. बहु or बह्वी. The Com. is loc. Tat. **पतिवत्नी** fem., also पत्नी and पतिवती (Vedic). वन्त् is the pos. ter. instead of मत्. पतिवत्नी जीवत्पतिः कथं केन प्रकारेण न वा नैवं भवसीत्यर्थः J. M; कथं वा त्वं पतिवत्नी सभर्तृका न भवसि पतिसत्वे ईद्दक् स्वातन्त्र्यासम्भवात् Bh.

 24 **पर्णशालायां** sc. अवस्थितं ‘residing in the hut. **अनुरहसं** (adj. of राघवं ), 'who is now in solitude' and therefore fit to be approached by you; अनुगतं रहः विजनस्थानं रतं वा यस्य तं B. रहः is therefore taken by B. to mean solitude or copulation. Both the senses are likely. Rama is now in retirement, a condition necessary for enjoyment, or Rama has commenced this kind of life. Both furnish reason why the woman should go to Rama. **स्वामी**, यो ममापि स्वामी ईश्वरस्तस्मिन् सति मद्वरणं न युक्तं Bh. **कान्तावान्** (कान्तायस्यास्तीति, वत् pos. ter.) समार्थः प्रवृत्तसम्भोगोऽसौ नाहमिति दर्शयति J. M.; एतेन स्त्रीसुखाभिज्ञोऽपिरामोऽहं तुतपस्वीतिध्वनिः Bh. **औपकर्णिकलोचनः** (कर्णयो; समीपम् उपकर्णं Av. Com. तन्नभवइति, इक being the Tad. ter.

similarly औपजानुक in st. 25), ' reaching the ears,' औपकर्णिकेलोचने यस्य Bah. Com., एतेनरूपवत्वं दर्शितं Bh. The form is always accompanied by Vriddhi of the word.

 25 **चान्दनिकं** 'annoited with sandal,' चन्दनेनराजितं Bh. इक being as before the Tad. ter.; also in ॰वेष्टनिक. **कार्णवेष्टनिक** 'having earringlets,' such as कुण्डल. एतेन विलासित्वं दर्शितं Bn. **सर्वकर्मिणौ** 'dexterous in every kind of military art' i. c. he can wield all kinds of weapons; धनुःखड्गादिव्यापाररूपे कुशलौ; सर्वकर्मणि व्याश्रुतइत्यर्थः **औपजानुकौ **(vide औपकर्णिक supra) 'reaching the ears.' Dis. जानुसमीपे भवौ (the termination क is then added) तावत्प्रलम्बा वित्यर्थः एतेन महापुरूषलक्षण मुक्तं B. It is a sign of good luck and high dignity to possess hands reaching the knees. Some of the heroic kings are described to have such long hands. Our great Shivaji is said to have possessed long arms. Op. तदेत दाजानुबिलम्बिना .....। भुजेन.... पुनरंसलेन R. 16.84; also राजानमाजानुविलम्बिबाहुं &c. R. 18. 24. also R. 1. 13 where Dilipa is thus described.

 26 दुर्बलरक्षार्थं 'in order to protect the weak and helpless.' It is the duty of a kshatriya to protect the weak and the destitute against the strong and oppressive. Cp. Rama's speech in Can. III st. 35 and the note thereon. Cp. क्षात्रो धर्मः श्रित इव तनुं ब्रह्मघोषस्य गुप्त्यै U. 6. 9., and आर्त्तत्राणायवः शस्त्रन्नप्रहतुमनागसि S. the Com. is Dative Tatpurusha **औपनीविकः** 'near the knot of the wearing garment' नीविसमीते (प्रायेण) भवतीति, vide औपकणिक Supra 24; वामपार्श्वाधोभागस्थायीत्यर्थः B. नीवि is generally applied to the knot of a woman's wearing garment. Cp...... प्रस्थानभिन्नां न बबन्ध नीवि R. 7, 9. **आश्मनप्रख्यं** ' like a stony thing i. e. as hard as something made from stone. आश्मन ‘prepared from stone,' अश्मनो विकारः (अ termination denotes 'coming from') आश्मनं, तेनप्रख्यं सदृशं B; तेनप्रख्या सादृशमस्य तदाश्मनप्रख्यं J. M. This gives a व्यधिकरण Bah. Com. which is not good. प्रख्य itself is used at the end of a compound to denote likeness.' **धत्ते **(3rd per. Sing of धा ‘to hold’) ‘holds,' 'wields'. अन्यदु-

र्वहं (रामादन्येन दुःखेन उह्यत इति) 'to be borne by another with great difficulty.' Cp. Supra Can. I 26 धनुररिभिरसह्यं Understand तमिच्छ in 25-27.

 27 **धर्मसन्तानसूः** 'the source of righteousness.' सन्तान 'a continuous flow or succession' from सन्तन्; ॰नंसतइति ॰स्ः. In the formation of such nouns the termination is dropped. Cp. यज्ञद्रुह् in this st., ब्रह्मद्विषस्ते in Can. II 35. **दारगवानां** 'wives and cattle.' दाराश्चगावश्च दारगवानि Dwandva Com. of the समाहारद्वन्द्व kind; (दारगवम्). In the dissolution the plural is used to show many collections. Each Muni may be supposed to be there with his wife and cattle. When two actions are to be predicated of the some person, one prior to the other, the prior action may be denoted by the infinitive in त्वा; so we have here ॰यं प्राप्याभयं वर्तते. The action of 'going' is here denoted by प्राप्य (inf. form of प्र +आप्, य being used instead of त्व as there is preposition), the second predication is put in the verb form. cp. e. g. विष्णुन्नत्वास्तौति ‘first bows down to Vishnu and then praises;' (येषां प्राप्तिस्तेषामेवाभयं B). **अभयं** 'no fear.' I think that the poet has here committed a दोष in using the negative compound word. As here negation is an important fact here he should have used न भयं (Vide Kavya P. VII), नभयम् अभयं (नञ् T. Com.) Cons.मुनीनां दारगवानां यं प्राप्य सदा अभयं वर्तते, (more correctly) सदा भयं न वर्तते; (तमिच्छ).

 28 **वावृत्त्यमाना** (Present par. of वावृत् 4th Conj. At, मान being like आन, an Atm. termination), 'wishing to choose, or marry.' **न्यविक्षत** (Aoг. 7th Variety of नि+ विश्) 'entered' the hut (शाला) of Rama. **उपायंस्त **understand भवान् as subject to this) 'marry.' This shows entreaty on her part; (4th Var. of उप + यम्) note on st. 20 of this Canto, हे राम अहं प्रार्थये भवान् मामुपायंस्त परिणयत्विति वाक्यभेदेनयोज्यम्, J. M. **वदन्ती** fem. of the Pre. par. from वद् 'addressing;' वचः cognate object of वद्, cp. 'to live a life.'

 29 **अस्त्रीकः** (नविद्यते यस्यस्त्रीति) having no wife,' 'single.' The Tad. affix क is added in some Bah. Compounds. Compare व्युढोरस्कः R. 1. 13 and नदीमातृकः, देवमातृकः Vide note on अभयं st. 27 supra **पुष्यतितराम् **"will maintain fully,"'will take greatest care.' The present is used to denote immediate future, which is one of the functions of the Present. This use is akin to the English use of the same tense. तराम् is affixed to verbs and indeclinables, as remarked before, to form superlative signifying intensity;' sc. त्वां **मामुचः **(माम् अमुचः, 2nd Variety ) 'do leave me. Another sense is possible, taking मा as a negative particle after which the augment अ of the aor. is dropped; 'do not leave' (Lakshamana), i. e. urge him. **तुष्यतितराम्** is another reading which is not bad. It means 'will highly please (you).' Cons. सएव तवपतिः, (त्वां ) पुष्यतितराम्.

 30 **वृषस्यन्ती** (fem. of Den. P. pre. par.), this word must be doubly interpreted to be applicable both to सा and गौः, in the former case longing for sexual intercourse; in the latter longing for a bull' for the same purpose. The word governs the acc. of the male. वृषोऽत्र शुकलवचनः मैथुनाय वृषं शुक्रलपुरुषमिच्छन्ती कामुकीत्यर्थः। गोपक्षे वृषं वृषभमिच्छन्ती Bh. The Deno. is formed in some cases by means of the suffix स्य or अस्य. Such bases are conjugated in the Paras. only and convey the notion of 'wishing ardently' for that which is expressed by the nominal base. So we have here वृषस्यन्ति, अश्व, क्षीरलवण, मधु are some of the words whose nominal base is thus formed. क्यविधानं स्वेच्छायां सनागमस्तु याभार्घे तेन मैथुनविषयस्वेच्छावगम्यते। केचित्तु प्रकृत्यर्थ त्यागेन मैथुनेच्छामात्रे वृषस्य अश्वस्येति क्यवन्तरूपं (Nom. Base) अतएव 'विरथहयानश्वस्यन्ती'ति नैषधप्रयोगः। तत्रहिहृयान् मैथुनायेच्छन्तीत्यवगम्यते। प्रकृत्यर्थपुरस्कारे (in case you stick to the meaning implied by the crude base) हयशद्वानन्वयापत्ते (the word हय will have no meaning) रित्याहुः। अन्येतु वृषस्याश्वस्यइत्यव्युत्पन्नमेव धातुद्वयं मैथुनेच्छायां वर्तते इत्याहुः। B. CP ... इति रामोवृषस्यन्तीं वृषस्कन्धः शशासतां R. 12. 34. **महोक्षं **(महांश्चासौउक्षा Kar. Com) 'a great bull' उक्षन् becomes

उक्ष when compounded with महा, वृद्ध, जात. For महोक्ष Com. R. 4. 22 ......महोक्षातस्यविक्रमं and महोक्षतां (state of a great buil) वत्सतरःस्पृशन्निव R. 3. 32. **मन्मथायुध...... मतिः **'whose mind is troubled by the stroke of Cupid's arrows' (मन्मथस्य आयुधानां सम्पातस्तेनव्यथ्यमानामतिर्यस्याः Bah. Com.) Mark the compound मन्मथ (मनोमध्नातीति) 'Cupid' Poetically the God of Love is said to dart arrows at men and women when really speaking they are inflamed with that passion. The arrows of Cupid are said to be of flowers but their power for mischief is very great. The following verses give the names of the arrows of the god: अरविन्दमशोकञ्च चूतञ्च नवमाल्लिका। नीलोत्पलञ्चपञ्चैते पञ्चबाणस्यसायकाः॥ or सम्मोहनोन्मादनौ च शोषणस्तापनस्तथा।स्तम्भनश्चेति कामस्य पञ्चबाणा प्रकीर्तिताः. One might think these arrows, flowery as they are, to be harmless but cp. M. act iii. 2. क्वरुजाहृदयप्रमाथिनी। क्वच ते विश्वसनीयमायुधम्। (because flowery) मृदु तीक्ष्णतरं (take तर with मृदु also) यदुच्यते। तदिदं मन्मथ दृश्यते त्वयि॥ **व्यथ्यमान** (pas pre. par. of व्यथ् ‘to torment') 'which is being tormented.

 31 **सासद्यमानायाः** (pre par of the fre. of सद्) ‘practising disgraceful jesticulation;' समीपे गर्हितं सीदन्त्याः प्रविश्यन्त्याः J. M. समीपेगर्हितं सीदन्त्याः उपविशन्त्याः B. The fre-quentatives of the roots सद् and चर् (Com. चञ्चूर्यमाणा in 19) convey the notion of reproach &c. I like to suggest the idea of indecent gesticulation, which is very possible in the case of a woman troubled with the passion of enjoyment. She may try, by such means, to rouse a similar passion in the man; (Mar. अश्लीलहावभाव करणारी) **लोलूयावान्** 'desirous to cut off,' (लोलूया + वत् poss. ter., लोलूया abs. noun from the freq. of लू), अतिशयच्छेदनयुक्ता, लवनक्रियायुक्तः **कौक्षेयं** (कुक्षौभवः, एय being the krit ter, the final vowel before which is dropped) 'a sword in the sheath.' Another interpretation is ‘made of steel' 'कुक्षिःखड्गपिधाने स्यात्तीक्ष्णलोहे तथो दरे' इति कोषः **अपनसम्** (अपगता नासिका यस्मात्) void of nose,’ ‘noseless.' नासिका becomes नस as in उन्नसं, vide st. 18, in such Bah. Compounds chiefly after propositions.

 32 **सूर्पणखा** (or शूर्पणखा, शूर्प + नखा), 'having fingernails like winnowing baskets;' Name of a female demon, being the step-sister of Ravana. शूर्पनाखा रावणस्य सापत्नस्वसा। आरण्यकाण्डे। “पुष्पोत्कटायाः जज्ञाते द्वौ पुत्रौ राक्षसेश्वरौ। कुम्भकर्णदशग्रीवौ बलेनाप्रतिमौ भुवि। मालिनी जनयामास पुत्रमेकं विभीषणम्। शङ्कायां मिथुनं जज्ञे खरः शूर्पणखा तथा"॥ The student will find that this episode, as narrated by our poet differs a little from the one we have in Raghuvamsa. Our poet says that the woman first came to Lakshmana and begged him to marry her and so on. The Raghuvamsa has it that she was attracted by the beauty of Rama and solicited him to marry her but Rama sent her to Lakshmana for the same reason as in our poem. The latter rejected her too when she again repaired to Rama. This circumstance excited Sita's laughter, and the revengeful demoness, feeling herself grossly insulted; assumed her original hideous form and threatened to eat her up. But Lakshmanas cut off her ears and nose and thus doubly deformed her. Cp. R. 12. 32-40. **अज्ञायिषि** (2nd per. sing pas. aor V variety) have been recognised.' Vide Kielhorn's Grammar Arts. 332, 2a., and 398. **क्षेत्रियः** this word has a peculiar meaning. Literally it means 'belonging to the body from क्षेत्र 'a body (regarded as the field of the working of the soul) and इय Tad suffix in the sense of 'belonging to,' But the peculiar sense is 'curable in the future body and incurable in the present life,' (therefore) irremediable, incurable अज्ञाने कारणमाह। येनायं दण्डो नासाछेदनलक्षणो मय्यपाति पातितः। क्षेत्रियः परक्षेत्रे (in a future body) चिकित्स्यः (that can be healed) जन्मान्तरशरीरे यदिशक्यश्चिकित्सितुं तदा नासिकायाः सम्भवात् क्षेत्रियेच परक्षेत्रे चिकित्स्य इति निपातनम् (irregular), J. M. Bh. **अपाति **(pas. aorist third per. sing) has been directed,' note that in the pas. aorist the third person singular is formed in one and the same manner of all roots, by prefixing to the root the augment and by adding it to the termination इ before which roots undergo changes, (Kielhorn's Gra. art. 393).

 33 **पर्यशाप्सीत्** (3rd per. sing. aor. 4th Variety from शप् with परि) 'riviled,' 'abused.' **दिविष्ठते '**standing in the sky,' दिवि+स्था the Compound is Aluk Locative Tat; दिवि (loc. of दिव् 'the sky) तिष्ठतीति दिविष्टा. Mark the declension of दिव् f, **अपिस्फवत् **(3rd per. sing. aor. 3rd form of the causal of स्फाय् 1A 'increase), 'augmented,' 'extolled.' The extolling of the prowess of her brothers was intended to terrify Rama and Lakshmana who had insulted them by causing injury to their sister and who would be revenged for it by them at her instigation. **विक्रमं** 'strength,' prowess' is object of this verb. **निनङ्क्षुः** 'wishing to perish or disappear,' (adj. from the desids. of नश् 'to perish' which forms निनङ्क्षति or निनशिषति). We have to make a choise between these two senses of नष्टुमिच्छु J, M, and अन्तर्धातुमिच्छु B, The latter sense is preferable to the former since we find in the next stanza her presence before her brothers. Before disappearing to inform her brothers of the insult given them by their enemies she thought it necessary to give an exaggerated description of the prowess of her brothers in order to, as said above, terrify them, (Rama &c,), Doing this she disappears. The latter sense may suggest the destruction of her brothers in the battle shortly to be fought. B. Gives two variants अपिस्फुरत् and अपुस्फरत् both meaning प्रकाशितवती 'described.' The forms are 3rd pers. sing aorist of the causal of स्फुर् 'to shine,' the first from the caus. base स्फोरि and the second from स्फारि. These two readings are inferior.

 34 **पर्यदेविष्ट** (at. aor. 5th form of परिदिव् or परिदेव् ‘to lament') lamented,' 'wept.' gr: construe this with भ्रात्रोः **विजिग्राहयिषुः** (adj. from the Desid. base of the causal of विग्रह), 'wishing to make (Rama) fight' with her brothers. रामं विजिग्राहयिषुः विप्राहयितुं खरादिभिः सह योधयितुमिच्छुः B. Mark the Sandhi विजिग्राहयिषूरामं.

 35 **कृते** 'on account of.' It is used with gen. or

in Com. cp. अमीषां प्राणान्नां तुलितबिसिनपितपयसाम्। कृते किं ...... B. 3. 36; ...... अपित्रैलोक्यराज्यस्य हेतोः किन्नु महीकृते Bg. 1. 35. **सौभागिनेयस्य** adj. to भरतस्य, 'son of the fortunate केकयी. सुभगा केकयी तस्या अपत्यं पुमान् सौभागिनेयस्तस्य. The adjectives सुभगा and दुर्भगा form by the addition of the Tad. suffix इनेय, before which there is उभयपद वृद्धि ie Vriddhi of उ in सु and दुः and the penultimate अ in भग, सौभागिनेय and दौर्भागिनेय to denote 'the son of ' सुभगा means also 'a beloved wife' where भग 'lovе;' but I prefer to say that केकयी was more fortunate than her co-wives. There is nothing to show that सुमित्रा and कौशल्या were less beloved by their husband. We know also that Rama was his father's eye-ball. We have also read of the sad termination of Dasaratha's life owing to the ba. nishment of Rama. **विवासितौ '**banished,' 'exiled.' p. p. of the caus. of विवस् 'to send into exile.' **दौर्भागिने यौ** 'sons of the unfortunate mothers.' दर्भगे तयोरपत्ये रामलक्ष्मणौ. **चेष्टितं** 'deed' i. e. cutting of the nose नासाच्छेपनरूपं. Cons. सौभागिनेयस्यभरतस्य कृते पित्रा निवासितौ दौर्भागिनेयौ यौ तयोश्चेष्टितं (युवां) पश्यतम्.

 36 **रावणनाथायाः** whose lord or protector was Ravana. Ravana was her protector since he was her elder brother and the king of the demons. रावणोनाथोयस्याः Bah. Com. adj, to मम. **तापसकात्** 'by the wretch of an ascetic.' The demoness speaks of Rama as an insignificant ascetic and it is therefore to be more regretted and revenged. It is highest disgrace that the sister of powerful demons like you and Ravana should be maltreated in this way. The Tad. affix is added to nouns and adjectives, mostly to the former, in the sense of dimunition c. 9. वृक्षक 'a small tree,' deterioration अश्वक्रः 'a bad horse,' similarity अश्वक 'like a horse,' endearment पुत्रकः 'dear boy,' or sometimes to express the original meaning of the word itself अल्पार्थे कुत्स्तथैवाकः (the affix क). **ध्बसः **'destruction, i. 6. the cutting of the nose नासाच्छेदन रूपः or नासिकाविनाशः **वः क्षमम्** 'to be forgiven by you.' वः the plural is used

since there is a mention of three in the first line, her two brothers and her protector Ravana. The Com. mentator Jaya M. gives another reason for the use of plural. He says युष्मदि गुरावेकेषामिति बहुवचनन्तयोर्ज्येष्टत्वात् i.e. the plural is used to show the priority of her elder brothers in years and therefore her reverence to them requires the plural. In this sense the plural may be used even in the case of one. J. M. evidently excludes Ravana but I think that his explanation, though generally correct, does not hold good here. She has already said of them as युवयोः which is dual referring to her two brothers. Our explanation, therefore, appears more correct since there is no reason why Ravana should be excluded. "Here is an insult given by one who is so and so. This deserves to be revenged at your hands. But if you think it pardonable you may do it." क्षमम् this use is indeclinable as in वरं. क्षमं क्षमायोग्यं सामान्यतः प्रयुक्तम्। युक्ते योग्ये हिते क्षममिति कोषः। क्षममव्ययपित्यन्ये। Bh पुरः is Bh's reading, युवयो रेवपुरः अग्रतः।

 37 **असंस्कृत्रिमसव्यानम्** (असंस्कृत्रिमाणि संव्यानानि परिधानानि उत्तरीयाणिययोः) 'whose garments were not richly wrought, i. c. who wore bark-garments. For such forms as संस्कृत्रिम vide note on विपक्त्रिम Сan. I. 10. The contention of the demoness is that the insult is too great to be disregarded coming as it does from insignificant men.

 40 °**कान्वितौ** – परशुभिर्युध्यन्ते पारश्वधिकाः धनुभिर्युध्यन्ते धानुष्काः शक्तिभिः युध्यन्ते शाक्तीकाः प्रासैर्युध्यन्ते प्रासिकाः। सेनाङ्गत्वात्कृतैकवद्भावः। Bh. J. M. The several terminations used here to form different derivative words show possessions.

 42 In this verse we get a number of past passive participles. पप्रे pas. perf. of पृ 'was filled with. दीनैः =हा मातः हाभ्रातरित्यवं भाषमाणैः J. M., सुतादि दुःखान्वितैः Bh.

 43 **आसेदुः** is the verb and वेपथुं, दवथुं, वमथुं, भ्राजथुं are its several objects. अथु is a krit termination used to

form abstract nouns of certain verbs. वेपथु is from वेप् 'to tremble,' दवथु from दु 'to be afflicted with pain, वमथु from वम् to vomit, and भ्राजथु from भ्राज् ' to shine. The metre of this canto is अनुष्टुभ upto this verse including.

 44 **मृगयुं** 'a hunter,' मृगान् यातीति मृगयुः। **दक्षिणेर्मा** 'wounded in the right thigh,' दक्षिणे ईर्म व्रणं यस्येति। मृगलुब्धकत्रणितदक्षिणाङ्गः J. M. Bh. **उदन्यन्** 'thirsty.' **त्रिमूर्धः** named also त्रिशिरस् was the name of a demon, so called because he had three months. Mark that मुर्धन् is optionally changed to मूर्ध Cp. st. 41. The similes used are very expressive. The अलङ्कार is मालोपमा and the metre is उपजाति. Mark that राजन् is changed to राज in पतत्रिराजम् 'a king of birds,' i. e. Garuda. राजाहः सखिभ्यष्टच् J. M.

 45, ॰**वत्क्रः,** निकृत्त p. p. of निकृन्त् 'to cut off.' The Com. is Báh. कीर्ण P. P. कॄ. The अलङ्कार is उपमा, The metre is उपजाति.

**APPENDIX.**  
**\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_**

ON METRE.

 A poetic composition (पद्य) is expressed in the form of stanzas. A stanza or Padya is a combination of four Pádas or quarters which are regulated either by the number of syllables (अक्षर), or by the number of syllabic instants (मात्रा). As we do not meet with stanzas of the latter kind in our text-book we shall speak about metres regulated by syllables, some of which are used in the portion we have to study.
Stanzas regulated by syllables are called Vrittas (वृत्त).

 Vrittas are divided into three classes:—समवृत्त which the Pádas or quarters composing the stanza are all similar; अर्धसमवृत्त in which the alternate quarters are similar; विषमवृत्त in which the quarters are all dissimilar.

 A syllable is as much of a word as can be pronounced at once, that it, a vowel with or without one or more consonants. A syllable is लघु 'short,' or गुरु 'long,' according as its vowel is 'short' or long.' The vowels अ, इ, उ, ऋ, and ऌ are short; and आ, ई, ऊ, ऋ, ऌॄ , ए, ऐ, ओ and औ are long but a naturally short vowel is considered long under following conditions

**सानुस्वारश्चदीर्घश्च विसर्गी च गुरुर्भवेत्।  
वर्णः संयोगपूर्वश्च तथा पादान्तगोऽपि वा॥**

 For the purpose of scanning metres regulated by the number of syllables, writers on prosody have devised eight 'Ganas' or syllabic feet, each consisting of three syllables, and distinguished from one another

by particular syllables being short or long. They are given in the following verse:—

**आदिमध्यावसानेषु यरता यान्ति लाघवम्।  
भजसा गौरवं यान्ति मनौ तु गुरुलाघवम्॥**

Expressed in symbols (the symbol ॅ denoting a short syllable and — a long one, the different Ganas are thus represented:—

य ॅ – –, र – ॅ –, त – – ॅ , भ – ॅ ॅ,

ज ॅ – ॅ , स ॅ ॅ –, म – – –, न ॅ ॅ ॅ.

Similarly ल ( ॅ) is used to denote a short syllable, and ग (–) a long one

 We shall now define only such metres as are used in our poem.

1 **रुचिरा** also called **प्रभावती**,  
Def. जभौ सजौ गिति रुचिरा चतुर्ग्रहैः।  
Sch. G. ज, भ, स, ज, ग (4. 9)

 Ex. The first stanza in the Can. I. The figures in the brackets denote यति i. e. coesura or pause that may be made in reciting a quarter or verse.

2 **इन्द्रवज्रा**.

Def. स्यादिन्द्रवज्रा यदि तौ जगौ गः।  
Sch. G. त, त, ज, ग, ग (5. 6)  
Ex. st. 2 in Can. I.

3 **उपेन्द्रवज्रा**.

Def. उपेन्द्रवज्रा प्रथमे लघौ सा।  
Sch. G. ज, त, ज, ग, ग (5. 6)  
Ex. st. 3 in Can. I.

 The poet has largely used these. metres in the three first Cantos of his poem.

4 **मालिनी**.

Def. ननमयययुतेयं मालिनी भोगिलोकैः।  
Sch: G. न, न, म, य, य (8. 7)

Ex. stanzas 26, 27 Can. I, st. 55 Can. II  
and st. 56 Can. III.

5 **अनुष्टुप्** (also called **श्लोक**).

**श्लोके षष्ठं गुरु ज्ञेयं सर्वत्र लघु पञ्चमम्।  
द्विचतुः पादयोर्ह्रस्वं सप्तमं दीर्घमन्ययोः॥**

 Can. IV except its last two stanzas is composed in this metre. This was the first metre invented by Valmiki spontaneously.

**उपजाति.**

 This metre is a combination of two metres.

**वंशस्थ.**

(also called **वंशस्थविल** and **वंशस्तनित**)

Def. वदन्ति वंशस्थविलं जतौ जरौ.  
Sch. G. ज, त, ज, र ( 57 ).  
Ex. Can II 47.
